&& Cell Cycle and Cell Division

#### Easy

**1.** The sequence of events by which a cell duplicates its genome and eventually divides into two daughter cells is termed the:
A. Cell cycle
B. Mitosis
C. Meiosis
D. Cytokinesis
**Correct Answer: A**

**2.** DNA replication occurs during which phase of the cell cycle?
A. G₁ phase
B. S phase
C. G₂ phase
D. M phase
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** The division of the cytoplasm is called:
A. Karyokinesis
B. Cytokinesis
C. Interphase
D. Mitosis
**Correct Answer: B**

**4. Mitosis is also known as:**
A. Reductional division
B. Equational division
C. Direct division
D. Sexual division
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The stage of mitosis in which the chromosomes align at the equatorial plate is:
A. Prophase
B. Metaphase
C. Anaphase
D. Telophase
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The division of the nucleus is called:
A. Cytokinesis
B. Karyokinesis
C. Interkinesis
D. Apoptosis
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** Meiosis results in the formation of:
A. Two diploid daughter cells
B. Four diploid daughter cells
C. Two haploid daughter cells
D. Four haploid daughter cells
**Correct Answer: D**

**8.** The pairing of homologous chromosomes during meiosis is called:
A. Crossing over
B. Synapsis
C. Disjunction
D. Bivalent formation
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The exchange of genetic material between non-sister chromatids of homologous chromosomes occurs during which stage of meiosis I?
A. Leptotene
B. Zygotene
C. Pachytene
D. Diplotene
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** The stage of mitosis in which the sister chromatids separate and move to opposite poles is:
A. Prophase
B. Metaphase
C. Anaphase
D. Telophase
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** The correct sequence of the stages of mitosis is:
A. Prophase, Metaphase, Anaphase, Telophase
B. Metaphase, Prophase, Anaphase, Telophase
C. Anaphase, Telophase, Prophase, Metaphase
D. Prophase, Anaphase, Metaphase, Telophase
**Correct Answer: A**

**12.** Interphase is the phase between two successive:
A. Prophases
B. M phases
C. Anaphases
D. Telophases
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The cell plate is formed during cytokinesis in:
A. Animal cells
B. Plant cells
C. Both plant and animal cells
D. Bacteria
**Correct Answer: B**

**14.** The anaphase promoting complex (APC) is a protein degradation machinery necessary for proper:
A. DNA replication
B. Transcription
C. Mitosis
D. G₁ phase progression
**Correct Answer: C**

**15.** Meiosis is also known as:
A. Equational division
B. Reductional division
C. Somatic division
D. Direct division
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The cell cycle is divided into two basic phases:
A. Mitosis and Meiosis
B. Prophase and Metaphase
C. Interphase and M phase
D. Karyokinesis and Cytokinesis
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The point of attachment between sister chromatids is the:
A. Centriole
B. Centromere
C. Kinetochore
D. Telomere
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The stage where cells are metabolically active but no longer proliferate unless called on to do so is the:
A. G₁ phase
B. S phase
C. G₀ phase (Quiescent stage)
D. M phase
**Correct Answer: C**

**19.** The formation of a bivalent or a tetrad occurs during which stage of meiosis?
A. Leptotene
B. Zygotene
C. Pachytene
D. Diplotene
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** The final stage of mitosis, where the chromosomes decondense and the nuclear envelope reforms, is:
A. Prophase
B. Metaphase
C. Anaphase
D. Telophase
**Correct Answer: D**

D. 20 chromosomes, 4C DNA

**30.** A cell at the end of prophase of mitosis is different from a cell at the end of prophase I of meiosis in the presence of:

**33.** The synaptonemal complex is a protein structure that forms between homologous chromosomes during:
A. Leptotene

D. Diplotene

**34.** Meiosis II is similar to mitosis in that:
A. Homologous chromosomes separate

**35.** Terminalisation of chiasmata occurs during:
A. Pachytene

C. Diakinesis
D. Metaphase I

B. Telophase

A. Karyokinesis

&& Transport in Plants

#### Easy

**1.** The movement of substances from a region of higher concentration to a region of lower concentration is called:
A. Osmosis
B. Diffusion
C. Active transport
D. Imbibition
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The movement of water across a semipermeable membrane is called:
A. Diffusion
B. Osmosis
C. Transpiration
D. Guttation
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** Transport of substances over long distances in plants occurs through the vascular tissues, xylem and phloem. This is called:
A. Diffusion
B. Translocation
C. Osmosis
D. Imbibition
**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** The water potential of pure water at standard temperature is taken to be:
A. 1
B. -1
C. 0
D. 100
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** The loss of water in the form of vapor from the living tissues of aerial parts of the plant is known as:
A. Guttation
B. Transpiration
C. Bleeding
D. Respiration
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The transport of food materials in plants is carried out by the:
A. Xylem
B. Phloem
C. Cortex
D. Epidermis
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** A plant cell placed in a hypertonic solution will undergo:
A. Plasmolysis
B. Deplasmolysis
C. Turgidity
D. No change
**Correct Answer: A**

**8.** The opening and closing of stomata are regulated by the:
A. Epidermal cells
B. Guard cells
C. Subsidiary cells
D. Mesophyll cells
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The cohesion-tension theory explains the:
A. Translocation of food
B. Ascent of sap
C. Opening and closing of stomata
D. Absorption of water
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** Which of the following is an example of imbibition?
A. Swelling of a raisin in water
B. Swelling of wooden doors during the rainy season
C. Movement of water into a root hair
D. Opening of stomata
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** Facilitated diffusion requires protein carriers and:
A. Requires ATP energy
B. Does not require ATP energy
C. Is an uphill transport
D. Is independent of the concentration gradient
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** The water potential of a solution is always:
A. Positive
B. Negative
C. Zero
D. Greater than the solute potential
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The loss of water in its liquid phase from the tips of grass blades at night and in the early morning is known as:
A. Transpiration
B. Guttation
C. Bleeding
D. Evaporation
**Correct Answer: B**

**14.** The main driving force for transpiration is the:
A. Root pressure
B. Cohesion of water molecules
C. Adhesion of water molecules
D. Water potential gradient between the leaf and the atmosphere
**Correct Answer: D**

**15.** The transport of sugar from the source to the sink in plants is explained by the:
A. Cohesion-Tension theory
B. Pressure-Flow hypothesis
C. Imbibition theory
D. Root pressure theory
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** Active transport of ions by the cell requires:
A. A concentration gradient
B. A semipermeable membrane
C. ATP (metabolic energy)
D. Light energy
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The pathway of water movement in a root that involves the cell walls and intercellular spaces is the:
A. Symplast pathway
B. Apoplast pathway
C. Vacuolar pathway
D. Transmembrane pathway
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The water potential (Ψw) is equal to the sum of the solute potential (Ψs) and the:
A. Osmotic potential (Ψπ)
B. Pressure potential (Ψp)
C. Matrix potential (Ψm)
D. Gravitational potential (Ψg)
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** Guttation is the result of:
A. Transpiration pull
B. Root pressure
C. Osmosis
D. Diffusion
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** The stomata are primarily responsible for:
A. Absorption of water
B. Gaseous exchange
C. Anchorage
D. Conduction of food
**Correct Answer: B**

---

#### Medium

**21.** If a plant cell is placed in pure water, its water potential will:
A. Increase
B. Decrease
C. Remain the same
D. First increase then decrease
**Correct Answer: A**

**22.** The most widely accepted theory for the ascent of sap in trees is the:
A. Root pressure theory
B. Capillarity theory
C. Cohesion-tension-transpiration pull theory
D. Pumping action of living cells theory
**Correct Answer: C**

**23.** The direction of movement of water between two cells depends on their:
A. Individual water potentials
B. Turgor pressures
C. Solute potentials
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: A**

**24.** Which of the following elements is crucial for the opening and closing of stomata?
A. Calcium (Ca²⁺)
B. Magnesium (Mg²⁺)
C. Potassium (K⁺)
D. Iron (Fe²⁺)
**Correct Answer: C**

**25.** The Casparian strip is a band of suberin found in the endodermis of the root. Its function is to:
A. Provide mechanical support
B. Block the apoplastic pathway of water
C. Store food
D. Help in the formation of lateral roots
**Correct Answer: B**

**26.** In the pressure-flow hypothesis of translocation, what causes the pressure to build up at the source end?
A. Photosynthesis producing sugars
B. Active transport of sugars into the phloem
C. Absorption of water by osmosis into the phloem
D. Both B and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**27.** Which of the following is not a factor that affects the rate of transpiration?
A. Temperature
B. Light
C. Wind speed
D. Chlorophyll concentration in the leaves
**Correct Answer: D**

**28.** When a cell is fully turgid, its:
A. Water potential (Ψw) is zero
B. Turgor pressure (Ψp) is zero
C. Solute potential (Ψs) is zero
D. Water potential is equal to its solute potential
**Correct Answer: A**

**29.** The symplastic pathway of water movement involves:
A. Cell walls and intercellular spaces
B. The cytoplasm and plasmodesmata
C. The vacuole only
D. The xylem vessels only
**Correct Answer: B**

**30.** Unidirectional flow of water, minerals, and some organic nitrogen occurs through the:
A. Phloem
B. Xylem
C. Cortex
D. Pith
**Correct Answer: B**

**31.** The special proteins that help in the movement of water across the cell membrane are called:
A. Aquaporins
B. Porins
C. Permeases
D. Channels
**Correct Answer: A**

**32.** A flaccid cell has a turgor pressure (pressure potential) of:
A. 1
B. -1
C. 0
D. Equal to the solute potential
**Correct Answer: C**

**33.** Phloem sap mainly consists of:
A. Water and minerals
B. Water and sucrose
C. Hormones and amino acids
D. Starch and lipids
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** What will be the direction of net osmotic movement of water if a solution A, with Ψw = -8 bars, is separated by a semipermeable membrane from solution B, with Ψw = -10 bars?
A. From A to B
B. From B to A
C. There will be no net movement
D. Water will move in both directions equally
**Correct Answer: A**

**35.** The carrier proteins used in facilitated diffusion and active transport are similar in that they are both:
A. Highly specific
B. Susceptible to saturation
C. Respond to inhibitors
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**36.** Apoplastic movement of water in the root cortex is blocked at the endodermis due to the presence of:
A. The Casparian strip
B. The pericycle
C. The pith
D. The vascular cambium
**Correct Answer: A**

**37.** The exudation of xylem sap from the cut end of a stem is due to:
A. Transpiration pull
B. Guttation
C. Root pressure
D. Adhesion
**Correct Answer: C**

**38.** In the mechanism of stomatal opening, the influx of K⁺ ions into the guard cells is an example of:
A. Simple diffusion
B. Facilitated diffusion
C. Osmosis
D. Active transport
**Correct Answer: D**

**39.** The form in which sugar is transported through the phloem is:
A. Glucose
B. Fructose
C. Starch
D. Sucrose
**Correct Answer: D**

**40.** Porins are proteins that form large pores in the:
A. Inner membrane of mitochondria
B. Outer membrane of plastids and mitochondria
C. Cell membrane of plant cells
D. Tonoplast of vacuoles
**Correct Answer: B**

#### Hard

**41.** What would be the Ψp of a flaccid cell which has Ψs of -10 bars?
A. -10 bars
B. +10 bars
C. 0 bars
D. -5 bars
**Correct Answer: C**

**42.** The value of the water potential of a turgid plant cell is:
A. Equal to zero
B. Less than zero
C. More than zero
D. Equal to the solute potential
**Correct Answer: A**

**43.** Stomata of a plant open due to:
A. Influx of potassium ions
B. Efflux of potassium ions
C. Influx of calcium ions
D. Influx of magnesium ions
**Correct Answer: A**

**44.** The cohesion of water molecules and their adhesion to the walls of the xylem vessels are responsible for maintaining the:
A. Turgidity of cells
B. Continuity of the water column
C. Root pressure
D. Osmotic balance
**Correct Answer: B**

**45.** A plant cell has a solute potential of -15 bars and a pressure potential of 5 bars. The cell is placed in a solution with a water potential of -12 bars. The net movement of water will be:
A. From the cell into the solution
B. From the solution into the cell
C. There will be no net movement
D. It cannot be determined
**Correct Answer: B**
*(Note: Cell's Ψw = Ψs + Ψp = -15 + 5 = -10 bars. Since -10 > -12, water moves into the cell.)*

**46.** The loading of sucrose into the sieve tube elements at the source is an active process that:
A. Decreases the water potential in the sieve tube
B. Increases the water potential in the sieve tube
C. Does not affect the water potential
D. Requires the expenditure of glucose
**Correct Answer: A**

**47.** In a girdling experiment, the bark of a tree, including the phloem, is removed. Which of the following observations will be made?
A. The leaves will wilt immediately.
B. The roots will die first.
C. The shoot will die first.
D. The plant will continue to grow normally.
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** The primary difference between active transport and facilitated diffusion is that active transport:
A. Moves substances down a concentration gradient
B. Requires membrane proteins
C. Can move substances against a concentration gradient
D. Is a passive process
**Correct Answer: C**

**49.** If the turgor pressure of a cell becomes equal to its wall pressure, then:
A. The cell will become flaccid
B. The cell will undergo plasmolysis
C. There will be no further entry of water
D. The cell will burst
**Correct Answer: C**

**50.** The properties of cohesion, adhesion, and surface tension give water which of the following characteristics that helps in the ascent of sap?
A. Low viscosity
B. High tensile strength
C. High specific heat
D. The ability to act as a universal solvent
**Correct Answer: B**

&& Mineral Nutrition

#### Easy

**1.** The technique of growing plants in a nutrient solution, in the complete absence of soil, is known as:
A. Aeroponics
B. Hydroponics
C. Geoponics
D. Tissue culture
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** Which of the following is considered a macronutrient for plants?
A. Iron (Fe)
B. Manganese (Mn)
C. Nitrogen (N)
D. Zinc (Zn)
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** A mineral element is considered essential if:
A. It is present in the plant ash
B. The plant cannot complete its life cycle without it
C. It improves the growth of the plant
D. It is found in the soil
**Correct Answer: B**

**4. The deficiency of which element causes chlorosis (yellowing of leaves)?**
A. Calcium
B. Magnesium
C. Phosphorus
D. Boron
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The conversion of atmospheric nitrogen (N₂) into ammonia (NH₃) is called:
A. Nitrification
B. Denitrification
C. Nitrogen fixation
D. Ammonification
**Correct Answer: C**

**6.** Which of the following is a micronutrient?
A. Carbon
B. Potassium
C. Boron
D. Sulphur
**Correct Answer: C**

**7.** The bacterium *Rhizobium*, found in the root nodules of leguminous plants, is an example of a:
A. Symbiotic nitrogen-fixing bacterium
B. Free-living nitrogen-fixing bacterium
C. Nitrifying bacterium
D. Denitrifying bacterium
**Correct Answer: A**

**8.** The enzyme nitrogenase, which is crucial for nitrogen fixation, is highly sensitive to:
A. Carbon dioxide
B. Oxygen
C. Nitrogen
D. Water
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The conversion of ammonia to nitrate by soil bacteria is called:
A. Nitrogen fixation
B. Denitrification
C. Nitrification
D. Ammonification
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** Which mineral element is a constituent of the chlorophyll molecule?
A. Iron (Fe)
B. Manganese (Mn)
C. Magnesium (Mg)
D. Zinc (Zn)
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** The process of conversion of nitrate present in the soil back to atmospheric nitrogen is called:
A. Nitrification
B. Ammonification
C. Denitrification
D. Nitrogen fixation
**Correct Answer: C**

**12.** Necrosis, or the death of plant tissue, is a deficiency symptom of elements like:
A. N, K, S
B. Ca, Mg, Cu
C. Fe, Mn, Zn
D. N, P, K
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The pink-coloured pigment in the root nodules of legumes that acts as an oxygen scavenger is:
A. Haemoglobin
B. Leghaemoglobin
C. Phycoerythrin
D. Fucoxanthin
**Correct Answer: B**

**14.** Hydroponics was first demonstrated by:
A. Aristotle
B. Julius von Sachs
C. van Helmont
D. Priestley
**Correct Answer: B**

**15.** Which element is required for the synthesis of auxin?
A. Zinc (Zn)
B. Copper (Cu)
C. Boron (B)
D. Molybdenum (Mo)
**Correct Answer: A**

**16.** The main function of phosphorus in a plant is as a constituent of:
A. Cell membranes, nucleic acids, and ATP
B. Proteins and vitamins
C. Chlorophyll
D. Carbohydrates
**Correct Answer: A**

**17.** Which of the following is a free-living, anaerobic nitrogen-fixing bacterium?
A. *Azotobacter*
B. *Beijerinckia*
C. *Rhodospirillum*
D. *Rhizobium*
**Correct Answer: C**

**18.** The element that is a component of the enzyme nitrogenase is:
A. Molybdenum (Mo)
B. Manganese (Mn)
C. Zinc (Zn)
D. Copper (Cu)
**Correct Answer: A**

**19.** Deficiency symptoms of mobile elements like nitrogen first appear in the:
A. Younger leaves
B. Older (senescent) leaves
C. Roots
D. Flowers
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** The uptake of ions by the plant from the soil is primarily an:
A. Active process
B. Passive process
C. Osmotic process
D. Imbibitional process
**Correct Answer: A**

D. Roots

**26.** The toxicity of manganese can lead to the deficiency of:

**33.** Which of the following is not a macronutrient?

**35.** The form in which plants absorb nitrogen from the soil is primarily:

D. NO₂⁻

**36.** The element required for the uptake and utilization of Ca²⁺ is:

**37.** The conversion of organic nitrogen from dead plants and animals into ammonia is called:
A. Nitrification
B. Denitrification
C. Ammonification
D. Nitrogen fixation

**38.** Which of the following is a symptom of manganese toxicity in plants?
A. Appearance of brown spots surrounded by chlorotic veins

C. Stunted growth
D. Wilting of leaves

**39.** The function of leghaemoglobin in the root nodules of legumes is to:
A. Fix atmospheric nitrogen

&& Photosynthesis in Higher Plants

#### Easy

**1.** Photosynthesis is the process by which green plants synthesize:
A. Proteins
B. Fats
C. Carbohydrates
D. Vitamins
**Correct Answer: C**

**2.** The primary pigment responsible for trapping light energy in photosynthesis is:
A. Chlorophyll b
B. Xanthophyll
C. Carotenoid
D. Chlorophyll a
**Correct Answer: D**

**3.** The site of photosynthesis in a eukaryotic cell is the:
A. Mitochondrion
B. Ribosome
C. Chloroplast
D. Nucleus
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** The oxygen released during photosynthesis comes from the splitting of:
A. Carbon dioxide
B. Water
C. Glucose
D. Chlorophyll
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The light-dependent reactions of photosynthesis occur in the:
A. Stroma of the chloroplast
B. Thylakoid membranes of the chloroplast
C. Cytoplasm
D. Mitochondria
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The light-independent reactions (Calvin cycle) of photosynthesis occur in the:
A. Stroma of the chloroplast
B. Thylakoid membranes of the chloroplast
C. Cytoplasm
D. Ribosomes
**Correct Answer: A**

**7.** The products of the light-dependent reactions are:
A. Glucose and O₂
B. CO₂ and H₂O
C. ATP, NADPH, and O₂
D. ADP, NADP⁺, and H₂O
**CorrectAnswer: C**

**8.** The process of synthesizing ATP from ADP and inorganic phosphate in the presence of light is called:
A. Oxidative phosphorylation
B. Photophosphorylation
C. Substrate-level phosphorylation
D. Glycolysis
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The first stable product of the Calvin cycle in C₃ plants is a 3-carbon compound called:
A. Ribulose-1,5-bisphosphate (RuBP)
B. 3-phosphoglycerate (3-PGA)
C. Oxaloacetic acid (OAA)
D. Malic acid
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** Plants that use the C₄ pathway for carbon fixation are adapted to:
A. Cold and wet climates
B. Hot and dry climates
C. Temperate climates
D. Aquatic environments
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** The primary CO₂ acceptor in the C₃ cycle is:
A. Phosphoenolpyruvate (PEP)
B. Ribulose-1,5-bisphosphate (RuBP)
C. 3-phosphoglycerate (3-PGA)
D. Oxaloacetic acid (OAA)
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** The enzyme responsible for the primary carboxylation step in C₃ plants is:
A. PEP carboxylase
B. RuBisCO
C. Pyruvate kinase
D. Hexokinase
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The law of limiting factors was proposed by:
A. Blackman
B. Calvin
C. Hill
D. Arnon
**Correct Answer: A**

**14.** In the C₄ pathway, the first stable product of CO₂ fixation is:
A. 3-phosphoglycerate (3-PGA)
B. Oxaloacetic acid (OAA)
C. Malic acid
D. Ribulose-1,5-bisphosphate (RuBP)
**Correct Answer: B**

**15.** Photorespiration is a wasteful process because:
A. It produces ATP
B. It consumes ATP and releases CO₂
C. It produces sugar
D. It consumes O₂
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The two photosystems, PS I and PS II, are named according to the:
A. Wavelength of light they absorb
B. Order of their discovery
C. Their location in the chloroplast
D. Their role in the Calvin cycle
**Correct Answer: B**

**17.** In non-cyclic photophosphorylation, the electrons lost by PS II are replaced by electrons from:
A. PS I
B. CO₂
C. H₂O
D. NADPH
**Correct Answer: C**

**18.** The accessory pigments in photosynthesis, like carotenoids, function to:
A. Absorb light energy and transfer it to chlorophyll a
B. Protect chlorophyll a from photo-oxidation
C. Absorb wavelengths of light not absorbed by chlorophyll a
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**19.** An example of a C₄ plant is:
A. Rice
B. Wheat
C. Sugarcane
D. Tomato
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** During photosynthesis, light energy is converted into:
A. Mechanical energy
B. Chemical energy
C. Heat energy
D. Electrical energy
**Correct Answer: B**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The special leaf anatomy found in C₄ plants, characterized by a ring of large bundle sheath cells around the vascular bundles, is called:
A. Kranz anatomy
B. Isobilateral anatomy
C. Dorsiventral anatomy
D. Radial anatomy
**Correct Answer: A**

**22.** In cyclic photophosphorylation, only Photosystem I is involved, and the product is:
A. ATP only
B. NADPH only
C. Both ATP and NADPH
D. Oxygen
**Correct Answer: A**

**23.** For the synthesis of one molecule of glucose in the Calvin cycle, the number of ATP and NADPH molecules required is:
A. 12 ATP and 12 NADPH
B. 18 ATP and 12 NADPH
C. 6 ATP and 6 NADPH
D. 12 ATP and 18 NADPH
**Correct Answer: B**

**24.** The primary CO₂ acceptor in C₄ plants is:
A. RuBP
B. 3-PGA
C. PEP (Phosphoenolpyruvate)
D. OAA
**Correct Answer: C**

**25.** The enzyme PEP carboxylase is found in the:
A. Stroma of bundle sheath cells
B. Thylakoids of bundle sheath cells
C. Mesophyll cells of C₄ plants
D. Mesophyll cells of C₃ plants
**Correct Answer: C**

**26.** Photorespiration occurs when the enzyme RuBisCO acts as an oxygenase, binding with O₂ instead of CO₂. This happens when:
A. CO₂ concentration is high and O₂ concentration is low
B. O₂ concentration is high and CO₂ concentration is low
C. Both CO₂ and O₂ concentrations are high
D. Both CO₂ and O₂ concentrations are low
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** The chemiosmotic hypothesis for ATP synthesis in chloroplasts proposes that the proton gradient develops across the:
A. Outer chloroplast membrane
B. Inner chloroplast membrane
C. Stroma
D. Thylakoid membrane
**Correct Answer: D**

**28.** The reaction center of Photosystem I (PS I) is:
A. P680
B. P700
C. P870
D. P650
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** During the Z-scheme of light reactions, the final electron acceptor is:
A. Oxygen
B. ATP
C. NADP⁺
D. PS I
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** C₄ plants are more efficient in photosynthesis than C₃ plants mainly because:
A. They have more chloroplasts
B. They do not undergo photorespiration
C. They absorb more light
D. They have a higher CO₂ compensation point
**Correct Answer: B**

**31.** The three stages of the Calvin cycle are, in order:
A. Reduction, Carboxylation, Regeneration
B. Carboxylation, Regeneration, Reduction
C. Regeneration, Carboxylation, Reduction
D. Carboxylation, Reduction, Regeneration
**Correct Answer: D**

**32.** In non-cyclic photophosphorylation, both PS I and PS II are involved. The flow of electrons is from:
A. PS I to PS II
B. H₂O to PS II to PS I to NADP⁺
C. PS I to NADP⁺ to PS II
D. H₂O to PS I to PS II to NADP⁺
**Correct Answer: B**

**33.** CAM plants, like cacti, are adapted to arid conditions because they:
A. Do not have stomata
B. Keep their stomata open during the day and closed at night
C. Keep their stomata closed during the day and open at night
D. Have a very high rate of transpiration
**Correct Answer: C**

**34.** At a certain light intensity, the rate of photosynthesis is equal to the rate of respiration. This is known as the:
A. Saturation point
B. Compensation point
C. Limiting point
D. Optimal point
**Correct Answer: B**

**35.** The graph showing the effect of different wavelengths of light on the rate of photosynthesis is called an:
A. Absorption spectrum
B. Action spectrum
C. Emission spectrum
D. Reflection spectrum
**Correct Answer: B**

**36.** The enzyme RuBisCO has a dual nature, acting as both a carboxylase and an:
A. Oxygenase
B. Dehydrogenase
C. Isomerase
D. Hydrolase
**Correct Answer: A**

**37.** In the C₄ pathway, the CO₂ fixed in the mesophyll cells is transported to the bundle sheath cells in the form of:
A. Oxaloacetic acid
B. Malic acid or Aspartic acid
C. 3-PGA
D. PEP
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** Engelmann's experiment with *Cladophora* and aerobic bacteria demonstrated that:
A. Photosynthesis occurs in chloroplasts
B. Light is essential for photosynthesis
C. The most effective light for photosynthesis is in the blue and red regions of the spectrum
D. Oxygen is evolved during photosynthesis
**Correct Answer: C**

**39.** The first step in the Calvin cycle is the reaction of CO₂ with:
A. 3-PGA
B. PEP
C. RuBP
D. OAA
**Correct Answer: C**

**40.** The source of protons for the proton gradient in the thylakoid lumen is primarily the:
A. Splitting of water
B. Pumping of protons from the stroma
C. Breakdown of NADPH
D. Both A and B
**Correct Answer: D**

---

#### Hard

**41.** For every CO₂ molecule entering the Calvin cycle, the number of ATP and NADPH required for its fixation and reduction is:
A. 2 ATP and 2 NADPH
B. 2 ATP and 3 NADPH
C. 3 ATP and 2 NADPH
D. 3 ATP and 3 NADPH
**Correct Answer: C**

**42.** In the C₄ pathway, the decarboxylation of malic acid to release CO₂ for the Calvin cycle occurs in the:
A. Cytoplasm of mesophyll cells
B. Chloroplasts of mesophyll cells
C. Cytoplasm of bundle sheath cells
D. Chloroplasts of bundle sheath cells
**Correct Answer: D**

**43.** During photorespiration, the oxygenase activity of RuBisCO leads to the formation of:
A. One molecule of 3-PGA and one molecule of phosphoglycolate
B. Two molecules of 3-PGA
C. One molecule of RuBP
D. One molecule of OAA
**Correct Answer: A**

**44.** Which of the following statements is correct regarding the light-harvesting complex (LHC)?
A. It is made up of hundreds of pigment molecules bound to proteins.
B. The reaction center is formed by a molecule of chlorophyll b.
C. It absorbs light and directly participates in the photochemical reaction.
D. The LHC is part of the stroma.
**Correct Answer: A**

**45.** In the Hatch and Slack pathway (C₄ pathway), the enzyme RuBisCO is located in the:
A. Mesophyll cell chloroplasts
B. Bundle sheath cell chloroplasts
C. Cytoplasm of mesophyll cells
D. Cytoplasm of bundle sheath cells
**Correct Answer: B**

**46.** If a plant is shifted from a high CO₂ concentration to a low CO₂ concentration, what will happen to the C₃ cycle?
A. The concentration of RuBP will increase, and the concentration of 3-PGA will decrease.
B. The concentration of RuBP will decrease, and the concentration of 3-PGA will increase.
C. Both RuBP and 3-PGA concentrations will increase.
D. Both RuBP and 3-PGA concentrations will decrease.
**Correct Answer: A**

**47.** The net result of photorespiration is:
A. The net gain of ATP and NADPH
B. The net loss of ATP and NADPH, and a loss of fixed carbon
C. The net gain of fixed carbon
D. No change in the carbon or energy balance
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** If only cyclic photophosphorylation occurs in a chloroplast, which of the following will be produced?
A. O₂
B. NADPH
C. ATP
D. Both ATP and NADPH
**Correct Answer: C**

**49.** The movement of protons from the thylakoid lumen to the stroma through the F₀-F₁ particle is an example of:
A. Simple diffusion
B. Facilitated diffusion
C. Active transport
D. Osmosis
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** The experiment by Cornelius van Niel, using purple and green sulphur bacteria, was significant because it demonstrated that:
A. Light is essential for photosynthesis
B. Oxygen comes from the splitting of water, not carbon dioxide
C. Chlorophyll is the main photosynthetic pigment
D. Photosynthesis is a two-stage process
**Correct Answer: B**

&& Respiration in Plants

#### Easy

**1.** The process of breakdown of glucose to pyruvic acid in the cytoplasm is called:
A. Krebs' cycle
B. Glycolysis
C. Electron Transport System
D. Fermentation
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The universal energy currency of the cell is:
A. Glucose
B. ATP
C. NADP
D. Pyruvic acid
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** Aerobic respiration takes place in the:
A. Cytoplasm and Ribosomes
B. Cytoplasm and Mitochondria
C. Chloroplasts
D. Nucleus
**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** Glycolysis is also known as the:
A. EMP pathway
B. TCA cycle
C. Citric acid cycle
D. C₄ pathway
**Correct Answer: A**

**5.** The complete oxidation of one molecule of glucose in aerobic respiration yields approximately:
A. 2 ATP
B. 8 ATP
C. 38 ATP
D. 24 ATP
**Correct Answer: C**

**6.** The end product of glycolysis is:
A. Acetyl CoA
B. Citric acid
C. Pyruvic acid
D. Glucose-6-phosphate
**Correct Answer: C**

**7.** Fermentation is the process of anaerobic respiration that occurs in organisms like:
A. Algae
B. Yeast
C. Ferns
D. Higher plants
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The Krebs' cycle takes place in the:
A. Cytoplasm
B. Matrix of the mitochondria
C. Inner mitochondrial membrane
D. Outer mitochondrial membrane
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The final electron acceptor in the electron transport system of aerobic respiration is:
A. Hydrogen
B. Carbon dioxide
C. Cytochrome c
D. Oxygen
**Correct Answer: D**

**10.** The Respiratory Quotient (RQ) is the ratio of the:
A. Volume of O₂ consumed to the volume of CO₂ evolved
B. Volume of CO₂ evolved to the volume of O₂ consumed
C. Volume of CO₂ consumed to the volume of O₂ evolved
D. Volume of O₂ evolved to the volume of CO₂ consumed
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** Which of the following is a 5-carbon compound in the Krebs' cycle?
A. Citric acid
B. Malic acid
C. Succinic acid
D. α-ketoglutaric acid
**Correct Answer: D**

**12.** The synthesis of ATP during the electron transport system is called:
A. Photophosphorylation
B. Substrate-level phosphorylation
C. Oxidative phosphorylation
D. Dephosphorylation
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** The net gain of ATP molecules from one molecule of glucose during glycolysis is:
A. 8
B. 4
C. 2
D. 0
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The connecting link between glycolysis and the Krebs' cycle is:
A. Pyruvic acid
B. Acetyl CoA
C. Citric acid
D. Oxaloacetic acid
**Correct Answer: B**

**15.** The RQ for carbohydrates is:
A. 1
B. 0.7
C. 0.9
D. More than 1
**Correct Answer: A**

**16.** Respiration is considered an:
A. Anabolic process
B. Catabolic process
C. Amphibolic process
D. Photosynthetic process
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The number of CO₂ molecules released during one turn of the Krebs' cycle is:
A. 1
B. 2
C. 3
D. 4
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** Glycolysis occurs in:
A. All living cells
B. Only eukaryotic cells
C. Only aerobic organisms
D. Only anaerobic organisms
**Correct Answer: A**

**19.** The enzyme that converts glucose to glucose-6-phosphate in glycolysis is:
A. Phosphofructokinase
B. Hexokinase
C. Aldolase
D. Isomerase
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** The RQ for fats is typically:
A. Equal to 1
B. Less than 1
C. Greater than 1
D. Zero
**Correct Answer: B**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The net gain of ATP from the complete oxidation of one molecule of glucose in a eukaryotic cell is:
A. 2 ATP
B. 36 or 38 ATP
C. 4 ATP
D. 30 ATP
**Correct Answer: B**

**22.** In the electron transport system, the final electron is passed to oxygen by which complex?
A. Complex I (NADH dehydrogenase)
B. Complex II (Succinate dehydrogenase)
C. Complex III (Cytochrome bc₁)
D. Complex IV (Cytochrome c oxidase)
**Correct Answer: D**

**23.** During the conversion of succinyl-CoA to succinic acid in the Krebs' cycle, a molecule of GTP is formed. This is an example of:
A. Oxidative phosphorylation
B. Photophosphorylation
C. Substrate-level phosphorylation
D. Dehydrogenation
**Correct Answer: C**

**24.** The number of ATP molecules produced from one molecule of NADH that enters the ETS is:
A. 1
B. 2
C. 3
D. 4
**Correct Answer: C**

**25.** The number of ATP molecules produced from one molecule of FADH₂ that enters the ETS is:
A. 1
B. 2
C. 3
D. 4
**Correct Answer: B**

**26.** The RQ of an organism respiring a substrate that is incompletely oxidized, such as in anaerobic respiration, is:
A. 1
B. 0.7
C. 0
D. Infinite
**Correct Answer: D**

**27.** Which of the following statements is incorrect?
A. Glycolysis operates as long as it is supplied with NAD⁺ that can pick up hydrogen atoms.
B. Glycolysis is a universal pathway in all living organisms.
C. The enzymes of the Krebs' cycle are present in the mitochondrial matrix.
D. Oxygen is required for the process of glycolysis.
**Correct Answer: D**

**28.** The crucial event in aerobic respiration is the complete oxidation of:
A. Glucose to CO₂ and H₂O
B. Pyruvic acid to CO₂ and H₂O
C. Acetyl CoA to CO₂ and H₂O
D. Pyruvic acid to Acetyl CoA
**Correct Answer: C**

**29.** The overall goal of glycolysis, the Krebs' cycle, and the electron transport system is the formation of:
A. Sugars
B. Nucleic acids
C. ATP in small, stepwise units
D. ATP in one large oxidation
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** The respiratory pathway is considered an amphibolic pathway because it involves:
A. Both glycolysis and the Krebs' cycle
B. Both aerobic and anaerobic respiration
C. Both catabolism and anabolism
D. Both prokaryotic and eukaryotic cells
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** In alcoholic fermentation by yeast, the two key enzymes that convert pyruvic acid to ethanol are pyruvic acid decarboxylase and:
A. Alcohol dehydrogenase
B. Hexokinase
C. Aldolase
D. Lactate dehydrogenase
**Correct Answer: A**

**32.** The mobile electron carrier located on the outer surface of the inner mitochondrial membrane is:
A. Cytochrome a₃
B. Cytochrome c
C. Ubiquinone
D. Complex II
**Correct Answer: B**

**33.** How many molecules of pyruvic acid are formed from one molecule of glucose during glycolysis?
A. 1
B. 2
C. 3
D. 4
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** The first member of the citric acid cycle is citric acid, which is a 6-carbon compound formed by the condensation of Acetyl CoA with:
A. Malic acid
B. Succinic acid
C. Oxaloacetic acid
D. α-ketoglutaric acid
**Correct Answer: C**

**35.** The RQ for proteins is approximately:
A. 1.0
B. 0.9
C. 0.7
D. > 1
**Correct Answer: B**

**36.** The net ATP production during anaerobic respiration (fermentation) from one molecule of glucose is:
A. 38 ATP
B. 36 ATP
C. 8 ATP
D. 2 ATP
**Correct Answer: D**

**37.** Fats enter the respiratory pathway after being broken down into fatty acids and glycerol. Fatty acids are converted to:
A. Pyruvic acid
B. Acetyl CoA
C. Glucose
D. Malic acid
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The chemiosmotic coupling hypothesis of oxidative phosphorylation proposes that ATP is formed because:
A. There is a high concentration of protons in the intermembrane space.
B. A proton gradient forms across the inner mitochondrial membrane.
C. Protons are pumped from the matrix to the intermembrane space.
D. All of the above.
**Correct Answer: D**

**39.** The primary role of oxygen in cellular respiration is to:
A. Combine with carbon to form CO₂
B. Act as the final acceptor for electrons and protons
C. Catalyze the reactions of glycolysis
D. Provide energy for ATP synthesis
**Correct Answer: B**

**40.** The TCA (tricarboxylic acid) cycle starts with the formation of a six-carbon compound by the reaction between:
A. Malic acid and acetyl CoA
B. Succinic acid and pyruvic acid
C. Fumaric acid and pyruvic acid
D. Oxaloacetic acid and acetyl CoA
**Correct Answer: D**

#### Hard

**41.** During the complete oxidation of a glucose molecule, the number of ATP molecules synthesized through substrate-level phosphorylation is:
A. 2
B. 4
C. 6
D. 10
**Correct Answer: C**
*(Note: 4 from glycolysis (2 net) and 2 from Krebs' cycle (GTP))*

**42.** The RQ value of Tripalmitin (a fatty acid) is:
A. 0.9
B. 0.7
C. 1.0
D. 1.2
**Correct Answer: B**

**43.** In the electron transport system, Complex I and Complex II transfer their electrons to:
A. Cytochrome c
B. Oxygen
C. Ubiquinone (Coenzyme Q)
D. Cytochrome a₃
**Correct Answer: C**

**44.** The number of protons pumped into the intermembrane space for every two electrons that pass from NADH to oxygen is:
A. 4
B. 6
C. 8
D. 10
**Correct Answer: D**

**45.** In the mitochondrial electron transport chain, which of the following is the correct sequence of electron carriers?
A. NADH → FMN → Fe-S → CoQ → Cyt b → Cyt c₁ → Cyt c → Cyt a → Cyt a₃ → O₂
B. NADH → CoQ → Fe-S → Cyt c₁ → Cyt c → Cyt a → Cyt a₃ → O₂
C. NADH → FMN → CoQ → Cyt c → Cyt a → Cyt a₃ → O₂
D. NADH → Fe-S → Cyt b → Cyt c → O₂
**Correct Answer: A**

**46.** The enzyme of the Krebs' cycle that is located on the inner mitochondrial membrane, rather than in the matrix, is:
A. Isocitrate dehydrogenase
B. Malate dehydrogenase
C. Succinate dehydrogenase
D. Fumarase
**Correct Answer: C**

**47.** The inhibitor cyanide binds to the iron atom in cytochrome a₃, preventing the transfer of electrons to oxygen. This would directly result in:
A. The stoppage of the Krebs' cycle
B. The stoppage of glycolysis
C. A buildup of reduced NADH and FADH₂
D. An increase in ATP production
**Correct Answer: C**

**48.** In which of the following conversions in the Krebs' cycle is a molecule of FADH₂ formed?
A. Isocitrate to α-ketoglutarate
B. Succinate to Fumarate
C. Malate to Oxaloacetate
D. α-ketoglutarate to Succinyl-CoA
**Correct Answer: B**

**49.** If the RQ of a respiring plant is 1.3, the respiratory substrate is likely a(n):
A. Carbohydrate
B. Fat
C. Protein
D. Organic acid
**Correct Answer: D**

**50.** The regulatory, allosteric enzyme in glycolysis that is inhibited by high levels of ATP is:
A. Hexokinase
B. Pyruvate kinase
C. Phosphofructokinase
D. Aldolase
**Correct Answer: C**

&& Plant Growth and Development

#### Easy

**1.** Growth in plants is largely:
A. Determinate and restricted to certain regions
B. Indeterminate and restricted to certain regions
C. Determinate and occurs throughout the plant body
D. Indeterminate and occurs throughout the plant body
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The permanent and irreversible increase in size of an organ or its parts is called:
A. Development
B. Differentiation
C. Growth
D. Dedifferentiation
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** The plant growth regulators (PGRs) are also known as:
A. Phytohormones
B. Enzymes
C. Vitamins
D. Phytonutrients
**Correct Answer: A**

**4.** Which plant hormone is responsible for apical dominance?
A. Gibberellin
B. Cytokinin
C. Auxin
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** The hormone that promotes bolting (internode elongation prior to flowering) in rosette plants is:
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Cytokinin
D. Abscisic acid
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** Which of the following is a gaseous plant hormone?
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Cytokinin
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: D**

**7.** The hormone that acts as a general plant growth inhibitor and is also called the 'stress hormone' is:
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Ethylene
D. Abscisic acid (ABA)
**Correct Answer: D**

**8.** The effect of the relative length of day and night on the flowering of plants is called:
A. Vernalisation
B. Phototropism
C. Photoperiodism
D. Geotropism
**Correct Answer: C**

**9.** The induction of flowering in plants by treating them with low temperatures is called:
A. Photoperiodism
B. Vernalisation
C. Cryopreservation
D. Stratification
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** The process by which meristematic cells mature to perform specific functions is known as:
A. Growth
B. Development
C. Differentiation
D. Dedifferentiation
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** The growth of a plant organ can be plotted against time, resulting in an S-shaped curve. This is called a:
A. Linear growth curve
B. Exponential growth curve
C. Sigmoid growth curve
D. Bell-shaped curve
**Correct Answer: C**

**12.** The first plant hormone to be discovered was:
A. Gibberellin
B. Cytokinin
C. Ethylene
D. Auxin
**Correct Answer: D**

**13.** The hormone that promotes cell division is:
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Cytokinin
D. Abscisic acid
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The phenomenon of 'bolting' is induced by which hormone?
A. Auxin
B. Ethylene
C. Gibberellin
D. ABA
**Correct Answer: C**

**15.** Ripening of fruits is promoted by:
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Cytokinin
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: D**

**16.** Which hormone is responsible for the closure of stomata during water stress?
A. Auxin
B. Cytokinin
C. Abscisic acid
D. Gibberellin
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** Plants that require a light period shorter than a critical length to flower are called:
A. Long-day plants
B. Short-day plants
C. Day-neutral plants
D. Intermediate-day plants
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The process by which living, differentiated cells regain the capacity to divide is called:
A. Differentiation
B. Dedifferentiation
C. Redifferentiation
D. Development
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** An example of a synthetic auxin is:
A. IAA (Indole-3-acetic acid)
B. IBA (Indole-3-butyric acid)
C. NAA (Naphthalene acetic acid)
D. Zeatin
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** The site of perception of light/dark duration for photoperiodism is the:
A. Root
B. Stem
C. Flower
D. Leaf
**Correct Answer: D**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The sigmoid growth curve has three phases. The correct sequence is:
A. Lag phase, Log phase, Stationary phase
B. Log phase, Lag phase, Stationary phase
C. Stationary phase, Lag phase, Log phase
D. Lag phase, Stationary phase, Log phase
**Correct Answer: A**

**22.** Which of the following is not a physiological effect of auxin?
A. Promotes rooting in stem cuttings
B. Promotes flowering in pineapples
C. Promotes bolting in beet
D. Prevents fruit and leaf drop at early stages
**Correct Answer: C**

**23.** The 'bakanae' or foolish seedling disease of rice led to the discovery of:
A. Auxins
B. Gibberellins
C. Cytokinins
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: B**

**24.** Which hormone can overcome apical dominance?
A. Auxin
B. Cytokinin
C. Abscisic acid
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** The hormone responsible for the triple response in seedlings (inhibition of stem elongation, promotion of lateral growth, and swelling of the axis) is:
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Cytokinin
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: D**

**26.** Abscisic acid (ABA) acts as an antagonist to which hormone?
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellic acid
C. Cytokinin
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** A short-day plant, like Xanthium, will flower only if:
A. The day length is longer than a critical period.
B. The day length is shorter than a critical period.
C. The continuous dark period is shorter than a critical period.
D. The continuous dark period is longer than a critical period.
**Correct Answer: D**

**28.** The formation of interfascicular cambium and cork cambium from fully differentiated parenchyma cells is an example of:
A. Differentiation
B. Dedifferentiation
C. Redifferentiation
D. Plasticity
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** The 'Richmond-Lang effect' refers to the delay of senescence by:
A. Auxins
B. Gibberellins
C. Cytokinins
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** The absolute growth rate is the measurement of the total growth per unit time, while the relative growth rate is the:
A. Growth per unit time per initial parameter
B. Growth per unit area
C. Growth in length only
D. Total growth divided by the number of cells
**Correct Answer: A**

**31.** The phytochrome pigment is involved in the perception of the stimulus for:
A. Geotropism
B. Phototropism
C. Photoperiodism
D. Vernalisation
**Correct Answer: C**

**32.** The 'agent orange', a herbicide used in the Vietnam War, was a mixture of synthetic:
A. Auxins
B. Gibberellins
C. Cytokinins
D. ABA
**Correct Answer: A**

**33.** Which of the following statements about ethylene is incorrect?
A. It is a simple gaseous PGR.
B. It is synthesized in large amounts by tissues undergoing senescence and ripening.
C. It promotes seed and bud dormancy.
D. It is highly effective in fruit ripening.
**Correct Answer: C**

**34.** Development in plants is the sum of two processes:
A. Growth and Photosynthesis
B. Growth and Differentiation
C. Photosynthesis and Respiration
D. Differentiation and Reproduction
**Correct Answer: B**

**35.** The ability of plants to follow different pathways in response to the environment to form different kinds of structures is called:
A. Plasticity
B. Elasticity
C. Senescence
D. Dormancy
**Correct Answer: A**

**36.** The most widely used compound as a source of ethylene is:
A. Ethephon
B. Kinetin
C. NAA
D. 2,4-D
**Correct Answer: A**

**37.** In the geometric growth phase, the number of cells increases exponentially. It is expressed as:
A. W₁ = W₀ + rt
B. W₁ = W₀ e^(rt)
C. Lₜ = L₀ + rt
D. Lₜ = L₀ e^(rt)
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** Kinetin, a modified form of adenine, was discovered from autoclaved:
A. Coconut milk
B. Corn kernels
C. Herring sperm DNA
D. Rice seedlings
**Correct Answer: C**

**39.** The phenomenon of vernalisation can be seen in:
A. Sugarcane
B. Wheat and Barley
C. Cotton
D. Maize
**Correct Answer: B**

**40.** Which hormone helps in inducing parthenocarpy in tomatoes?
A. Cytokinin
B. Abscisic acid
C. Gibberellin
D. Auxin
**Correct Answer: D**
*(Note: Both Auxin and Gibberellin can induce parthenocarpy, but auxin is a more common answer for tomatoes.)*

#### Hard

**41.** To speed up the malting process in the brewing industry, which plant growth regulator is used?
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Cytokinin
D. Ethylene
**Correct Answer: B**

**42.** A short-day plant is exposed to a long day but the long day is interrupted by a flash of red light followed by a flash of far-red light in the middle of the dark period. The plant will:
A. Flower
B. Not flower
C. Produce more leaves
D. Die
**Correct Answer: A**

**43.** The coconut milk factor, which promotes cell division, is a:
A. Auxin
B. Gibberellin
C. Cytokinin
D. Abscisic acid
**Correct Answer: C**

**44.** The process of cells derived from meristems differentiating and maturing to perform specific functions is called differentiation. The structures formed by this process are:
A. Primary tissues
B. Secondary tissues
C. Apical meristems
D. Lateral meristems
**Correct Answer: A**

**45.** Which of the following is a correct statement regarding the discovery of plant hormones?
A. Charles Darwin and Francis Darwin observed that the coleoptile of canary grass responded to red light.
B. F. Skoog and his co-workers discovered kinetin from coconut milk.
C. F.W. Went isolated auxin from the tips of oat coleoptiles.
D. E. Kurosawa reported the appearance of symptoms of 'bakanae' disease in uninfected rice seedlings when treated with sterile filtrates of the fungus *Gibberella fujikuroi*.
**Correct Answer: D**

**46.** If a plant produces flowers when exposed to alternating periods of 5 hours of light and 3 hours of dark, it is a:
A. Short-day plant
B. Long-day plant
C. Day-neutral plant
D. Cannot be determined
**Correct Answer: C**

**47.** The differentiation of shoots and roots in a callus during plant tissue culture is controlled by the ratio of:
A. Auxin to Gibberellin
B. Cytokinin to Gibberellin
C. Auxin to Cytokinin
D. Gibberellin to Abscisic acid
**Correct Answer: C**

**48.** Which of the following PGRs is a derivative of carotenoids?
A. Indole-3-acetic acid (IAA)
B. Gibberellic acid (GA₃)
C. Abscisic acid (ABA)
D. Kinetin
**Correct Answer: C**

**49.** A plant that requires a photoperiod of 13 hours of light to flower is exposed to a cycle of 8 hours light, 8 hours dark, and another 8 hours of light. The plant will:
A. Flower
B. Not flower
C. Form more vegetative buds
D. Die
**Correct Answer: A**

**50.** The phase of growth which shows the maximum increase in the size of the cells is the:
A. Phase of cell division (meristematic phase)
B. Phase of elongation
C. Phase of maturation
D. Lag phase
**Correct Answer: B**

&& Digestion and Absorption

#### Easy

**1.** The process of converting complex food substances into simple, absorbable forms is called:
A. Respiration
B. Circulation
C. Excretion
D. Digestion
**Correct Answer: D**

**2.** The human dental formula for an adult is:
A. 2123/2123
B. 2102/2102
C. 2122/2122
D. 2023/2023
**Correct Answer: A**

**3.** The hard chewing surface of the teeth, which helps in the mastication of food, is the:
A. Dentine
B. Enamel
C. Pulp
D. Cementum
**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** The enzyme salivary amylase, present in saliva, begins the digestion of:
A. Proteins
B. Fats
C. Carbohydrates (Starch)
D. Nucleic acids
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** The stomach primarily stores food for:
A. 1-2 hours

**6.** Pepsin, the protein-digesting enzyme of the stomach, is activated by:

**7.** The largest gland in the human body is the:
A. Pancreas

**8.** Bile, which is secreted by the liver, aids in the digestion of:
A. Proteins
B. Carbohydrates
C. Fats
D. Vitamins

**9.** The small intestine is distinguishable into three regions: a 'C' shaped duodenum, a long coiled middle portion jejunum, and a highly coiled:
A. Caecum
B. Colon
C. Ileum
D. Rectum

**10.** The finger-like foldings in the small intestine that increase the surface area for absorption are called:
A. Villi
B. Rugae
C. Taeniae coli
D. Haustra

**11.** The function of the enzyme trypsin is to digest:
A. Starch
B. Fats
C. Proteins
D. Lactose

**12.** The end products of carbohydrate digestion are:
A. Amino acids
B. Fatty acids and glycerol
C. Monosaccharides (like glucose)
D. Polypeptides

**13.** Absorption of substances takes place in different parts of the alimentary canal. However, maximum absorption occurs in the:
A. Stomach
B. Small intestine
C. Large intestine
D. Mouth

**14.** The muscular contractions that move food through the alimentary canal are called:
A. Peristalsis
B. Mastication
C. Deglutition
D. Emulsification

**15.** The acidic environment of the stomach is due to the secretion of:

**17.** The large intestine primarily absorbs:
A. Water, minerals, and certain drugs

**18.** The inflammation of the liver, often caused by a viral infection, is known as:
A. Jaundice

&& Breathing and Exchange of Gases

#### Easy

**1.** The primary site for the exchange of gases in the human respiratory system is the:
A. Trachea
B. Bronchi
C. Bronchioles
D. Alveoli
**Correct Answer: D**

**2.** The process of breathing involves two stages: inspiration and:
A. Expiration
B. Respiration
C. Circulation
D. Excretion
**Correct Answer: A**

**3.** The volume of air inspired or expired during a normal, quiet breath is called the:
A. Tidal Volume (TV)
B. Inspiratory Reserve Volume (IRV)
C. Expiratory Reserve Volume (ERV)
D. Vital Capacity (VC)
**Correct Answer: A**

**4.** The respiratory pigment present in human blood that binds with oxygen is:
A. Haemocyanin
B. Haemoglobin
C. Myoglobin
D. Cytochrome
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The diaphragm is a muscular structure that separates the thoracic cavity from the:
A. Abdominal cavity
B. Pelvic cavity
C. Cranial cavity
D. Pleural cavity
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** During inspiration, the diaphragm:
A. Relaxes and moves up
B. Contracts and flattens
C. Relaxes and flattens
D. Contracts and moves up
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** The exchange of gases in the lungs occurs by the process of:
A. Active transport
B. Osmosis
C. Simple diffusion
D. Facilitated diffusion
**Correct Answer: C**

**8.** The 'Adam's apple' is a common name for the:
A. Epiglottis
B. Larynx (voice box)
C. Trachea
D. Pharynx
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The maximum volume of air a person can breathe in after a forced expiration is known as:
A. Tidal Volume
B. Vital Capacity
C. Total Lung Capacity
D. Residual Volume
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** Most of the carbon dioxide (about 70%) in the blood is transported in the form of:
A. Dissolved gas in plasma
B. Bicarbonate ions
C. Carbamino-haemoglobin
D. Carbonic acid
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** The trachea is lined with incomplete cartilaginous rings that prevent it from:
A. Collapsing
B. Expanding
C. Secreting mucus
D. Exchanging gases
**Correct Answer: A**

**12.** The structure that prevents the entry of food into the glottis during swallowing is the:
A. Larynx
B. Pharynx
C. Epiglottis
D. Vocal cord
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** Normal breathing rate in a healthy adult human at rest is about:
A. 5-8 breaths/min
B. 12-16 breaths/min
C. 20-25 breaths/min
D. 70-75 breaths/min
**Correct Answer: B**

**14.** The total volume of air accommodated in the lungs at the end of a forced inspiration is the:
A. Vital Capacity
B. Total Lung Capacity
C. Inspiratory Capacity
D. Functional Residual Capacity
**Correct Answer: B**

**15.** The partial pressure of oxygen (pO₂) in the alveoli is approximately:
A. 40 mm Hg
B. 95 mm Hg
C. 104 mm Hg
D. 159 mm Hg
**Correct Answer: C**

**16.** A spirometer is an instrument used to measure:
A. Blood pressure
B. Heart rate
C. Breathing volumes
D. Blood sugar level
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The volume of air that remains in the lungs even after a forceful expiration is the:
A. Tidal Volume
B. Vital Capacity
C. Residual Volume
D. Inspiratory Reserve Volume
**Correct Answer: C**

**18.** The binding of oxygen with haemoglobin is primarily related to the:
A. Partial pressure of O₂
B. Partial pressure of CO₂
C. Hydrogen ion concentration
D. Temperature
**Correct Answer: A**

**19.** The respiratory rhythm centre is located in the:
A. Cerebrum
B. Cerebellum
C. Medulla oblongata
D. Pons
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** The layer of fluid between the two pleural membranes surrounding the lungs serves to:
A. Reduce friction on the lung surface
B. Secrete hormones
C. Exchange gases
D. Store air
**Correct Answer: A**

#### Medium

**21.** The oxygen-haemoglobin dissociation curve is:
A. A straight line
B. A rectangular hyperbola
C. A sigmoid (S-shaped) curve
D. A parabolic curve
**Correct Answer: C**

**22.** The amount of CO₂ that can be delivered by every 100 ml of deoxygenated blood to the alveoli is approximately:
A. 1 ml
B. 2 ml
C. 3 ml
D. 4 ml
**Correct Answer: D**

**23.** A shift of the oxygen dissociation curve to the right indicates:
A. Increased affinity of haemoglobin for oxygen
B. Decreased affinity of haemoglobin for oxygen
C. A decrease in pCO₂
D. An increase in pH
**Correct Answer: B**

**24.** The condition of difficulty in breathing causing wheezing due to inflammation of bronchi and bronchioles is called:
A. Emphysema
B. Asthma
C. Pneumonia
D. Bronchitis
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** The formation of bicarbonate ions from CO₂ and H₂O in red blood cells is catalyzed by the enzyme:
A. Carbonic anhydrase
B. Carboxylase
C. Amylase
D. Lipase
**Correct Answer: A**

**26.** The partial pressure of CO₂ (pCO₂) in the deoxygenated blood flowing from the tissues is approximately:
A. 40 mm Hg
B. 45 mm Hg
C. 95 mm Hg
D. 104 mm Hg
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** The pneumotaxic centre, which can moderate the functions of the respiratory rhythm centre, is present in the:
A. Medulla
B. Pons
C. Cerebellum
D. Cerebrum
**Correct Answer: B**

**28.** The condition in which the alveolar walls are damaged, leading to a decrease in the respiratory surface area, is known as:
A. Asthma
B. Emphysema
C. Pleurisy
D. Rhinitis
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** The Bohr effect describes the phenomenon where an increase in CO₂ concentration in the blood leads to:
A. An increase in the affinity of haemoglobin for oxygen
B. A decrease in the affinity of haemoglobin for oxygen
C. An increase in the number of red blood cells
D. A decrease in the breathing rate
**Correct Answer: B**

**30.** The total amount of air a person can expire after a normal inspiration is the:
A. Expiratory Reserve Volume (ERV)
B. Functional Residual Capacity (FRC)
C. Expiratory Capacity (EC)
D. Vital Capacity (VC)
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** What is true about the transport of CO₂ in the blood?
A. About 20-25% is carried by haemoglobin as carbamino-haemoglobin.
B. About 70% is carried as bicarbonate ions.
C. About 7% is transported in a dissolved state in plasma.
D. All of the above are true.
**Correct Answer: D**

**32.** The chloride shift is a process that occurs in the red blood cells to:
A. Transport oxygen
B. Maintain ionic balance during bicarbonate transport
C. Clot blood
D. Regulate pH
**Correct Answer: B**

**33.** Which of the following conditions is favourable for the dissociation of oxygen from oxyhaemoglobin at the tissues?
A. High pO₂, low pCO₂, lower H⁺ concentration
B. Low pO₂, high pCO₂, higher H⁺ concentration
C. Low pO₂, low pCO₂, lower H⁺ concentration
D. High pO₂, high pCO₂, higher H⁺ concentration
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** Occupational respiratory disorders, like silicosis and asbestosis, are common in people working in:
A. Cotton industries
B. Stone-breaking and grinding industries
C. Chemical plants
D. Pharmaceutical companies
**Correct Answer: B**

**35.** The volume of air involved in breathing movements can be estimated by using a:
A. Sphygmomanometer
B. Stethoscope
C. Spirometer
D. Electrocardiograph
**Correct Answer: C**

**36.** Vital Capacity (VC) is equal to:
A. TV + IRV
B. TV + ERV
C. IRV + ERV
D. TV + IRV + ERV
**Correct Answer: D**

**37.** The amount of oxygen delivered by every 100 ml of oxygenated blood to the tissues under normal physiological conditions is about:
A. 2 ml
B. 5 ml
C. 10 ml
D. 20 ml
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The role of the conducting part of the respiratory system (from nostrils to bronchioles) is to:
A. Transport atmospheric air to the alveoli
B. Clear the air from foreign particles
C. Humidify and bring the air to body temperature
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**39.** An increase in H⁺ concentration (decrease in pH) in the blood will cause the oxygen dissociation curve to:
A. Shift to the left
B. Shift to the right
C. Become a straight line
D. Remain unchanged
**Correct Answer: B**

**40.** The Haldane effect explains that:
A. Oxygenation of haemoglobin promotes the release of CO₂ from the blood
B. Deoxygenation of haemoglobin promotes the uptake of CO₂ by the blood
C. Both A and B are correct
D. The binding of CO₂ with haemoglobin is related to pO₂
**Correct Answer: C**

**41.** The partial pressure of oxygen is the same in:
A. Alveolar air and oxygenated blood
B. Deoxygenated blood and tissue fluid
C. Oxygenated blood and tissue fluid
D. Alveolar air and deoxygenated blood
**Correct Answer: B**

**42.** A person has an Inspiratory Capacity of 3500 ml and an Expiratory Reserve Volume of 1000 ml. If the Residual Volume is 1200 ml, what is their Total Lung Capacity?
A. 4500 ml
B. 4700 ml
C. 5700 ml
D. 5200 ml
**Correct Answer: B**
*(Note: IC = TV+IRV. VC = TV+IRV+ERV = IC+ERV = 3500+1000 = 4500. TLC = VC+RV = 4500+1200 = 5700. Wait, there's a typo in my reasoning. Let's re-calculate. IC = TV+IRV=3500. ERV=1000. RV=1200. TLC = TV+IRV+ERV+RV = IC+ERV+RV = 3500+1000+1200 = 5700. The provided answer C is correct, my previous check was wrong.)*
**Correct Answer: C**

**43.** The chemosensitive area of the respiratory centre in the medulla is highly sensitive to changes in:
A. Blood O₂ concentration
B. Blood CO₂ concentration and H⁺ ions
C. The pressure in the alveoli
D. The stretching of the lung tissue
**Correct Answer: B**

**44.** If a person breathes in a gas mixture with a pO₂ of 100 mm Hg, but their arterial blood pO₂ is only 70 mm Hg, this could be due to:
A. Increased physical activity
B. High altitude
C. A ventilation-perfusion mismatch in the lungs
D. Anemia
**Correct Answer: C**

**45.** Carbonic anhydrase is found in high concentration in:
A. Plasma
B. Leucocytes
C. Erythrocytes (RBCs)
D. Blood platelets

**46.** What percentage of oxygen is transported bound to haemoglobin in the blood?
A. 7%
B. 20-25%
C. 70%
D. 97%
**Correct Answer: D**

**47.** The inspiratory muscles that contract during normal quiet breathing are the:
A. Diaphragm only
B. External intercostal muscles only
C. Diaphragm and external intercostal muscles
D. Internal intercostal muscles and abdominal muscles
**Correct Answer: C**

**48.** The partial pressure of oxygen in inspired air and expired air is approximately (at sea level):
A. 159 mm Hg and 116 mm Hg
B. 104 mm Hg and 40 mm Hg
C. 159 mm Hg and 40 mm Hg
D. 104 mm Hg and 95 mm Hg

**49.** A person's Tidal Volume is 500 ml, Vital Capacity is 4000 ml, and Inspiratory Reserve Volume is 2500 ml. Their Expiratory Reserve Volume is:
A. 1000 ml
B. 1500 ml

**50.** During forced expiration, the actively contracting muscles are the:
A. Diaphragm and external intercostals

&& Body Fluids and Circulation

#### Easy

**1.** The fluid matrix of blood is called:
A. Plasma
B. Serum
C. Lymph
D. Formed elements
**Correct Answer: A**

**2.** The red blood cells (RBCs) in humans are:
A. Biconcave and nucleated
B. Biconcave and enucleated
C. Spherical and nucleated
D. Oval and enucleated
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** The most abundant type of white blood cell (WBC) is the:
A. Basophil
B. Eosinophil
C. Lymphocyte
D. Neutrophil
**Correct Answer: D**

**4.** The process of blood clotting is initiated by:
A. RBCs
B. WBCs
C. Platelets (Thrombocytes)
D. Plasma
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** A person with blood group 'O' is called a universal donor because they lack:
A. Antigens on their RBCs
B. Antibodies in their plasma
C. Both antigens and antibodies
D. A nucleus in their RBCs
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** The human heart has how many chambers?
A. One
B. Two
C. Three
D. Four
**Correct Answer: D**

**7.** The muscular wall that separates the right and left ventricles of the heart is the:
A. Inter-atrial septum
B. Inter-ventricular septum
C. Atrioventricular septum
D. Tricuspid valve
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The natural pacemaker of the heart is the:
A. Atrioventricular (AV) node
B. Sino-atrial (SA) node
C. Purkinje fibres
D. Bundle of His
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The sequence of events that occurs in the heart from the beginning of one heartbeat to the beginning of the next is called the:
A. Cardiac cycle
B. Heart rate
C. Stroke volume
D. Cardiac output
**Correct Answer: A**

**10.** An electrocardiogram (ECG) is a graphical representation of the:
A. Electrical activity of the heart
B. Blood pressure in the arteries
C. Volume of blood pumped by the heart
D. Sound of the heartbeat
**Correct Answer: A**

**11.** The pulmonary artery carries:
A. Oxygenated blood from the heart to the lungs
B. Deoxygenated blood from the heart to the lungs
C. Oxygenated blood from the lungs to the heart
D. Deoxygenated blood from the body to the heart
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** The bicuspid valve (or mitral valve) is located between the:
A. Right atrium and right ventricle
B. Left atrium and left ventricle
C. Right ventricle and pulmonary artery
D. Left ventricle and aorta
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The fluid that is filtered out of the blood capillaries and bathes the tissues is called:
A. Blood
B. Plasma
C. Serum
D. Lymph (Tissue fluid)
**Correct Answer: D**

**14.** The normal blood pressure in a healthy adult is:
A. 120/80 mm Hg
B. 80/120 mm Hg
C. 140/90 mm Hg
D. 90/140 mm Hg
**Correct Answer: A**

**15.** The lifespan of a human red blood cell is approximately:
A. 120 hours
B. 120 days
C. 12 days
D. 12 years
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** Which of the following blood cells are involved in the immune response?
A. Erythrocytes
B. Thrombocytes
C. Lymphocytes
D. Osteocytes
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The circulation in which blood flows from the heart to the lungs and back to the heart is called:
A. Systemic circulation
B. Pulmonary circulation
C. Coronary circulation
D. Portal circulation
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The 'lub' sound of the heartbeat is produced by the closure of the:
A. Semilunar valves
B. Tricuspid and bicuspid valves
C. Aortic valve only
D. Pulmonary valve only
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** The T wave in an ECG represents:
A. Depolarisation of the atria
B. Depolarisation of the ventricles
C. Repolarisation of the ventricles
D. Repolarisation of the atria
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** A person with blood group 'AB' can receive blood from:
A. Only group AB
B. Only group O
C. Groups A, B, and O
D. Any blood group (A, B, AB, O)
**Correct Answer: D**

#### Medium

**21.** Serum is different from blood plasma because it lacks:
A. Antibodies
B. Albumin
C. Clotting factors (like fibrinogen)

B. Leukemia

D. Polycythemia
**Correct Answer: C**

**23.** The Rh factor is an antigen found on the surface of:
A. WBCs
B. Platelets
C. RBCs
D. Plasma proteins

**24.** The cardiac output is the volume of blood pumped out by each ventricle per minute. It is calculated as:
A. Heart rate × Stroke volume
B. Heart rate / Stroke volume
C. Stroke volume / Heart rate
D. Heart rate + Stroke volume
**Correct Answer: A**

**25.** The P wave in a standard ECG represents:
A. Ventricular depolarisation
B. Atrial depolarisation
C. Ventricular repolarisation
D. Atrial repolarisation

**26.** The 'dub' sound of the heartbeat is associated with the closure of the:
A. Tricuspid valve
B. Bicuspid valve
C. Both A and B
D. Semilunar valves
**Correct Answer: D**

**27.** The hepatic portal vein carries blood from the:
A. Liver to the heart

C. Heart to the liver
D. Liver to the intestine

**28.** The enzyme that converts fibrinogen to fibrin during blood clotting is:
A. Thrombin
B. Prothrombin
C. Thromboplastin
D. Fibrinolysin
**Correct Answer: A**

**29.** The condition where plaque builds up inside your arteries, hardening and narrowing them, is called:
A. Atherosclerosis
B. Arteriosclerosis
C. Angina pectoris
D. Hypertension
**Correct Answer: A**

**30.** The QRS complex in an ECG represents:
A. The depolarisation of the atria
B. The repolarisation of the atria
C. The depolarisation of the ventricles
D. The repolarisation of the ventricles
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** The basophils are a type of WBC that secrete:
A. Histamine, serotonin, and heparin
B. Antibodies
C. Phagocytic cells
D. Thromboplastin
**Correct Answer: A**

**32.** A person with AB blood group has:
A. Antigen A and antigen B on RBCs, and no antibodies in plasma
B. No antigens on RBCs, and both anti-A and anti-B antibodies in plasma
C. Antigen A on RBCs and anti-B antibody in plasma
D. Antigen B on RBCs and anti-A antibody in plasma
**Correct Answer: A**

**33.** The duration of a normal cardiac cycle is:
A. 0.5 seconds
B. 0.8 seconds
C. 1.0 seconds
D. 1.2 seconds
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** Double circulation is a circulatory system in which:
A. Blood flows through the heart twice for each complete circuit of the body
B. There are two hearts
C. Blood is a mixture of oxygenated and deoxygenated blood
D. The blood flows in two different directions
**Correct Answer: A**

**35.** Erythroblastosis foetalis can occur if:
A. The mother is Rh-positive and the foetus is Rh-negative
B. The mother is Rh-negative and the foetus is Rh-positive
C. Both mother and foetus are Rh-negative
D. Both mother and foetus are Rh-positive
**Correct Answer: B**

**36.** The nodal tissue located in the lower-left corner of the right atrium is the:
A. SA node
B. AV node
C. Purkinje fibres
D. Bundle of His
**Correct Answer: B**

**37.** Hypertension, or high blood pressure, is diagnosed when the blood pressure is consistently:
A. 120/80 mm Hg
B. 140/90 mm Hg or higher
C. 100/70 mm Hg or lower
D. 80/120 mm Hg
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The primary function of lymph is to:
A. Transport oxygen to the tissues
B. Return interstitial fluid to the blood
C. Initiate blood clotting
D. Produce red blood cells
**Correct Answer: B**

**39.** During the joint diastole phase of the cardiac cycle:
A. Both atria and ventricles are contracted
B. Both atria and ventricles are relaxed
C. Atria are contracted and ventricles are relaxed
D. Ventricles are contracted and atria are relaxed
**Correct Answer: B**

**40.** The mineral ion that is essential for blood clotting is:
A. Sodium (Na⁺)
B. Potassium (K⁺)
C. Iron (Fe²⁺)
D. Calcium (Ca²⁺)
**Correct Answer: D**

#### Hard

**41.** If the stroke volume of the left ventricle is 70 ml and the heart rate is 72 beats per minute, the cardiac output is:
A. 5040 ml/min
B. 7200 ml/min
C. 7000 ml/min
D. 4900 ml/min
**Correct Answer: A**

**42.** The correct pathway for the conduction of the cardiac impulse is:
A. SA node → AV node → Bundle of His → Purkinje fibres
B. AV node → SA node → Bundle of His → Purkinje fibres
C. SA node → Purkinje fibres → AV node → Bundle of His
D. Bundle of His → Purkinje fibres → SA node → AV node
**Correct Answer: A**

**43.** Which of the following statements is incorrect?
A. A person of blood group O can donate blood to a person of any blood group.
B. A person of blood group AB can receive blood from a person of any blood group.
C. A person of blood group A can donate blood to a person of blood group B.
D. A person of blood group B has anti-A antibodies in their plasma.
**Correct Answer: C**

**44.** Heart failure is a condition where the heart is not pumping blood effectively enough to meet the needs of the body. It is sometimes called:
A. Cardiac arrest
B. Heart attack
C. Congestive heart failure
D. Angina pectoris
**Correct Answer: C**

**45.** The sympathetic nervous system's effect on the heart is to:
A. Decrease the heart rate and strength of contraction
B. Increase the heart rate and strength of contraction
C. Only decrease the heart rate
D. Only increase the strength of contraction
**Correct Answer: B**

**46.** During ventricular systole:
A. The AV valves are open and the semilunar valves are closed.
B. The AV valves are closed and the semilunar valves are open.
C. Both AV and semilunar valves are open.
D. Both AV and semilunar valves are closed.
**Correct Answer: B**

**47.** The 'graveyard' of red blood cells is the:
A. Liver
B. Spleen
C. Bone marrow
D. Kidney
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** The P wave of the ECG coincides with which event of the cardiac cycle?
A. Ventricular systole
B. Atrial systole
C. Joint diastole
D. Ventricular diastole
**Correct Answer: B**

**49.** An open circulatory system is found in:
A. Earthworms and Leeches (Annelids)
B. Insects and Prawns (Arthropods)
C. Humans and Rabbits (Mammals)
D. Frogs and Toads (Amphibians)
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** The first heart sound 'lub' is of longer duration and lower pitch, while the second heart sound 'dub' is of shorter duration and higher pitch. This is because:
A. 'Lub' is from the closure of semilunar valves, and 'dub' is from AV valves.
B. 'Lub' is from the closure of AV valves, and 'dub' is from semilunar valves.
C. The ventricles are larger than the atria.
D. The aorta is larger than the pulmonary artery.
**Correct Answer: B**

&& Excretory Products and their Elimination

#### Easy

**1.** The primary excretory organ in humans is the:
A. Liver
B. Skin
C. Lung
D. Kidney
**Correct Answer: D**

**2.** The major nitrogenous waste product excreted by humans is:
A. Ammonia
B. Uric acid
C. Urea
D. Creatinine
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** The functional unit of the kidney is the:
A. Neuron
B. Nephron
C. Alveolus
D. Sarcomere
**Correct Answer: B**

**4. The process of urine formation involves three main steps: glomerular filtration, reabsorption, and:**
A. Secretion
B. Excretion
C. Micturition
D. Dialysis
**Correct Answer: A**

**5.** The part of the nephron where filtration of blood occurs is the:
A. Loop of Henle
B. Proximal Convoluted Tubule (PCT)
C. Distal Convoluted Tubule (DCT)
D. Glomerulus
**Correct Answer: D**

**6.** The U-shaped part of the nephron that dips into the renal medulla is the:
A. Bowman's capsule
B. Loop of Henle
C. Collecting duct
D. Proximal Convoluted Tubule
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** The hormone that helps in the reabsorption of water from the latter parts of the tubule is:
A. Aldosterone
B. Adrenaline
C. Antidiuretic Hormone (ADH)
D. Insulin
**Correct Answer: C**

**8.** The process of releasing urine from the urinary bladder is called:
A. Filtration
B. Reabsorption
C. Secretion
D. Micturition
**Correct Answer: D**

**9.** Birds and reptiles excrete nitrogenous waste primarily in the form of:
A. Ammonia
B. Urea
C. Uric acid
D. Amino acids
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** The glomerular filtrate contains all the constituents of the blood plasma except:
A. Water and glucose
B. Urea and salts
C. Proteins and formed elements
D. Amino acids and vitamins
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** Most of the reabsorption of essential nutrients and water from the glomerular filtrate occurs in the:
A. Loop of Henle
B. Proximal Convoluted Tubule (PCT)
C. Distal Convoluted Tubule (DCT)
D. Collecting duct
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** Animals that excrete urea as their primary nitrogenous waste are called:
A. Ammonotelic
B. Ureotelic
C. Uricotelic
D. Aminotelic
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The glomerulus along with Bowman's capsule is called the:
A. Renal corpuscle
B. Malpighian body
C. Both A and B
D. Loop of Henle
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The accumulation of urea in the blood due to kidney malfunction is known as:
A. Uremia
B. Anuria
C. Glycosuria
D. Ketonuria
**Correct Answer: A**

**15.** The excretory organs in insects, like the cockroach, are the:
A. Kidneys
B. Nephridia
C. Malpighian tubules
D. Flame cells
**Correct Answer: C**

**16.** The presence of glucose in the urine is known as:
A. Ketonuria
B. Uremia
C. Glycosuria
D. Polyuria
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The tube that carries urine from the kidney to the urinary bladder is the:
A. Urethra
B. Ureter
C. Renal vein
D. Collecting duct
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The excretory structures in flatworms (Platyhelminthes) are:
A. Nephridia
B. Malpighian tubules
C. Kidneys
D. Flame cells (Protonephridia)
**Correct Answer: D**

**19.** The normal pH of human urine is slightly:
A. Acidic (around 6.0)
B. Basic (around 8.0)
C. Neutral (7.0)
D. Highly acidic (around 2.0)
**Correct Answer: A**

**20.** Sweat produced by the sweat glands contains water, NaCl, small amounts of urea, and:
A. Uric acid
B. Lactic acid
C. Amino acids
D. Glucose
**Correct Answer: B**

#### Medium

**21.** The glomerular filtration rate (GFR) in a healthy individual is approximately:
A. 125 ml/minute or 180 L/day
B. 125 L/day
C. 180 ml/minute
D. 500 ml/minute
**Correct Answer: A**

**22.** The counter-current mechanism in the kidney helps to:
A. Filter the blood in the glomerulus
B. Reabsorb glucose and amino acids
C. Secrete ions into the filtrate
D. Concentrate the urine in the collecting ducts
**Correct Answer: D**

**23.** The hormone ADH (Antidiuretic Hormone) is secreted by the:
A. Adrenal cortex
B. Adrenal medulla
C. Anterior pituitary
D. Posterior pituitary (neurohypophysis)
**Correct Answer: D**

**24.** The juxtaglomerular apparatus (JGA) is a special sensitive region formed by the cellular modifications in the:
A. Proximal convoluted tubule and the afferent arteriole
B. Distal convoluted tubule and the afferent arteriole
C. Loop of Henle and the efferent arteriole
D. Collecting duct and the efferent arteriole
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** A fall in the glomerular filtration rate (GFR) can activate the JG cells to release:
A. Aldosterone
B. ADH
C. Renin
D. ANF
**Correct Answer: C**

**26.** Aldosterone is a hormone that causes the reabsorption of Na⁺ and water from the:
A. Proximal parts of the tubule
B. Distal parts of the tubule
C. Descending limb of Henle's loop
D. Ascending limb of Henle's loop
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** The ascending limb of the loop of Henle is impermeable to water but allows the transport of:
A. Glucose
B. Amino acids
C. Electrolytes (like NaCl)
D. Urea
**Correct Answer: C**

**28.** The hormone that acts as a check on the renin-angiotensin mechanism and causes vasodilation is:
A. ADH
B. Aldosterone
C. Atrial Natriuretic Factor (ANF)
D. Adrenaline
**Correct Answer: C**

**29.** The condition of the formation of insoluble masses of crystallized salts (stones) within the kidney is called:
A. Glomerulonephritis
B. Renal calculi
C. Uremia
D. Pyelonephritis
**Correct Answer: B**

**30.** Micturition is a reflex process, but it is under some voluntary control from the:
A. Medulla oblongata
B. Cerebellum
C. Cerebrum
D. Pons
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** In haemodialysis, the dialysing fluid has the same composition as the plasma except for the:
A. Glucose
B. Amino acids
C. Nitrogenous wastes (like urea)
D. Water and salts
**Correct Answer: C**

**32.** The vasa recta is a U-shaped minute vessel of the peritubular capillary network that runs parallel to the:
A. PCT
B. DCT
C. Loop of Henle
D. Collecting duct
**Correct Answer: C**

**33.** Which of the following is correct regarding the human kidney?
A. The cortex is the inner part, and the medulla is the outer part.
B. The medulla is divided into a few conical masses called medullary pyramids.
C. The glomerulus is a part of the renal tubule.
D. Bowman's capsule opens into the loop of Henle.
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** An increase in blood flow to the atria of the heart can cause the release of ANF, which in turn:
A. Increases blood pressure
B. Decreases blood pressure
C. Increases GFR
D. Causes vasoconstriction
**Correct Answer: B**

**35.** The part of the nephron that is primarily responsible for the conditional reabsorption of Na⁺ and water is the:
A. PCT
B. Loop of Henle
C. DCT
D. Bowman's capsule
**Correct Answer: C**

**36.** The excretory product that requires the maximum amount of water for its elimination is:
A. Urea
B. Uric acid
C. Ammonia
D. Creatine
**Correct Answer: C**

**37.** The podocytes are specialized cells found in the:
A. Afferent arteriole
B. Visceral layer of Bowman's capsule
C. Parietal layer of Bowman's capsule
D. Distal convoluted tubule
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The primary function of the Loop of Henle is:
A. Reabsorption of glucose
B. Secretion of H⁺ and K⁺ ions
C. Reabsorption of water and NaCl
D. Creating a concentration gradient in the medullary interstitium
**Correct Answer: D**

**39.** The lungs, liver, and skin also play a role in excretion. The liver secretes substances like bilirubin and biliverdin in the:
A. Urine
B. Sweat
C. Saliva
D. Bile
**Correct Answer: D**

**40.** The effective filtration pressure in the glomerulus is the net pressure that favors filtration. It is given by:
A. Glomerular Hydrostatic Pressure (GHP) only
B. GHP - (Blood Colloid Osmotic Pressure + Capsular Hydrostatic Pressure)
C. GHP + Blood Colloid Osmotic Pressure - Capsular Hydrostatic Pressure
D. Blood Colloid Osmotic Pressure - GHP
**Correct Answer: B**
