#### Hard

**41.** The correct sequence of the parts of a nephron is:
A. Bowman's capsule → DCT → Loop of Henle → PCT → Collecting Duct
B. Bowman's capsule → Loop of Henle → PCT → DCT → Collecting Duct
C. Bowman's capsule → PCT → Loop of Henle → DCT → Collecting Duct
D. PCT → Bowman's capsule → Loop of Henle → DCT → Collecting Duct
**Correct Answer: C**

**42.** The renin-angiotensin-aldosterone system (RAAS) is triggered by a fall in GFR/glomerular blood pressure. The correct sequence of events is:
A. Renin → Angiotensinogen → Angiotensin I → Angiotensin II → Aldosterone secretion
B. Angiotensinogen → Renin → Angiotensin I → Angiotensin II → Aldosterone secretion
C. Renin → Angiotensin I → Angiotensin II → Angiotensinogen → Aldosterone secretion
D. Aldosterone → Renin → Angiotensinogen → Angiotensin I → Angiotensin II
**Correct Answer: B**

**43.** If the loop of Henle were absent from the mammalian nephron, which of the following would be the expected result?
A. The urine would be more concentrated.
B. The urine would be more dilute.
C. There would be no urine formation.
D. There would be no change in the urine concentration.
**Correct Answer: B**

**44.** Diabetes insipidus is a condition caused by the hyposecretion of ADH. It is characterized by:
A. Excretion of glucose in the urine
B. Excretion of large volumes of dilute urine (polyuria)
C. High blood sugar levels
D. Presence of ketone bodies in the urine
**Correct Answer: B**

**4\<strong\>5\</strong\>.** The osmolarity of the filtrate at the bottom of the loop of Henle in the inner medulla is approximately:
A. 300 mOsmol/L
B. 600 mOsmol/L
C. 900 mOsmol/L
D. 1200 mOsmol/L
**Correct Answer: D**

**46.** Tubular secretion is an important step in urine formation because it helps in:
A. Maintaining the ionic and acid-base balance of body fluids
B. Removing foreign substances and drugs from the blood
C. Both A and B
D. Reabsorbing useful substances like glucose
**Correct Answer: C**

**47.** Which of the following is correct with respect to the permeability of the different parts of the Loop of Henle?
A. Descending limb is permeable to electrolytes, ascending limb is permeable to water.
B. Descending limb is impermeable to water, ascending limb is permeable to water.
C. Descending limb is permeable to water, ascending limb is impermeable to water.
D. Both limbs are permeable to both water and electrolytes.
**Correct Answer: C**

**48.** The primary function of Angiotensin II is to:
A. Act as a powerful vasoconstrictor, increasing blood pressure
B. Activate the adrenal cortex to release aldosterone
C. Increase the glomerular filtration rate
D. Both A and B
**Correct Answer: D**

**49.** On average, an adult human excretes about 1 to 1.5 liters of urine per day. Out of the 180 L of filtrate formed per day, this represents a reabsorption of over:
A. 50%
B. 75%
C. 90%
D. 99%
**Correct Answer: D**

**50.** The presence of blood cells in the urine, known as hematuria, is an indication of damage to the:
A. Loop of Henle
B. PCT
C. Filtration membrane in the glomerulus
D. Collecting duct
**Correct Answer: C**

&& Locomotion and Movement

#### Easy

**1.** The type of movement exhibited by macrophages and leucocytes in the blood is:
A. Ciliary movement
B. Flagellar movement
C. Muscular movement
D. Amoeboid movement
**Correct Answer: D**

**2.** The contractile property of muscles allows for:
A. Locomotion and movement
B. Circulation of blood
C. Digestion of food
D. Excretion of waste
**Correct Answer: A**

**3.** Which of the following is a type of muscle tissue?
A. Skeletal
B. Smooth
C. Cardiac
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**4.** The muscle fibres that are voluntary, striated, and attached to the skeleton are:
A. Smooth muscles
B. Cardiac muscles
C. Skeletal muscles
D. Visceral muscles
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** The basic functional unit of a muscle fiber is the:
A. Sarcomere
B. Myofibril
C. Fascicle
D. Sarcoplasm
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** The thick filament in a sarcomere is composed of the protein:
A. Actin
B. Myosin
C. Troponin
D. Tropomyosin
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** The thin filament in a sarcomere is composed primarily of the protein:
A. Myosin
B. Actin
C. Myoglobin
D. Fibrin
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The human skeleton is broadly divided into the axial skeleton and the:
A. Appendicular skeleton
B. Vertebral skeleton
C. Cranial skeleton
D. Pectoral skeleton
**Correct Answer: A**

**9.** The skull, vertebral column, sternum, and ribs constitute the:
A. Appendicular skeleton
B. Axial skeleton
C. Pectoral girdle
D. Pelvic girdle
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** The number of vertebrae in the human vertebral column is:
A. 12
B. 26
C. 33
D. 7
**Correct Answer: B**
*(Note: 26 in adults as some fuse, 33 in children)*

**11.** Joints are points of contact between:
A. Bones
B. Bones and cartilages
C. Muscles and bones
D. Both A and B
**Correct Answer: D**

**12.** The joint that allows no movement is called a:
A. Fibrous joint
B. Cartilaginous joint
C. Synovial joint
D. Ball and socket joint
**Correct Answer: A**

**13.** The ball and socket joint, which allows for movement in many planes, is found in the:
A. Knee
B. Elbow
C. Shoulder
D. Ankle
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The accumulation of uric acid crystals in the joints causes an inflammation known as:
A. Arthritis
B. Osteoporosis
C. Gout
D. Muscular dystrophy
**Correct Answer: C**

**15.** The number of ribs in a normal human is:
A. 10 pairs
B. 12 pairs
C. 14 pairs
D. 7 pairs
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The bones of the limbs along with their girdles constitute the:
A. Axial skeleton
B. Appendicular skeleton
C. Vertebral column
D. Skull
**Correct Answer: B**

**17.** The red colour of skeletal muscle fibers is due to the pigment:
A. Haemoglobin
B. Myoglobin
C. Melanin
D. Cytochrome
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The central part of the thick filament which is not overlapped by thin filaments is called the:
A. A-band
B. I-band
C. H-zone
D. Z-line
**Correct Answer: C**

**19.** The largest bone in the human body is the:
A. Humerus
B. Tibia
C. Femur
D. Sternum
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** The joint between the atlas and axis vertebrae is a:
A. Hinge joint
B. Pivot joint
C. Saddle joint
D. Gliding joint
**Correct Answer: B**

**31.** The type of joint found at the knee is a:
A. Ball and socket joint
B. Hinge joint

**32.** The 'floating ribs' are the last two pairs (11th and 12th) because they are:
A. Not connected to the sternum at all

C. Connected directly to the sternum
D. Made of cartilage only

**33.** Tetany is a condition of rapid spasms in muscles due to:
A. Low Ca²⁺ in body fluids
B. High Ca²⁺ in body fluids
C. High uric acid levels

**34.** Each half of the pelvic girdle is made of three fused bones: ilium, ischium, and:
A. Femur
B. Sacrum

**36.** The number of bones in each human limb is:
A. 25
B. 30
C. 35
D. 20
**Correct Answer: B**

**37.** The G-actin (globular actin) polymerizes to form F-actin (filamentous actin). Two F-actins helically wind to form the backbone of the:
A. Thin filament
B. Thick filament
C. Z-line
D. M-line

**38.** Osteoporosis is an age-related disease characterized by:
A. Inflammation of joints
B. Increased bone mass and chance of fractures
C. Decreased bone mass and increased chance of fractures
D. Accumulation of uric acid

A. Troponin
B. Tropomyosin
C. Meromyosin
D. Calmodulin

**40.** A motor unit consists of:
A. A motor neuron and all the muscle fibers it innervates

#### Hard

**41.** The H-zone in the skeletal muscle fibre is due to:
A. The central gap between actin filaments extending through myosin filaments in the A-band.
B. Extension of myosin filaments in the central portion of the A-band.
C. The absence of myofibrils in the central portion of the A-band.
D. The central gap between myosin filaments in the A-band.
**Correct Answer: A**

**42.** The correct sequence of events in a muscle contraction is:
(i) Release of Ca²⁺ from the sarcoplasmic reticulum
(ii) An action potential arrives at the neuromuscular junction
(iii) Binding of myosin head to exposed active sites on actin
(iv) Release of acetylcholine
(v) Unmasking of active sites on actin by troponin
A. (ii) → (iv) → (i) → (v) → (iii)
B. (i) → (ii) → (iv) → (iii) → (v)
C. (ii) → (i) → (iv) → (v) → (iii)
D. (iv) → (ii) → (v) → (i) → (iii)
**Correct Answer: A**

**43.** The glenoid cavity is a depression found in the:
A. Pelvic girdle that articulates with the femur
B. Pectoral girdle that articulates with the humerus
C. Skull that articulates with the atlas
D. Humerus that articulates with the ulna
**Correct Answer: B**

**44.** Which of the following is a correct statement?
A. Red muscle fibers are rich in myoglobin and mitochondria.
B. White muscle fibers depend on anaerobic processes for energy.
C. Red muscle fibers are also called aerobic muscles.
D. All of the above are correct.
**Correct Answer: D**

**45.** The joint between the carpal and metacarpal of the thumb is an example of a:
A. Hinge joint
B. Gliding joint
C. Pivot joint
D. Saddle joint
**Correct Answer: D**

**46.** During muscle contraction, the energy from ATP hydrolysis is used for:
A. The binding of the myosin head to actin
B. The power stroke, where the myosin head pivots and pulls the actin filament
C. The detachment of the myosin head from actin
D. Both B and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**47.** The total number of bones in the human axial skeleton is:
A. 126
B. 80
C. 206
D. 60
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** A person suffering from muscular dystrophy, a genetic disorder, experiences:
A. Progressive degeneration of skeletal muscle
B. Inflammation of the joints
C. Weakening of the bones
D. Autoimmune destruction of neuromuscular junctions
**Correct Answer: A**

**49.** The acromion process is a part of the:
A. Clavicle
B. Scapula
C. Humerus
D. Sternum
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** A single muscle twitch involves three phases in the correct order:
A. Latent period, Contraction phase, Relaxation phase
B. Contraction phase, Latent period, Relaxation phase
C. Latent period, Relaxation phase, Contraction phase
D. Relaxation phase, Contraction phase, Latent period
**Correct Answer: A**

&& Neural Control and Coordination

#### Easy

**1.** The structural and functional unit of the nervous system is the:
A. Nephron
B. Neuron
C. Sarcomere
D. Osteon
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The central nervous system (CNS) in humans consists of the brain and the:
A. Nerves
B. Ganglia
C. Spinal cord
D. Cranial nerves
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** The part of the neuron that receives signals from other neurons is the:
A. Axon
B. Cell body (Cyton)
C. Dendrite
D. Myelin sheath
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** The junction between two neurons, through which a nerve impulse passes, is called a:
A. Synapse
B. Joint
C. Neuromuscular junction
D. Receptor
**Correct Answer: A**

**5.** The largest part of the human brain, responsible for intelligence and memory, is the:
A. Cerebellum
B. Cerebrum
C. Medulla oblongata
D. Pons
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The brain and spinal cord are protected by three layers of membranes called:
A. Pleura
B. Pericardium
C. Meninges
D. Peritoneum
**Correct Answer: C**

**7.** The gap between two adjacent myelin sheaths on an axon is known as the:
A. Synaptic cleft
B. Node of Ranvier
C. Axon terminal
D. Schwann cell
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The part of the brain that controls balance, posture, and coordination is the:
A. Cerebrum
B. Cerebellum
C. Thalamus
D. Hypothalamus
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** A rapid, involuntary response to a stimulus that occurs without conscious thought is called a:
A. Reflex action
B. Voluntary action
C. Hormonal action
D. Synaptic transmission
**Correct Answer: A**

**10.** The light-sensitive layer at the back of the eye that contains photoreceptor cells is the:
A. Cornea
B. Lens
C. Sclera
D. Retina
**Correct Answer: D**

**11.** The photoreceptor cells responsible for daylight (photopic) vision and colour vision are the:
A. Rods
B. Cones
C. Bipolar cells
D. Ganglion cells
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** The part of the human ear responsible for hearing is the:
A. Cochlea
B. Vestibular apparatus
C. Eustachian tube
D. Tympanic membrane
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** The chemicals that are released from the axon terminal to transmit a nerve impulse across a synapse are called:
A. Hormones
B. Enzymes
C. Neurotransmitters
D. Pheromones
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The peripheral nervous system (PNS) consists of:
A. The brain only
B. The spinal cord only
C. The brain and spinal cord
D. All the nerves of the body associated with the CNS
**Correct Answer: D**

**15.** The tough, outermost layer of the meninges is the:
A. Pia mater
B. Arachnoid mater
C. Dura mater
D. Choroid
**Correct Answer: C**

**16.** The electrical potential difference across the resting neural membrane is called the:
A. Action potential
B. Resting potential
C. Graded potential
D. Threshold potential
**Correct Answer: B**

**17.** The fluid-filled space between the lens and the retina of the eye is the:
A. Aqueous humour
B. Vitreous humour
C. Perilymph
D. Endolymph
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The auditory receptors in the cochlea are located on the:
A. Reissner's membrane
B. Basilar membrane
C. Tectorial membrane
D. Tympanic membrane
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** The somatic neural system relays impulses from the CNS to:
A. Involuntary organs
B. Smooth muscles
C. Skeletal muscles
D. Cardiac muscles
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** The part of the human hindbrain that controls involuntary actions like breathing and heartbeat is the:
A. Cerebellum
B. Pons
C. Medulla oblongata
D. Thalamus
**Correct Answer: C**

**21.** During the conduction of a nerve impulse, the depolarisation of the axon membrane occurs due to the:

A. Incus, Malleus, Stapes
B. Malleus, Incus, Stapes
C. Stapes, Incus, Malleus
D. Malleus, Stapes, Incus

A. Body temperature, urge for eating, and drinking

D. Respiration and cardiovascular reflexes

A. Influx of Na⁺ ions

A. Cerebellum
B. Medulla oblongata
C. Corpus callosum

A. Red, yellow, and blue

**32.** The Eustachian tube connects the middle ear cavity with the:
A. Inner ear
B. External ear
C. Pharynx
D. Larynx

**33.** Which part of the human ear plays no role in hearing but is otherwise very much required?
A. Ear ossicles

A. Electrical currents

**35.** The cerebral cortex is referred to as the grey matter due to the high concentration of:

**36.** The fovea, the point of most acute vision in the retina, contains:
A. Only rods
B. Only cones
C. Both rods and cones
D. No photoreceptor cells

**37.** The cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) is found in the:
A. Space between the dura mater and arachnoid mater
B. Ventricles of the brain and the subarachnoid space
C. Middle ear
D. Vitreous chamber of the eye
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The sensory part of the saccule and utricle, the macula, is responsible for sensing:
A. Hearing
B. Rotational movements
C. Static equilibrium and linear acceleration
D. Taste
**Correct Answer: C**

**39.** The sodium-potassium pump is an example of active transport because it:
A. Moves Na⁺ and K⁺ down their concentration gradients
B. Requires ATP to move Na⁺ and K⁺ against their concentration gradients

**42.** The correct sequence of the layers of the retina from the outside (choroid side) to the inside is:

D. All of the above

B. More permeable to K⁺ ions and nearly impermeable to Na⁺ ions
C. Equally permeable to both Na⁺ and K⁺ ions
D. Impermeable to both Na⁺ and K⁺ ions

A. Static equilibrium

A. Retinal and Opsin

B. More permeable to Na⁺ ions, causing depolarisation
C. Less permeable to Na⁺ ions
D. More permeable to Cl⁻ ions

A. Polysynaptic
B. Monosynaptic

C. Pons
D. Corpus callosum

A. A stimulus will either produce a full-sized action potential or no action potential at all.
B. All stimuli will produce an action potential.
C. The size of the action potential is proportional to the strength of the stimulus.
D. The neuron can fire impulses of varying sizes.
**Correct Answer: A**

&& Chemical Coordination and Integration

#### Easy

**1.** The glands that lack ducts and release their secretions directly into the bloodstream are called:
A. Exocrine glands
B. Endocrine glands
C. Salivary glands
D. Sebaceous glands
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The chemical messengers produced by endocrine glands are known as:
A. Enzymes
B. Vitamins
C. Hormones
D. Neurotransmitters
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** The hypothalamus is a part of the:
A. Forebrain
B. Midbrain
C. Hindbrain
D. Spinal cord
**Correct Answer: A**

**4.** The pituitary gland is located in a bony cavity called the:
A. Foramen magnum
B. Acetabulum
C. Glenoid cavity
D. Sella turcica
**Correct Answer: D**

**5.** Which of the following is known as the 'master endocrine gland'?
A. Thyroid gland
B. Adrenal gland
C. Pituitary gland
D. Pineal gland
**Correct Answer: C**

**6.** The hormone responsible for the regulation of the 24-hour (diurnal) rhythm of our body is:
A. Thyroxine
B. Melatonin
C. Adrenaline
D. Cortisol
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** The thyroid gland is composed of two lobes located on either side of the:
A. Oesophagus
B. Trachea
C. Larynx
D. Sternum
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The deficiency of iodine in our diet results in hypothyroidism and the enlargement of the thyroid gland, commonly called:
A. Goitre
B. Acromegaly
C. Cushing's syndrome
D. Addison's disease
**Correct Answer: A**

**9.** The hormone that regulates the blood calcium levels is secreted by the parathyroid gland and is called:
A. Thyroxine
B. Calcitonin
C. Parathyroid hormone (PTH)
D. Thymosin
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** The adrenal glands are located on the top of the:
A. Kidneys
B. Liver
C. Pancreas
D. Lungs
**Correct Answer: A**

**11.** The hormones secreted by the adrenal medulla during stress or emergency situations are adrenaline and:
A. Noradrenaline
B. Cortisol
C. Aldosterone
D. Insulin
**Correct Answer: A**

**12.** The pancreas is a composite gland that acts as both an endocrine and an:
A. Exocrine gland
B. Salivary gland
C. Sebaceous gland
D. Lymphatic gland
**Correct Answer: A**

**13.** The hormone insulin, which regulates blood glucose levels, is secreted by the:
A. Alpha-cells of the pancreas
B. Beta-cells of the pancreas
C. Delta-cells of the pancreas
D. Adrenal cortex
**Correct Answer: B**

**14.** The male sex hormone, testosterone, is secreted by the:
A. Ovaries
B. Adrenal gland
C. Pituitary gland
D. Testes
**Correct Answer: D**

**15.** The female sex hormone, estrogen, is secreted by the:
A. Testes
B. Ovaries
C. Placenta
D. Thyroid gland
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** Which of the following is not an endocrine gland?
A. Thyroid
B. Pituitary
C. Spleen
D. Adrenal
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The hormone responsible for ovulation and the maintenance of the corpus luteum is:
A. Follicle-Stimulating Hormone (FSH)
B. Luteinizing Hormone (LH)
C. Prolactin
D. Oxytocin
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The hormone that stimulates the synthesis and secretion of glucocorticoids from the adrenal cortex is:
A. TSH
B. ACTH
C. GH
D. FSH
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** The thymus gland secretes the hormone thymosin, which plays a major role in the differentiation of:
A. B-lymphocytes
B. T-lymphocytes
C. Red blood cells
D. Platelets
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** Glucagon is a hormone secreted by the pancreas that:
A. Lowers blood glucose levels

C. Stimulates the secretion of insulin
D. Promotes the synthesis of glycogen
**Correct Answer: B**

***

&& Sexual Reproduction in Flowering Plants

#### Easy

**1.** A typical angiosperm anther is:
A. Monothecous and bisporangiate
B. Dithecous and tetrasporangiate
C. Dithecous and bisporangiate
D. Monothecous and tetrasporangiate
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The outer protective layer of a pollen grain, made of sporopollenin, is the:
A. Intine
B. Exine
C. Germ pore
D. Generative cell
**Correct Answer: B**

**3. The female reproductive part of a flower is the pistil, which is also known as the:**
A. Androecium
B. Gynoecium
C. Corolla
D. Calyx
**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** The ovule is attached to the placenta by a stalk called the:
A. Hilum
B. Funicle
C. Micropyle
D. Chalaza
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The process of transfer of pollen grains from the anther to the stigma of a flower is called:
A. Fertilization
B. Pollination
C. Germination
D. Apomixis
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The fusion of male and female gametes is termed:
A. Pollination
B. Syngamy
C. Embryogenesis
D. Parthenogenesis
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** Double fertilization is a characteristic feature of:
A. Algae
B. Fungi
C. Gymnosperms
D. Angiosperms
**Correct Answer: D**

**8.** The primary endosperm nucleus (PEN) in angiosperms is formed by the fusion of a male gamete with the:
A. Egg cell
B. Synergids
C. Antipodal cells
D. Central cell (polar nuclei)
**Correct Answer: D**

**9.** After fertilization, the ovary develops into the:
A. Seed
B. Fruit
C. Embryo
D. Endosperm
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** A fruit that develops without fertilization is called a:
A. True fruit
B. False fruit
C. Parthenocarpic fruit
D. Aggregate fruit
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** The outermost protective layer of the ovule is the:
A. Nucellus
B. Embryo sac
C. Integument
D. Chalaza
**Correct Answer: C**

**12.** Pollination by wind is known as:
A. Hydrophily
B. Entomophily
C. Anemophily
D. Ornithophily
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** The part of the pistil that serves as a landing platform for pollen grains is the:
A. Style
B. Ovary
C. Stigma
D. Ovule
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The generative cell in a pollen grain divides to form:
A. One male gamete
B. Two male gametes
C. Three male gametes
D. The pollen tube
**Correct Answer: B**

**15.** The endosperm in most angiosperms is:
A. Haploid (n)
B. Diploid (2n)
C. Triploid (3n)
D. Tetraploid (4n)
**Correct Answer: C**

**16.** The transfer of pollen grains from the anther to the stigma of the same flower is called:
A. Geitonogamy
B. Xenogamy
C. Autogamy
D. Allogamy
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The hard outer layer of the seed coat is the:
A. Tegmen
B. Testa
C. Hilum
D. Micropyle
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The filiform apparatus is a characteristic feature of:
A. Egg cell
B. Synergids
C. Antipodal cells
D. Central cell
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** An example of a plant that shows pollination by water (hydrophily) is:
A. Rose
B. Maize
C. *Vallisneria*
D. Sunflower
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** The scutellum in a maize grain is the:
A. Endosperm
B. Embryo
C. Cotyledon
D. Protective sheath
**Correct Answer: C**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The production of seeds without fertilization is called:
A. Parthenocarpy
B. Apomixis
C. Polyembryony
D. Somatic hybridization
**Correct Answer: B**

**22.** In a typical mature embryo sac of an angiosperm, the arrangement of cells is:
A. 3-celled egg apparatus, 1 central cell, 3 antipodal cells
B. 2-celled egg apparatus, 1 central cell, 3 antipodal cells
C. 3-celled egg apparatus, 2 central cells, 2 antipodal cells
D. 2-celled egg apparatus, 2 central cells, 2 antipodal cells
**Correct Answer: A**

**23.** The transfer of pollen grains from the anther to the stigma of another flower of the same plant is called:
A. Autogamy
B. Geitonogamy
C. Xenogamy
D. Chasmogamy
**Correct Answer: B**

**24.** The innermost wall layer of a microsporangium, which provides nourishment to the developing pollen grains, is the:
A. Epidermis
B. Endothecium
C. Middle layers
D. Tapetum
**Correct Answer: D**

**25.** The phenomenon of the occurrence of more than one embryo in a seed is referred to as:
A. Polyembryony
B. Parthenocarpy
C. Apomixis
D. Adventive embryony
**Correct Answer: A**

**26.** Which of the following is a device for promoting cross-pollination?
A. Cleistogamy
B. Homogamy
C. Dichogamy
D. Bisexuality
**Correct Answer: C**

**27.** The flowers of *Vallisneria* are pollinated by water. The female flower reaches the surface of the water by a long stalk and:
A. The male flowers are released onto the surface of the water
B. The pollen grains are released inside the water
C. Insects carry the pollen to the female flower
D. The flowers are self-pollinated
**Correct Answer: A**

**28.** The function of the filiform apparatus is to:
A. Guide the entry of the pollen tube into the synergid
B. Produce nectar
C. Protect the embryo sac
D. Nourish the egg cell
**Correct Answer: A**

**29.** An example of a seed with a perisperm (persistent nucellus) is:
A. Pea
B. Groundnut
C. Black pepper
D. Maize
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** A dioecious flowering plant prevents:
A. Autogamy but not geitonogamy
B. Geitonogamy but not autogamy
C. Both autogamy and geitonogamy
D. Neither autogamy nor geitonogamy
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** The process of the formation of microspores from a pollen mother cell (PMC) through meiosis is called:
A. Megasporogenesis
B. Microsporogenesis
C. Gametogenesis
D. Embryogenesis
**Correct Answer: B**

**32.** In an angiosperm, the number of chromosomes in the endosperm is 30. The number of chromosomes in the gametes would be:
A. 10
B. 15
C. 30
D. 45
**Correct Answer: A**

**33.** The events of double fertilization involve the fusion of one male gamete with the egg cell and the other male gamete with the:
A. Synergids
B. Antipodal cells
C. Nucellus
D. Central cell
**Correct Answer: D**

**34.** A mature pollen grain (at the time of shedding in most angiosperms) is:
A. 1-celled
B. 2-celled (vegetative and generative cell)
C. 3-celled (one vegetative cell and two male gametes)
D. 4-celled
**Correct Answer: B**

**35.** The viability of pollen grains depends on:
A. Temperature
B. Humidity
C. The plant species
D. Both A and B
**Correct Answer: D**

**36.** The ovule of an angiosperm is technically equivalent to a:
A. Megasporangium
B. Megaspore
C. Female gametophyte
D. Zygote
**Correct Answer: A**

**37.** The coleoptile and coleorhiza are protective sheaths that cover the plumule and radicle, respectively, in a:
A. Dicot seed
B. Monocot seed
C. Gymnosperm seed
D. Pteridophyte spore
**CorrectAnswer: B**

**38.** If a flower is to be pollinated by insects, it must be:
A. Small and inconspicuous
B. Large, colourful, fragrant, and rich in nectar
C. Producing light, non-sticky pollen
D. Having feathery stigmas
**Correct Answer: B**

**39.** The portion of the embryonal axis above the level of the cotyledons is the:
A. Hypocotyl
B. Epicotyl
C. Radicle
D. Coleorhiza
**Correct Answer: B**

**40.** A false fruit is one in which:
A. The fruit develops without fertilization
B. The fruit develops from a single flower
C. The thalamus also contributes to fruit formation
D. The fruit has no seeds
**Correct Answer: C**

#### Hard

**41.** During the development of a monosporic embryo sac from a functional megaspore, the nucleus of the megaspore undergoes:
A. One meiotic division
B. Three mitotic divisions
C. Two mitotic divisions
D. One mitotic and two meiotic divisions
**Correct Answer: B**

**42.** The pollen grains can be preserved as fossils because the exine is made of sporopollenin, which is:
A. A complex carbohydrate
B. A protein that is resistant to enzymatic degradation
C. A highly resistant organic material that can withstand high temperatures and strong acids/alkalis
D. A waxy substance
**Correct Answer: C**

**43.** In a self-incompatibility mechanism, the pollen grain from the same plant is inhibited from germinating on the stigma. This is a genetic mechanism to prevent:
A. Self-pollination (Autogamy)
B. Cross-pollination (Xenogamy)
C. Geitonogamy
D. Both A and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**44.** The correct sequence of the development of a male gametophyte from a microspore mother cell is:
A. MMC (Meiosis) → Microspore tetrad → Pollen grain → Male gametes
B. MMC (Mitosis) → Pollen grain → Microspore tetrad → Male gametes
C. Pollen grain → MMC (Meiosis) → Microspore tetrad → Male gametes
D. MMC (Meiosis) → Male gametes → Pollen grain → Microspore tetrad
**Correct Answer: A**

**45.** In artificial hybridization experiments, the process of removal of anthers from a bisexual flower bud before the anther dehisces is called:
A. Emasculation
B. Bagging
C. Pollination
D. Tagging
**Correct Answer: A**

**46.** The ploidy levels of the nucellus, endosperm, and egg cell in a typical angiosperm are, respectively:
A. 2n, 3n, n
B. n, 2n, 3n
C. 2n, n, 3n
D. n, 3n, 2n
**Correct Answer: A**

**47.** The coconut water from a tender coconut is the:
A. Cellular endosperm
B. Free-nuclear endosperm
C. Degenerated nucellus
D. Immature embryo
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** The condition of having pistils fused together is called:
A. Apocarpous
B. Syncarpous
C. Epipetalous
D. Syngenesious
**Correct Answer: B**

**49.** If an endosperm cell of an angiosperm has 24 chromosomes, the number of chromosomes in the root cells of the sporophyte would be:
A. 8
B. 16
C. 24
D. 32
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** A plant has flowers, but they never open (cleistogamous). This condition ensures:
A. Cross-pollination
B. A high degree of genetic variability
C. Assured seed-set even in the absence of pollinators
D. Pollination by wind
**Correct Answer: C**

&& Human Reproduction

#### Easy

**1.** The primary male sex organ that produces sperm is the:
A. Prostate gland
B. Seminal vesicle
C. Testis
D. Scrotum
**Correct Answer: C**

**2.** The primary female sex organ that produces ova (eggs) is the:
A. Uterus
B. Vagina
C. Ovary
D. Fallopian tube
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** The process of formation of sperm from spermatogonia is called:
A. Oogenesis
B. Spermatogenesis
C. Gametogenesis
D. Spermiation
**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** The process of formation of a mature female gamete (ovum) is called:
A. Spermatogenesis
B. Oogenesis
C. Menstruation
D. Ovulation
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The monthly cycle of events that occurs in the ovaries and uterus of a human female is the:
A. Cardiac cycle
B. Menstrual cycle
C. Oestrous cycle
D. Cell cycle
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The fusion of a male gamete (sperm) with a female gamete (ovum) is called:
A. Implantation
B. Gestation
C. Parturition
D. Fertilization
**Correct Answer: D**

**7.** The attachment of the blastocyst to the wall of the uterus is known as:
A. Fertilization
B. Implantation
C. Gastrulation
D. Ovulation
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The period of embryonic development inside the uterus is called:
A. Parturition
B. Lactation
C. Gestation
D. Menstruation
**Correct Answer: C**

**9.** The process of childbirth is called:
A. Gestation
B. Implantation
C. Lactation
D. Parturition
**Correct Answer: D**

**10.** The process by which the mammary glands produce milk towards the end of pregnancy is called:
A. Lactation
B. Parturition
C. Menstruation
D. Ovulation
**Correct Answer: A**

**11.** The testes are located outside the abdominal cavity in a pouch called the scrotum because:
A. It provides more space for their growth
B. It protects them from injury
C. It maintains a lower temperature necessary for spermatogenesis
D. It is a secondary sexual characteristic
**Correct Answer: C**

**12.** The path of sperm from the testes to the urethra is through the:
A. Vas deferens, epididymis, ejaculatory duct, rete testis
B. Rete testis, epididymis, vas deferens, ejaculatory duct
C. Epididymis, rete testis, ejaculatory duct, vas deferens
D. Ejaculatory duct, vas deferens, epididymis, rete testis
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The part of the fallopian tube closer to the ovary is the funnel-shaped:
A. Isthmus
B. Ampulla
C. Infundibulum
D. Fimbriae
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The release of an ovum from a mature Graafian follicle is called:
A. Menstruation
B. Fertilization
C. Ovulation
D. Implantation
**Correct Answer: C**

**15.** The onset of the menstrual cycle at puberty is called:
A. Menopause
B. Menarche
C. Ovulation
D. Gestation
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** Fertilization in humans normally occurs in the:
A. Ovary
B. Uterus
C. Vagina
D. Ampullary region of the Fallopian tube
**Correct Answer: D**

**17.** The structure that provides a vascular connection between the foetus and the uterus is the:
A. Amnion
B. Chorion
C. Yolk sac
D. Placenta
**Correct Answer: D**

**18.** The first milk produced by the mother during the initial days of lactation, which is rich in antibodies, is called:
A. Colostrum
B. Sebum
C. Meconium
D. Amniotic fluid
**Correct Answer: A**

**19.** The hormone responsible for the development of male secondary sexual characteristics is:
A. Estrogen
B. Progesterone
C. Testosterone
D. LH
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** Each testis has about 250 compartments called:
A. Seminiferous tubules
B. Rete testis
C. Testicular lobules
D. Epididymis
**Correct Answer: C**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The cells that provide nutrition to the germ cells in the testes are the:
A. Leydig cells
B. Interstitial cells
C. Sertoli cells
D. Spermatogonia
**Correct Answer: C**

**22.** The process of release of sperm from the seminiferous tubules is called:
A. Spermatogenesis
B. Spermiogenesis
C. Spermiation
D. Ejaculation
**Correct Answer: C**

**23.** The hormone that stimulates the Leydig cells to synthesize and secrete androgens is:
A. FSH (Follicle-Stimulating Hormone)
B. LH (Luteinizing Hormone)
C. ACTH
D. Prolactin
**Correct Answer: B**

**24.** The transformation of a spermatid into a spermatozoon (sperm) is called:
A. Spermatogenesis
B. Spermiogenesis
C. Spermiation
D. Meiosis I
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** During oogenesis, a diploid primary oocyte undergoes meiosis I to produce a large haploid secondary oocyte and a tiny:
A. Oogonium
B. Ovum
C. First polar body
D. Second polar body
**Correct Answer: C**

**26.** The phase of the menstrual cycle in which the endometrium regenerates through proliferation is the:
A. Menstrual phase
B. Follicular phase (Proliferative phase)
C. Luteal phase (Secretory phase)
D. Ovulatory phase
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** The corpus luteum is a temporary endocrine gland formed from the remnants of the Graafian follicle after ovulation. It secretes large amounts of:
A. Estrogen
B. Progesterone
C. LH
D. FSH
**Correct Answer: B**

**28.** The acrosome of the sperm is a cap-like structure filled with enzymes that help in:
A. Providing energy for sperm motility
B. Fertilization of the ovum
C. Maturation of the sperm
D. Increasing the sperm count
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** The inner cell mass of the blastocyst develops into the:
A. Trophoblast
B. Placenta
C. Embryo proper
D. Chorion
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** Which of the following is not a function of the placenta?
A. Facilitates the supply of oxygen and nutrients to the embryo
B. Removes carbon dioxide and waste materials from the embryo
C. Acts as an endocrine tissue and produces several hormones
D. Mixes the blood of the mother and the foetus
**Correct Answer: D**

**31.** The first movements of the foetus and the appearance of hair on the head are usually observed during the:
A. Third month
B. Fourth month
C. Fifth month
D. Sixth month
**Correct Answer: C**

**32.** The signal for parturition originates from the fully developed foetus and the placenta, which induces mild uterine contractions called the:
A. Foetal ejection reflex
B. Lactational reflex
C. Withdrawal reflex
D. Startle reflex
**Correct Answer: A**

**33.** The correct sequence of the phases of the menstrual cycle is:
A. Follicular → Luteal → Menstrual → Ovulatory
B. Menstrual → Follicular → Ovulatory → Luteal
C. Luteal → Menstrual → Follicular → Ovulatory
D. Menstrual → Ovulatory → Follicular → Luteal
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** Which of the following hormones is produced by the human placenta?
A. hCG (Human Chorionic Gonadotropin)
B. hPL (Human Placental Lactogen)
C. Estrogens and Progesterone
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**35.** The cessation of the menstrual cycle in females, which usually occurs around 50 years of age, is called:
A. Menarche
B. Menopause
C. Amenorrhea
D. Dysmenorrhea
**Correct Answer: B**

**36.** A human primary spermatocyte contains:
A. 23 chromosomes
B. 46 chromosomes
C. 44 autosomes and XY chromosomes
D. Both B and C are correct
**Correct Answer: D**

**37.** The seminal plasma, the fluid part of semen, is rich in:
A. Fructose, calcium, and certain enzymes
B. Glucose and sodium
C. Proteins and potassium
D. DNA and RNA
**Correct Answer: A**

**38.** The LH surge, a rapid increase in LH level, is responsible for:
A. The beginning of the follicular phase
B. The rupture of the Graafian follicle and ovulation
C. The formation of the corpus albicans
D. The breakdown of the endometrium
**Correct Answer: B**

**39.** The finger-like projections on the edges of the infundibulum that help in the collection of the ovum after ovulation are called:
A. Villi
B. Cilia
C. Flagella
D. Fimbriae
**Correct Answer: D**

**40.** During fertilization, the sperm induces changes in the zona pellucida layer of the ovum that:
A. Help it to enter the ovum
B. Block the entry of additional sperm
C. Provide nutrition to the sperm
D. Dissolve the ovum's membrane
**Correct Answer: B**

#### Hard

**41.** The correct sequence of cell stages in spermatogenesis is:
A. Spermatogonia → Spermatids → Spermatocytes → Spermatozoa
B. Spermatogonia → Spermatocytes → Spermatids → Spermatozoa
C. Spermatocytes → Spermatogonia → Spermatids → Spermatozoa
D. Spermatids → Spermatocytes → Spermatogonia → Spermatozoa
**Correct Answer: B**

**42.** The second meiotic division in the female germ cell (oogenesis) is completed:
A. At the time of birth
B. At puberty
C. After the entry of a sperm into the ovum
D. Before ovulation
**Correct Answer: C**

**43.** The secretion of which of the following two pituitary hormones is controlled by GnRH from the hypothalamus?
A. TSH and ACTH
B. GH and Prolactin
C. ADH and Oxytocin
D. LH and FSH
**Correct Answer: D**

**44.** After implantation, the finger-like projections that appear on the trophoblast are called chorionic villi. They are surrounded by:
A. The uterine tissue and maternal blood
B. The yolk sac
C. The amniotic fluid
D. The endometrium only
**Correct Answer: A**

**45.** In the absence of fertilization, the corpus luteum:
A. Continues to secrete progesterone for a long time
B. Degenerates, leading to the disintegration of the endometrium
C. Is maintained by the hormone hCG
D. Develops into the corpus albicans and then re-forms the Graafian follicle
**Correct Answer: B**

**46.** The embryonic stage that consists of an outer layer (trophoblast) and an inner cell mass is the:
A. Morula
B. Zygote
C. Gastrula
D. Blastocyst
**Correct Answer: D**

**47.** The foetal ejection reflex triggers the release of which hormone from the maternal pituitary?
A. Prolactin
B. Oxytocin
C. Vasopressin
D. LH
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** The heart of the human embryo is formed:
A. After the first month of pregnancy
B. During the fifth month of pregnancy
C. At the end of the second month of pregnancy
D. After the second trimester
**Correct Answer: A**

**49.** The secretions of the male accessory glands (seminal vesicles, prostate, bulbourethral glands) are essential for:
A. Maturation and motility of sperm
B. Providing a fluid medium for sperm transport
C. Lubrication of the penis
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**50.** The three germ layers—ectoderm, endoderm, and mesoderm—are formed during the process of:
A. Cleavage
B. Implantation
C. Gastrulation
D. Neurulation
**Correct Answer: C**

&& Reproductive Health

#### Easy

**1.** According to the World Health Organization (WHO), reproductive health means total well-being in all aspects of reproduction, i.e., physical, emotional, behavioural, and:
A. Financial
B. Social
C. Educational
D. Political
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The family planning programmes in India were initiated in the year:
A. 1947
B. 1951
C. 1971
D. 1985
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** Which of the following is a natural method of contraception?
A. Condoms
B. Diaphragms
C. Periodic abstinence (Rhythm method)
D. Oral contraceptive pills
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** Condoms are a popular method of contraception because they:
A. Are easily available and effective
B. Are reusable
C. Protect against STDs and AIDS
D. Both A and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**5.** Oral contraceptive pills for females contain a combination of:
A. Progestogens and estrogens
B. Only progestogens
C. Only estrogens
D. Either A or B
**Correct Answer: D**

**6.** The surgical method of contraception in males, which involves cutting and tying the vas deferens, is called:
A. Tubectomy
B. Vasectomy
C. Oophorectomy
D. Hysterectomy
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** The surgical method of contraception in females, which involves cutting and tying the fallopian tubes, is called:
A. Vasectomy
B. Tubectomy
C. Castration
D. Abortion
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The intentional or voluntary termination of pregnancy before full term is called:
A. Medical Termination of Pregnancy (MTP) or induced abortion
B. Spontaneous abortion or miscarriage
C. Parturition
D. Implantation
**Correct Answer: A**

**9.** Which of the following is a sexually transmitted disease (STD)?
A. Cancer
B. AIDS
C. Typhoid
D. Cholera
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** Infertility is the inability to conceive or produce children even after:
A. 6 months of unprotected sexual cohabitation
B. 1 year of unprotected sexual cohabitation
C. 2 years of unprotected sexual cohabitation
D. 5 years of unprotected sexual cohabitation
**Correct Answer: C**
*(Note: Many sources define it as 1 year, but NCERT often uses 2 years, making it the more likely exam answer.)*

**11.** In Vitro Fertilization (IVF) is a technique in which:
A. Fertilization occurs inside the female's body
B. Fertilization occurs outside the body in a laboratory
C. A zygote is directly implanted into the uterus
D. Sperm is directly injected into the ovum
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** An Intra-Uterine Device (IUD) is inserted into the:
A. Vagina
B. Cervix
C. Uterus
D. Fallopian tube
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** The full form of AIDS is:
A. Acquired Immunodeficiency Syndrome
B. Acquired Immune Disease Syndrome
C. Acute Immunodeficiency Syndrome
D. Acquired Infectious Disease Syndrome
**Correct Answer: A**

**14.** A popular brand of condom for males in India is:
A. Saheli
B. Mala-D
C. Nirodh
D. Copper-T
**Correct Answer: C**

**15.** The 'Saheli' pill is a 'once a week' oral contraceptive that:
A. Contains a high dose of estrogen
B. Contains a non-steroidal preparation
C. Has many side effects
D. Is for males
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The RCH programmes stand for:
A. Reproductive and Child Healthcare
B. Regional and Community Health
C. Research in Child Health
D. Rural and City Health
**Correct Answer: A**

**17.** The withdrawal or coitus interruptus method involves the withdrawal of the penis from the vagina:
A. After ejaculation
B. Just before ejaculation
C. During ovulation
D. After fertilization
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The natural method of contraception, lactational amenorrhea, is effective only up to a maximum period of:
A. 3 months after parturition
B. 6 months after parturition
C. 9 months after parturition
D. 1 year after parturition
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** Diaphragms, cervical caps, and vaults are examples of:
A. Natural methods
B. Barrier methods
C. IUDs
D. Surgical methods
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** Which of the following STDs is not completely curable?
A. Syphilis
B. Gonorrhoea
C. Genital herpes
D. Chlamydiosis
**Correct Answer: C**

#### Medium

**21.** The function of copper ions in copper-releasing IUDs (like CuT, Cu7) is to:
A. Inhibit ovulation
B. Suppress sperm motility and fertilizing capacity
C. Make the uterus unsuitable for implantation
D. Thicken the cervical mucus
**Correct Answer: B**

**22.** Amniocentesis is a foetal sex determination test based on the chromosomal pattern in the amniotic fluid. It is banned in India because:
A. It is a risky procedure
B. It can cause genetic disorders
C. It is used for female foeticide
D. It is not a reliable test
**Correct Answer: C**

**23.** The transfer of an embryo with up to 8 blastomeres into the fallopian tube is called:
A. ZIFT (Zygote Intra Fallopian Transfer)
B. IUT (Intra Uterine Transfer)
C. GIFT (Gamete Intra Fallopian Transfer)
D. ICSI (Intra Cytoplasmic Sperm Injection)
**Correct Answer: A**

**24.** Oral contraceptive pills work by:
A. Killing the sperm
B. Blocking the fallopian tubes
C. Inhibiting ovulation and implantation
D. Preventing the entry of sperm through the cervix
**Correct Answer: C**

**25.** The assisted reproductive technology (ART) in which sperm is directly injected into the ovum is called:
A. ZIFT
B. GIFT
C. ICSI
D. AI
**Correct Answer: C**

**26.** The ideal contraceptive for females who want to delay pregnancy and/or space children is the:
A. Barrier method
B. IUD (Intra-Uterine Device)
C. Periodic abstinence
D. Surgical method
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** MTPs are considered relatively safe during the:
A. First trimester (up to 12 weeks)
B. Second trimester (up to 24 weeks)
C. Third trimester
D. Any time during pregnancy
**Correct Answer: A**

**28.** The technique of Artificial Insemination (AI) is useful for males having:
A. A very high sperm count
B. A very low sperm count or inability to inseminate
C. A blockage in the fallopian tubes
D. An inability to produce ova
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** Which of the following is a hormone-releasing IUD?
A. Lippes loop
B. Multiload 375
C. Progestasert
D. Copper-T
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** The transfer of an ovum collected from a donor into the fallopian tube of another female who cannot produce one but can provide a suitable environment for fertilization is called:
A. ZIFT
B. GIFT
C. IUT
D. ICSI
**Correct Answer: B**

**31.** What is the main cause of the rapid increase in the world's population over the last century?
A. An increase in birth rate
B. A rapid decline in the death rate, maternal mortality rate (MMR), and infant mortality rate (IMR)
C. An increase in the number of marriages
D. A lack of contraceptive methods
**Correct Answer: B**

**32.** The main disadvantage of natural methods of contraception is that:
A. They have high side effects
B. They are not easily available
C. The chances of failure are high
D. They are very expensive
**Correct Answer: C**

**33.** Emergency contraceptives are effective if used within:
A. 72 hours of coitus
B. 72 hours of ovulation
C. 72 hours of menstruation
D. 72 hours of implantation
**Correct Answer: A**

**34.** Which of the following STDs is caused by a bacterium?
A. Genital warts
B. AIDS
C. Syphilis
D. Genital herpes
**Correct Answer: C**

**35.** The transfer of embryos with more than 8 blastomeres into the uterus is called:
A. ZIFT
B. IUT
C. GIFT
D. AI
**Correct Answer: B**

**36.** The best way to prevent the spread of STDs is to:
A. Use oral contraceptives
B. Avoid sexual contact with unknown/multiple partners
C. Use condoms during coitus
D. Both B and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**37.** The statutory ban on amniocentesis for sex determination in India was primarily enacted to:
A. Check the increasing menace of female foeticide
B. Prevent the spread of STDs
C. Encourage the use of contraceptives
D. Reduce the population growth rate
**Correct Answer: A**

**38.** Infertility can be caused by:
A. Physical or congenital diseases
B. Drugs and immunological factors
C. Psychological factors
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**39.** Test tube baby programme employs which one of the following techniques?
A. GIFT
B. ICSI
C. ZIFT
D. IUI
**Correct Answer: C**

**40.** A major task of the RCH programmes is to create awareness among people about:
A. Various reproduction-related aspects
B. The benefits of a small family
C. The prevention of STDs
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

#### Hard

**41.** Which of the following contraceptive methods also protects against STDs?
A. Oral pills
B. IUDs
C. Female condoms
D. Tubectomy
**Correct Answer: C**

**42.** A childless couple can be assisted to have a child through a technique called GIFT. The full form of this technique is:
A. Gamete Internal Fertilisation and Transfer
B. Germ cell Internal Fallopian Transfer
C. Gamete Intra Fallopian Transfer
D. Gamete Inseminated Fallopian Transfer
**Correct Answer: C**

**43.** The function of the 'Saheli' pill is that it:
A. Blocks estrogen receptors in the uterus, preventing the egg from getting implanted.
B. Prevents ovulation by inhibiting LH and FSH secretion.
C. Kills the sperm in the female reproductive tract.
D. Creates a physical barrier for the sperm.
**Correct Answer: A**

**44.** Which of the following STDs can be transmitted from an infected mother to her foetus?
A. Syphilis
B. Hepatitis B
C. HIV
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**45.** Consider the statements given below regarding contraception and answer as directed thereafter:
(i) MTP during the first trimester is generally safe.
(ii) Generally, the chances of conception are nil from day 10 to 17 of the menstrual cycle.
(iii) IUDs like CuT increase phagocytosis of sperms.
(iv) Tubectomy is a terminal method of contraception.
Which of the following two statements are correct?
A. (i), (iii)
B. (i), (iv)
C. (ii), (iv)
D. (iii), (iv)
**Correct Answer: A**

**46.** A major reason for the increased awareness of reproductive health in recent years is:
A. Increased number of nuclear families and better detection of STDs
B. Improved audio-visual and print media
C. Statutory raising of the marriageable age
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**47.** In the context of amniocentesis, which of the following statements is incorrect?
A. It is used for prenatal diagnosis.
B. It can be used to detect genetic disorders like Down's syndrome.
C. It can be used to detect congenital defects like cleft palate.
D. It is usually done between the 14th and 16th week of pregnancy.
**Correct Answer: C**

**48.** The correct surgical procedure as a contraceptive method is:
A. Ovariectomy
B. Hysterectomy
C. Vasectomy
D. Castration
**Correct Answer: C**

**49.** The most important component of the oral contraceptive pill is:
A. Progesterone
B. Growth hormone
C. Thyroxine
D. Luteinizing hormone
**Correct Answer: A**

**50.** The success of a contraceptive method depends on its:
A. User-friendliness and effectiveness
B. Reversibility and lack of side effects
C. Availability and cost
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

***

&& Principles of Inheritance and Variation

#### Easy

**1.** The father of genetics is:
A. Charles Darwin
B. Gregor Mendel
C. Hugo de Vries
D. T.H. Morgan
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** A trait that is expressed in the F₁ generation of a cross is called:
A. Recessive
B. Dominant
C. Co-dominant
D. Incomplete dominant
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** The genetic makeup of an organism is its:
A. Phenotype
B. Genotype
C. Karyotype
D. Allele
**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** The different forms of a gene are called:
A. Loci
B. Alleles
C. Chromosomes
D. Genomes
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The law of segregation states that during gamete formation, the two alleles for a trait:
A. Segregate from each other
B. Link together
C. Blend together
D. Mutate
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** A cross between two parents differing in a single pair of contrasting characters is called a:
A. Dihybrid cross
B. Monohybrid cross
C. Test cross
D. Back cross
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** The phenotypic ratio of a monohybrid cross in the F₂ generation is:
A. 1:2:1
B. 3:1
C. 9:3:3:1
D. 1:1
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The observable characteristics of an organism are its:
A. Genotype
B. Phenotype
C. Karyotype
D. Genome
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** A cross made to determine the genotype of an organism with a dominant phenotype is a:
A. Reciprocal cross
B. Back cross
C. Test cross
D. Dihybrid cross
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** The ABO blood group system in humans is an example of:
A. Incomplete dominance
B. Co-dominance
C. Multiple alleles
D. Both B and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**11.** The physical association of genes on a chromosome is called:
A. Recombination
B. Linkage
C. Segregation
D. Independent assortment
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** Sex determination in humans is of the type:
A. XX-XO
B. XX-XY
C. ZW-ZZ
D. ZO-ZZ
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** A chart that represents the inheritance of a particular trait through several generations of a family is a:
A. Karyotype
B. Punnett square
C. Pedigree chart
D. Chromosomal map
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** Down's syndrome is a genetic disorder caused by the presence of an extra copy of which chromosome?
A. Chromosome 21
B. Chromosome 18
C. X-chromosome
D. Y-chromosome
**Correct Answer: A**

**15.** Sickle-cell anaemia is an example of a:
A. Chromosomal disorder
B. Mendelian disorder (Point mutation)
C. Viral disease
D. Bacterial disease
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The genotypic ratio of a monohybrid cross in the F₂ generation is:
A. 3:1
B. 1:1
C. 1:2:1
D. 9:3:3:1
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** Mendel's law of independent assortment is applicable for genes that are:
A. Located on the same chromosome
B. Located on different chromosomes or are far apart on the same chromosome
C. Recessive
D. Dominant
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The condition in which a single gene influences multiple phenotypic traits is called:
A. Pleiotropy
B. Polygenic inheritance
C. Co-dominance
D. Multiple allelism
**Correct Answer: A**

**19.** Turner's syndrome is a chromosomal disorder characterized by the genotype:
A. XXY
B. XYY
C. XO
D. XXX
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** Haemophilia is a:
A. Y-linked recessive disorder
B. X-linked recessive disorder
C. Autosomal dominant disorder
D. Autosomal recessive disorder
**Correct Answer: B**

---

#### Medium

**21.** In a dihybrid cross, the phenotypic ratio of 9:3:3:1 is obtained in the F₂ generation. This is an exhibition of the:
A. Law of Segregation
B. Law of Dominance
C. Law of Independent Assortment
D. Principle of Linkage
**Correct Answer: C**

**22.** When the F₁ generation phenotype does not resemble either of the two parents and is in between the two, the phenomenon is called:
A. Co-dominance
B. Incomplete dominance
C. Dominance
D. Pleiotropy
**Correct Answer: B**

**23.** A man with blood group 'A' marries a woman with blood group 'B'. What are the possible blood groups of their offspring?
A. A and B only
B. A, B, and AB only
C. A, B, AB, and O
D. O only
**Correct Answer: C**

**24.** The frequency of recombination between gene pairs on the same chromosome as a measure of the distance between genes was explained by:
A. Gregor Mendel
B. T.H. Morgan
C. Sutton and Boveri
D. Alfred Sturtevant
**Correct Answer: D**

**25.** A human female with Turner's syndrome:
A. Has 45 chromosomes with XO genotype
B. Is sterile and has rudimentary ovaries
C. Lacks Barr bodies
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**26.** Phenylketonuria (PKU) is a genetic disorder caused by a defect in the metabolism of the amino acid:
A. Tyrosine
B. Phenylalanine
C. Tryptophan
D. Glycine
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** A test cross is performed by crossing an individual of unknown genotype with a:
A. Homozygous dominant individual
B. Homozygous recessive individual
C. Heterozygous individual
D. Another F₁ individual
**Correct Answer: B**

**28.** The chromosomal theory of inheritance was proposed by:
A. Mendel
B. Morgan
C. Watson and Crick
D. Sutton and Boveri
**Correct Answer: D**

**29.** The condition of having an additional copy of a chromosome in a diploid cell is called:
A. Monosomy (2n-1)
B. Trisomy (2n+1)
C. Polyploidy
D. Aneuploidy
**Correct Answer: B**

**30.** The percentage of recombination between two linked genes is directly proportional to the:
A. Distance between the genes
B. Strength of the linkage
C. Number of chromosomes
D. Number of alleles
**Correct Answer: A**

**31.** In a pedigree analysis, a filled circle represents a(n):
A. Affected male
B. Affected female
C. Unaffected male
D. Unaffected female
**Correct Answer: B**

**32.** The experiment on *Drosophila melanogaster* that demonstrated the role of chromosomes in heredity was conducted by:
A. Gregor Mendel
B. Thomas Hunt Morgan
C. Alfred Hershey and Martha Chase
D. Friedrich Miescher
**Correct Answer: B**

**33.** A man whose father was colour-blind marries a woman who had a colour-blind mother and a normal father. What percentage of male children of this couple will be colour-blind?
A. 25%
B. 0%
C. 50%
D. 75%
**Correct Answer: C**

**34.** A classic example of pleiotropy is:
A. ABO blood groups
B. Flower colour in snapdragon
C. Human skin colour
D. Phenylketonuria
**Correct Answer: D**

**35.** Klinefelter's syndrome is characterized by a male with the genotype:
A. XO
B. XY
C. XXY
D. XYY
**Correct Answer: C**

**36.** A cross between a red-flowered plant and a white-flowered plant of Antirrhinum produces all pink-flowered plants. This is an example of:
A. Dominance
B. Co-dominance
C. Incomplete dominance
D. Linkage
**Correct Answer: C**

**37.** Human skin colour is an example of:
A. Multiple allelism
B. Pleiotropy
C. Polygenic inheritance
D. Co-dominance
**Correct Answer: C**

**38.** Thalassemia is an autosomal recessive blood disorder. It differs from sickle-cell anaemia in that:
A. Thalassemia is a qualitative problem of synthesizing globin molecules
B. Thalassemia is a quantitative problem of synthesizing too few globin molecules
C. Sickle-cell anaemia is a chromosomal disorder
D. Thalassemia is caused by a virus
**Correct Answer: B**

**39.** The term 'linkage' was coined by:
A. G. Mendel
B. W. Sutton
C. T. Boveri
D. T.H. Morgan
**Correct Answer: D**

**40.** A dihybrid cross between two heterozygous parents (RrYy) results in a phenotypic ratio of 9:3:3:1. This shows that the alleles for seed shape and seed colour are:
A. Linked
B. Co-dominant
C. Assorting independently
D. Recessive
**Correct Answer: C**

#### Hard

**41.** In a certain plant, red fruit (R) is dominant over yellow fruit (r) and tallness (T) is dominant over dwarfness (t). If a plant with genotype RRTt is crossed with a plant of genotype rrtt, what will be the percentage of tall plants with red fruits in the next generation?
A. 100%
B. 25%
C. 50%
D. 75%
**Correct Answer: C**

**42.** Two linked genes a and b show 20% recombination. The individuals of a dihybrid cross between ++/++ and ab/ab shall show gametes in the proportion:
A. ++ 80%, ab 20%
B. ++ 50%, ab 50%
C. ++ 40%, ab 40%, +a 10%, +b 10%
D. ++ 30%, ab 30%, +a 20%, +b 20%
**Correct Answer: C**

**43.** The probability of a child with blood group O being born to parents with blood groups A and B is:
A. 0%
B. 25%
C. 50%
D. 75%
**Correct Answer: B**
*(Note: This assumes both parents are heterozygous, Iᴬi and Iᴮi)*

**44.** In a pedigree chart, a marriage between relatives is represented by:
A. A single horizontal line
B. A double horizontal line
C. A vertical line
D. A shaded symbol
**Correct Answer: B**

**45.** A fruit fly is heterozygous for sex-linked genes. When mated with a normal female fruit fly, the males of the F₁ generation will be:
A. 50% dominant, 50% recessive
B. All dominant
C. All recessive
D. 75% dominant, 25% recessive
**Correct Answer: A**

**46.** How many different types of gametes can be produced by an individual with the genotype AABbCcDd?
A. 4
B. 8
C. 16
D. 32
**Correct Answer: B**

**47.** A cross in which an organism showing a dominant phenotype is crossed with the recessive parent in order to know its genotype is called:
A. Monohybrid cross
B. Dihybrid cross
C. Back cross
D. Test cross
**Correct Answer: D**
*(Note: A test cross is a specific type of back cross.)*

**48.** The number of linkage groups in an organism is equal to its:
A. Diploid number of chromosomes
B. Haploid number of chromosomes
C. Number of genes
D. Number of alleles
**Correct Answer: B**

**49.** If a genetic disease is transferred from a phenotypically normal but carrier female to only some of the male progeny, the disease is:
A. Autosomal dominant
B. Autosomal recessive
C. Sex-linked dominant
D. Sex-linked recessive
**Correct Answer: D**

**50.** The number of barr bodies in a female with Turner's syndrome (XO) is:
A. 0
B. 1
C. 2
D. 44
**Correct Answer: A**

&& Molecular Basis of Inheritance

#### Easy

**1.** The genetic material in most organisms is:
A. RNA
B. DNA
C. Protein
D. Carbohydrate
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** DNA is a polymer of:
A. Amino acids
B. Monosaccharides
C. Fatty acids
D. Deoxyribonucleotides
**Correct Answer: D**

**3.** The two strands of a DNA double helix are:
A. Parallel and complementary
B. Antiparallel and complementary
C. Parallel and identical
D. Antiparallel and identical
**Correct Answer: B**

**4.** The process of making a copy of a DNA molecule is called:
A. Transcription
B. Translation
C. Replication
D. Transformation
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** The process of synthesizing RNA from a DNA template is called:
A. Replication
B. Transcription
C. Translation
D. Reverse transcription
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The process of synthesizing a protein from an mRNA template is called:
A. Replication
B. Transcription
C. Translation
D. Transformation
**Correct Answer: C**

**7.** The "Central Dogma" of molecular biology was proposed by:
A. Watson and Crick
B. Francis Crick
C. Hershey and Chase
D. Gregor Mendel
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The enzyme that joins the short fragments of DNA (Okazaki fragments) during replication is:
A. DNA polymerase
B. DNA ligase
C. Helicase
D. Primase
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The genetic code is a set of rules by which information encoded in genetic material is translated into proteins. Each codon is a:
A. Duplet of bases
B. Triplet of bases
C. Singlet of bases
D. Quadruplet of bases
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** The start codon, which initiates protein synthesis, is:
A. UAA
B. UAG
C. UGA
D. AUG
**Correct Answer: D**

**11.** The experiment that proved that DNA is the genetic material was conducted by:
A. Griffith
B. Avery, MacLeod, and McCarty
C. Hershey and Chase
D. Meselson and Stahl
**Correct Answer: C**

**12.** The structure of a DNA double helix was proposed by:
A. Meselson and Stahl
B. Hershey and Chase
C. Watson and Crick
D. Wilkins and Franklin
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** The nitrogenous base Uracil is found in:
A. DNA only
B. RNA only
C. Both DNA and RNA
D. Neither DNA nor RNA
**Correct Answer: B**

**14.** The bonds that link the nucleotides in a single strand of a nucleic acid are called:
A. Peptide bonds
B. Hydrogen bonds
C. Phosphodiester bonds
D. Glycosidic bonds
**Correct Answer: C**

**15.** In eukaryotes, the DNA is packaged into a structure called chromatin. The basic repeating unit of chromatin is the:
A. Nucleosome
B. Solenoid
C. Chromosome
D. Histone
**Correct Answer: A**

**16.** The enzyme that catalyzes transcription is:
A. DNA polymerase
B. RNA polymerase
C. DNA ligase
D. Helicase
**Correct Answer: B**

**17.** The regions of a gene that are transcribed but later removed from the mRNA are called:
A. Exons
B. Introns
C. Promoters
D. Terminators
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The technique used to separate DNA fragments based on their size is:
A. PCR
B. Gel electrophoresis
C. DNA fingerprinting
D. Southern blotting
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** The lac operon is a model system for understanding gene regulation in:
A. Eukaryotes
B. Prokaryotes (like *E. coli*)
C. Viruses
D. Plants
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** The Human Genome Project aimed to:
A. Sequence the entire human genome
B. Clone a human
C. Cure all genetic diseases
D. Create new genes
**Correct Answer: A**

#### Medium

**21.** The experiment by Meselson and Stahl on *E. coli* demonstrated that DNA replication is:
A. Conservative
B. Semi-conservative
C. Dispersive
D. Non-conservative
**Correct Answer: B**

**22.** The enzyme that unwinds the DNA double helix during replication is:
A. DNA polymerase
B. DNA ligase
C. Helicase
D. Topoisomerase
**Correct Answer: C**

**23.** In a DNA molecule, the percentage of Adenine is 30%. The percentage of Guanine would be:
A. 30%
B. 70%
C. 40%
D. 20%
**Correct Answer: D**

**24.** The genetic code is said to be degenerate, which means that:
A. One codon can code for more than one amino acid
B. One amino acid can be coded by more than one codon
C. The code is universal
D. The code is non-overlapping
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** The process of removing introns and joining exons in a defined order in a primary transcript is called:
A. Splicing
B. Capping
C. Tailing
D. Termination
**Correct Answer: A**

**26.** In the lac operon, the lactose molecule acts as a(n):
A. Repressor
B. Inducer
C. Promoter
D. Operator
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** A nucleosome is a structure where a DNA segment is wrapped around a core of:
A. Four histone proteins
B. Eight histone proteins (histone octamer)
C. A single histone protein (H1)
D. Non-histone chromosomal proteins
**Correct Answer: B**

**28.** The enzyme reverse transcriptase catalyzes the synthesis of:
A. RNA from RNA
B. DNA from RNA
C. DNA from DNA
D. RNA from DNA
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** DNA fingerprinting is based on the identification of repetitive DNA sequences called:
A. Exons
B. Introns
C. Variable Number of Tandem Repeats (VNTRs)
D. Single Nucleotide Polymorphisms (SNPs)
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** The adapter molecule that reads the genetic code on mRNA and brings the specific amino acid is:
A. Ribosomal RNA (rRNA)
B. Messenger RNA (mRNA)
C. Transfer RNA (tRNA)
D. Small nuclear RNA (snRNA)
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** The process of adding a methyl guanosine triphosphate cap to the 5'-end of hnRNA is called:
A. Splicing
B. Tailing
C. Capping
D. Termination
**Correct Answer: C**

**32.** In Griffith's transformation experiment, the heat-killed S-strain bacteria injected into mice along with live R-strain bacteria caused the mice to die because:
A. The R-strain mutated into the S-strain
B. The S-strain was not completely killed
C. A "transforming principle" from the heat-killed S-strain transformed the R-strain
D. The mice were allergic to the R-strain
**Correct Answer: C**

**33.** The promoter region of a transcription unit is the site where:
A. The repressor protein binds
B. The RNA polymerase binds
C. Transcription terminates
D. The inducer binds
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** Which of the following is a stop codon?
A. AUG
B. GUG
C. UAA
D. UUU
**Correct Answer: C**

**35.** The lac operon is switched 'on' when:
A. Lactose is present and it binds to the repressor
B. Lactose is absent and the repressor binds to the operator
C. Glucose is present
D. The repressor binds to the promoter
**Correct Answer: A**

**36.** The Okazaki fragments formed during DNA replication are found on the:
A. Leading strand
B. Lagging strand
C. Both leading and lagging strands
D. RNA primer
**Correct Answer: B**

**37.** The unequivocal proof that DNA is the genetic material came from the experiments of:
A. Griffith
B. Watson and Crick
C. Avery, MacLeod, and McCarty
D. Hershey and Chase
**Correct Answer: D**

**38.** The enzyme that links amino acids together to form a polypeptide chain is:
A. Aminoacyl-tRNA synthetase
B. Peptidyl transferase
C. RNA polymerase
D. DNA ligase
**Correct Answer: B**

**39.** The structure in chromatin that appears as 'beads-on-a-string' is the:
A. Nucleosome
B. Solenoid
C. Chromosome
D. Gene
**Correct Answer: A**

**40.** If the sequence of bases in the coding strand of a DNA is ATTCGATG, then the sequence of bases in the mRNA will be:
A. TAAGCTAC
B. UAAGCUAC
C. AUUCGAUG
D. ATTCGATG
**Correct Answer: C**

#### Hard

**41.** The experiment by Avery, MacLeod, and McCarty showed that the transformation of R-strain bacteria into S-strain was inhibited by the enzyme:
A. Protease
B. RNase
C. DNase
D. Lipase
**Correct Answer: C**

**42.** A DNA molecule has 2000 base pairs. The length of this DNA molecule will be approximately:
A. 680 nm
B. 340 nm
C. 68 nm
D. 34 nm
**Correct Answer: A**
*(Note: Distance between base pairs is 0.34 nm, so 2000 × 0.34 = 680 nm)*

**43.** In the lac operon, if a mutation occurs in the operator region such that the repressor cannot bind, what will be the outcome?
A. The operon will never be switched on.
B. The operon will be switched on only in the presence of lactose.
C. The operon will be constitutively (always) switched on.
D. The Z, Y, and A genes will not be transcribed.
**Correct Answer: C**

**44.** Which of the following is correct regarding the genetic code?
A. It is ambiguous.
B. It is overlapping.
C. A codon is read in a contiguous fashion.
D. It is not universal.
**Correct Answer: C**

**45.** Taylor and colleagues performed experiments on *Vicia faba* using radioactive thymidine to prove that:
A. DNA is the genetic material
B. RNA is the genetic material in some viruses
C. DNA replication is semi-conservative in eukaryotes
D. The genetic code is a triplet
**Correct Answer: C**

**46.** The process of adding adenylate residues at the 3'-end of the primary transcript in a template-independent manner is called:
A. Capping
B. Splicing
C. Tailing (Polyadenylation)
D. Editing
**Correct Answer: C**

**47.** The UTRs (untranslated regions) are present on an mRNA:
A. Before the start codon and after the stop codon
B. Only before the start codon
C. Only after the stop codon
D. Within the coding sequence
**Correct Answer: A**

**48.** In the Hershey and Chase experiment, DNA was shown to be the genetic material because:
A. The radioactivity from ³²P was found in the supernatant after centrifugation.
B. The radioactivity from ³⁵S was found in the bacterial cells.
C. The radioactivity from ³²P was found in the bacterial cells.
D. The radioactivity from ³⁵S was found in the next generation of bacteriophages.
**Correct Answer: C**

**49.** If a DNA molecule has 20% Cytosine, the percentage of Adenine will be:
A. 20%
B. 30%
C. 40%
D. 60%
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** The binding of the inducer (lactose) to the lac repressor results in a conformational change that:
A. Increases the repressor's affinity for the operator
B. Decreases the repressor's affinity for the operator
C. Increases the repressor's affinity for the promoter
D. Causes the repressor to bind to the inducer and the operator simultaneously
**Correct Answer: B**
