&& Evolution

#### Easy

**1.** The theory that life on Earth originated from non-living organic molecules is known as:
A. Panspermia
B. Special creation
C. Abiogenesis (Chemical evolution)
D. Biogenesis
**Correct Answer: C**

**2.** The experiment to prove the chemical origin of life was performed by:
A. Oparin and Haldane
B. Miller and Urey
C. Louis Pasteur
D. Charles Darwin
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** The concept of "inheritance of acquired characters" was proposed by:
A. Charles Darwin
B. Alfred Wallace
C. Jean-Baptiste Lamarck
D. Hugo de Vries
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** The theory of natural selection as the mechanism for evolution was proposed by Charles Darwin and:
A. Gregor Mendel
B. Alfred Russel Wallace
C. Thomas Malthus
D. August Weismann
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The wings of a bat and the wings of an insect are examples of:
A. Homologous structures
B. Analogous structures
C. Vestigial structures
D. Atavistic structures
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The preserved remains or traces of ancient organisms are called:
A. Fossils
B. Relics
C. Artifacts
D. Specimens
**Correct Answer: A**

**7.** Homologous structures are those that have a similar origin and basic structure but may perform:
A. The same function
B. Different functions
C. No function
D. Only one function
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The book 'On the Origin of Species' was written by:
A. Lamarck
B. Wallace
C. Darwin
D. Oparin
**Correct Answer: C**

**9.** The sudden appearance of large differences in a population, which Hugo de Vries called mutations, is the basis of his theory of:
A. Natural selection
B. Pangenesis
C. Saltation
D. Inheritance of acquired characters
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** The Hardy-Weinberg principle describes a population that is:
A. Actively evolving
B. Not evolving (in genetic equilibrium)
C. Undergoing speciation
D. Experiencing genetic drift
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** The process by which different species evolve from a common ancestor in a given geographical area is called:
A. Convergent evolution
B. Adaptive radiation
C. Parallel evolution
D. Co-evolution
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** The phenomenon where two or more unrelated species evolve similar traits as they adapt to similar environments is:
A. Divergent evolution
B. Convergent evolution
C. Co-evolution
D. Adaptive radiation
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The appendix in humans and the pelvic bones in snakes are examples of:
A. Homologous organs
B. Analogous organs
C. Vestigial organs
D. Adaptive organs
**Correct Answer: C**

**14.** The change in the allele frequencies of a population that occurs by chance is called:
A. Gene flow
B. Mutation
C. Natural selection
D. Genetic drift
**Correct Answer: D**

**15.** The theory of panspermia suggests that life on Earth may have come from:
A. Non-living matter
B. Outer space
C. The deep sea
D. A divine creator
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** Which of the following is considered a 'living fossil'?
A. *Archaeopteryx*
B. *Limulus* (King crab)
C. Dodo
D. Mammoth
**Correct Answer: B**

**17.** The forelimbs of a human, a whale, and a bat are examples of:
A. Analogous structures
B. Homologous structures
C. Vestigial structures
D. Convergent structures
**Correct Answer: B**

**18.** The phrase "survival of the fittest" is most closely associated with the theory of:
A. Lamarckism
B. Natural Selection
C. Mutation
D. Catastrophism
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** The study of fossils is known as:
A. Paleontology
B. Embryology
C. Anthropology
D. Geology
**Correct Answer: A**

**20.** The final stage in the evolution of modern man (*Homo sapiens*) was preceded by:
A. *Australopithecus*
B. *Homo habilis*
C. Neanderthal man (*Homo neanderthalensis*)
D. *Homo erectus*
**Correct Answer: C**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The Miller-Urey experiment simulated the conditions of the primitive Earth's atmosphere. The gases they used were:
A. Methane, Ammonia, Hydrogen, and Water vapour
B. Methane, Oxygen, Hydrogen, and Water vapour
C. Oxygen, Nitrogen, Carbon dioxide, and Water vapour
D. Methane, Ammonia, Nitrogen, and Water vapour
**Correct Answer: A**

**22.** Darwin's finches on the Galapagos Islands are a classic example of:
A. Convergent evolution
B. Adaptive radiation
C. Genetic drift
D. Co-evolution
**Correct Answer: B**

**23.** According to the Hardy-Weinberg principle, which of the following is not a factor that affects allele frequencies in a population?
A. Mutation
B. Natural selection
C. Random mating
D. Genetic drift
**Correct Answer: C**

**24.** The connecting link between reptiles and birds is:
A. *Seymouria*
B. *Archaeopteryx*
C. *Peripatus*
D. *Sphenodon*
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** The "founder effect" is a special case of:
A. Natural selection
B. Mutation
C. Gene flow
D. Genetic drift
**Correct Answer: D**

**26.** The presence of gills in the embryos of all vertebrates supports the theory of:
A. Recapitulation (Biogenetic law)
B. Natural selection
C. Catastrophism
D. Mutation
**Correct Answer: A**

**27.** The evolution of marsupials in Australia and placental mammals in other parts of the world is an example of:
A. Convergent evolution
B. Parallel evolution
C. Divergent evolution
D. Saltation
**Correct Answer: B**

**28.** In a population at Hardy-Weinberg equilibrium, the frequency of a recessive allele is 0.4. What is the frequency of heterozygous individuals?
A. 0.16
B. 0.36
C. 0.48
D. 0.24
**Correct Answer: C**

**29.** The Industrial Melanism observed in the peppered moth (*Biston betularia*) is an example of:
A. Directional selection
B. Stabilizing selection
C. Disruptive selection
D. Artificial selection
**Correct Answer: A**

**30.** The similarity in the structure of the eye of an octopus and a mammal is an example of:
A. Homology
B. Analogy
C. Atavism
D. Vestigiality
**Correct Answer: B**

**31.** The concept that "Ontogeny recapitulates Phylogeny" was proposed by:
A. Darwin
B. Haeckel
C. Wallace
D. Weismann
**Correct Answer: B**

**32.** The first life forms on Earth were likely:
A. Aerobic chemoheterotrophs
B. Anaerobic chemoheterotrophs
C. Aerobic photoautotrophs
D. Anaerobic photoautotrophs
**Correct Answer: B**

**33.** Which era is known as the 'Age of Reptiles'?
A. Cenozoic
B. Mesozoic
C. Paleozoic
D. Proterozoic
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** A change in the gene pool of a population due to the migration of individuals is called:
A. Genetic drift
B. Gene flow
C. Mutation
D. Natural selection
**Correct Answer: B**

**35.** The human ancestor who was the first to stand erect and had a cranial capacity of about 900 cc was:
A. *Australopithecus*
B. *Homo habilis*
C. *Homo erectus*
D. *Homo neanderthalensis*
**Correct Answer: C**

**36.** Stabilizing selection is a type of natural selection in which:
A. More individuals acquire mean character value
B. More individuals acquire peripheral character value
C. More individuals acquire value other than the mean character value
D. A new species is formed
**Correct Answer: A**

**37.** The earliest organisms to release oxygen into the atmosphere through photosynthesis were likely:
A. Algae
B. Cyanobacteria
C. Plants
D. Fungi
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The Hardy-Weinberg equation is represented as:
A. p² + q² = 1
B. p + q = 1
C. p² + 2pq + q² = 1
D. Both B and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**39.** The primary sources of variation upon which natural selection acts are:
A. Genetic drift and gene flow
B. Mutation and sexual recombination
C. Asexual reproduction and budding
D. Acquired characteristics
**Correct Answer: B**

**40.** The first hominid, known as the 'handy man', was:
A. *Australopithecus*
B. *Homo habilis*
C. *Homo erectus*
D. Ramapithecus
**Correct Answer: B**

---

#### Hard

**41.** In a population of 1000 individuals, 360 belong to genotype AA, 480 to Aa, and the remaining 160 to aa. Based on this data, the frequency of allele 'A' in the population is:
A. 0.4
B. 0.5
C. 0.6
D. 0.7
**Correct Answer: C**

**42.** The appearance of antibiotic-resistant bacteria is an example of:
A. Adaptive radiation
B. Transduction
C. Pre-existing variation in the population selected by a changing environment
D. Divergent evolution
**Correct Answer: C**

**43.** If the frequency of a dominant allele 'A' is 0.6 in a population at Hardy-Weinberg equilibrium, then the percentage of the population that is homozygous recessive ('aa') will be:
A. 36%
B. 48%
C. 16%
D. 4%
**Correct Answer: C**

**44.** Which of the following is a correct statement regarding human evolution?
A. *Homo erectus* is the direct ancestor of modern man.
B. Neanderthal man and Cro-Magnon man co-existed for some time.
C. *Australopithecus* had a larger brain size than *Homo habilis*.
D. The first human-like being was *Dryopithecus*.
**Correct Answer: B**

**45.** A population is in Hardy-Weinberg equilibrium for a gene with two alleles, A and a. If the frequency of the genotype AA is 0.09, what is the frequency of the allele A?
A. 0.09
B. 0.3
C. 0.7
D. 0.49
**Correct Answer: B**

**46.** The concept of chemical evolution is based on:
A. The possible origin of life by a combination of chemicals under suitable environmental conditions.
B. The crystallization of chemicals.
C. The interaction of water, air, and clay under intense heat.
D. The effect of solar radiation on chemicals.
**Correct Answer: A**

**47.** Disruptive selection is a type of natural selection that:
A. Favors the mean character value
B. Favors both extreme phenotypes over the intermediate phenotype
C. Leads to the formation of a single, new species
D. Eliminates variation from a population
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** The evolution of the different beak shapes of Darwin's finches is a result of:
A. Interspecific competition for food resources
B. Intraspecific competition for mates
C. Genetic drift
D. The founder effect
**Correct Answer: A**

**49.** Which of the following provides the most evident proof of evolution?
A. Fossils
B. Embryology
C. Morphology
D. Vestigial organs
**Correct Answer: A**

**50.** The tendency of a population to remain in genetic equilibrium may be disturbed by:
A. Lack of mutations
B. Lack of random mating
C. Random mating
D. Lack of migration
**Correct Answer: B**

&& Human Health and Diseases

#### Easy

**1.** A state of complete physical, mental, and social well-being is defined as:
A. Disease
B. Health
C. Immunity
D. Infection
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The pathogen responsible for causing the common cold is:
A. *Salmonella typhi*
B. *Streptococcus pneumoniae*
C. Rhinovirus
D. *Plasmodium vivax*
**Correct Answer: C**

**3.** Typhoid fever is caused by a bacterium called:
A. *Plasmodium*
B. *Wuchereria*
C. *Salmonella typhi*
D. Rhinovirus
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** Malaria is a protozoan disease transmitted by the bite of a:
A. Male Anopheles mosquito
B. Female Anopheles mosquito
C. Male Aedes mosquito
D. Female Aedes mosquito
**Correct Answer: B**

**5.** The type of immunity that is present from birth and is non-specific is called:
A. Acquired immunity
B. Innate immunity
C. Active immunity
D. Passive immunity
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The army of proteins produced by B-lymphocytes in response to pathogens is:
A. Antigens
B. Antibodies
C. Interferons
D. Allergens
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** Vaccination is a form of:
A. Innate immunity
B. Active immunity
C. Passive immunity
D. Autoimmunity
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The exaggerated response of the immune system to certain antigens present in the environment is called:
A. Autoimmunity
B. Immunity
C. Allergy
D. Vaccination
**Correct Answer: C**

**9.** The primary lymphoid organs, where lymphocytes mature and differentiate, are the bone marrow and the:
A. Spleen
B. Tonsils
C. Thymus
D. Lymph nodes
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** AIDS is caused by the Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV), which is a type of:
A. Bacterium
B. Protozoan
C. Retrovirus
D. Helminth
**Correct Answer: C**

**11.** Cancer is a disease characterized by uncontrolled:
A. Cell division
B. Cell growth
C. Cell differentiation
D. Both A and B
**Correct Answer: D**

**12.** The property by which normal cells inhibit the growth of other cells upon contact is called:
A. Metastasis
B. Contact inhibition
C. Apoptosis
D. Angiogenesis
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The most common type of cancer is:
A. Sarcoma
B. Leukemia
C. Lymphoma
D. Carcinoma
**Correct Answer: D**

**14.** The causal organism for ringworm is a:
A. Bacterium
B. Virus
C. Protozoan
D. Fungus
**Correct Answer: D**

**15.** The antibodies produced in colostrum (first mother's milk) provide which type of immunity to the infant?
A. Active immunity
B. Passive immunity
C. Innate immunity
D. Cell-mediated immunity
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The cell-mediated immune response is carried out by:
A. B-lymphocytes
B. T-lymphocytes
C. Erythrocytes
D. Thrombocytes
**Correct Answer: B**

**17.** The full form of MALT, which constitutes about 50% of the lymphoid tissue in the human body, is:
A. Mucosal-Associated Lymphoid Tissue
B. Medullary-Associated Lymphoid Tissue
C. Membrane-Associated Lymphoid Tissue
D. Muscle-Associated Lymphoid Tissue
**Correct Answer: A**

**18.** The malignant stage of a tumor, where tumor cells spread to distant sites through blood, is called:
A. Benign
B. Neoplasm
C. Metastasis
D. Carcinogenesis
**Correct Answer: C**

**19.** The common disease filariasis or elephantiasis is caused by:
A. *Ascaris lumbricoides*
B. *Wuchereria bancrofti*
C. *Plasmodium falciparum*
D. *Entamoeba histolytica*
**Correct Answer: B**

**20.** Which of the following is an autoimmune disease?
A. AIDS
B. Cancer
C. Rheumatoid arthritis
D. Typhoid
**Correct Answer: C**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The Widal test is used for the diagnosis of:
A. Malaria
B. Typhoid
C. Pneumonia
D. AIDS
**Correct Answer: B**

**22.** The infective stage of *Plasmodium* that enters the human body through a mosquito bite is the:
A. Merozoite
B. Sporozoite
C. Gametocyte
D. Trophozoite
**Correct Answer: B**

**23.** A typical antibody molecule is Y-shaped and consists of:
A. Two heavy chains and two light chains
B. Four heavy chains
C. Four light chains
D. One heavy chain and one light chain
**Correct Answer: A**

**24.** The principle of vaccination is based on the property of 'memory' of the immune system. The cells responsible for this memory are:
A. B-lymphocytes and T-lymphocytes
B. Memory B-cells and Memory T-cells
C. Helper T-cells
D. Killer T-cells
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** During an allergic reaction, the chemicals like histamine and serotonin are released from:
A. B-lymphocytes
B. T-lymphocytes
C. Mast cells
D. Neutrophils
**Correct Answer: C**

**26.** The HIV virus attacks and destroys which cells of the immune system, leading to immunodeficiency?
A. B-lymphocytes
B. Helper T-lymphocytes (Tₕ cells)
C. Cytotoxic T-lymphocytes
D. Natural killer cells
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** Cancer-causing genes are known as:
A. Proto-oncogenes
B. Oncogenes
C. Tumor suppressor genes
D. Mutagens
**Correct Answer: B**

**28.** The diagnostic test for AIDS is:
A. Widal test
B. ELISA test
C. MRI scan
D. Biopsy
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** The 'chills and high fever' recurring every three to four days in a malarial infection are associated with the:
A. Rupture of RBCs and release of a toxic substance called hemozoin
B. Entry of sporozoites into the liver
C. Formation of gametocytes
D. Bite of a female Anopheles mosquito
**Correct Answer: A**

**30.** The type of barrier in innate immunity that includes tears from the eyes and acid in the stomach is:
A. Physical barrier
B. Physiological barrier
C. Cellular barrier
D. Cytokine barrier
**Correct Answer: B**

**31.** The spleen is a large bean-shaped organ that mainly contains lymphocytes and phagocytes. It acts as a:
A. Primary lymphoid organ
B. Filter for the blood, trapping blood-borne microorganisms
C. Site of T-cell maturation
D. Site for the production of all blood cells
**Correct Answer: B**

**32.** Which of the following is not a carcinogen?
A. UV radiation
B. X-rays
C. Tobacco smoke
D. Interferons
**Correct Answer: D**

**33.** The drug 'smack' is a chemically diacetylmorphine, which is a:
A. Stimulant
B. Depressant and opiate
C. Hallucinogen
D. Cannabinoid
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** Cirrhosis of the liver is a chronic disease caused by the long-term abuse of:
A. Tobacco
B. Opioids
C. Alcohol
D. Cocaine
**Correct Answer: C**

**35.** The antibody produced in response to an allergen is of the type:
A. IgA
B. IgE
C. IgG
D. IgM
**Correct Answer: B**

**36.** The life cycle of *Plasmodium* is completed in two hosts. The sexual stages develop in the mosquito, which is the:
A. Primary host
B. Secondary host
C. Intermediate host
D. Vector
**Correct Answer: D**
*(Note: For Plasmodium, the mosquito is the definitive/primary host and humans are the intermediate/secondary host. Vector is also a correct description.)*

**37.** The treatment of cancer involves chemotherapy, which uses drugs to kill cancer cells, but it often has side effects like hair loss and anemia because:
A. The drugs are not effective
B. The drugs also harm rapidly dividing normal cells
C. The drugs cause allergic reactions
D. The drugs are administered in low doses
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The main function of humoral or antibody-mediated immunity is to defend against:
A. Intracellular pathogens like viruses
B. Extracellular pathogens like bacteria and viruses in body fluids
C. Cancer cells
D. Fungi
**Correct Answer: B**

**39.** The blocking of the intestinal passage and the internal bleeding caused by *Ascaris lumbricoides* is known as:
A. Filariasis
B. Amoebiasis
C. Ascariasis
D. Pneumonia
**Correct Answer: C**

**40.** The withdrawal syndrome is a set of symptoms that occur when:
A. A drug is taken for the first time
B. The regular dose of a drug is abruptly discontinued
C. A person develops tolerance to a drug
D. A drug is taken in combination with another drug
**Correct Answer: B**

#### Hard

**41.** The structure of a typical antibody molecule is represented as H₂L₂. The 'H' and 'L' stand for:
A. Heavy chain and Light chain
B. Hinge region and Loop region
C. Helical chain and Linear chain
D. Histamine and Leucotriene
**Correct Answer: A**

**42.** The correct sequence of events after HIV enters the T-helper cells is:
A. Viral DNA is produced by reverse transcriptase → Viral DNA incorporates into host genome → New viral RNA is produced → New viruses are produced
B. Viral RNA is produced by reverse transcriptase → Viral RNA incorporates into host genome → New viral DNA is produced → New viruses are produced
C. Viral RNA is directly translated into viral proteins → New viruses are produced
D. The virus remains dormant in the cell indefinitely.
**Correct Answer: A**

**43.** Which of the following is a correct statement regarding immunity?
A. Active immunity is quick and gives a full response.
B. Foetus receives some antibodies from the mother; it is an example of active immunity.
C. When ready-made antibodies are directly given, it is called passive immunity.
D. The T-lymphocytes produce antibodies.
**Correct Answer: C**

**44.** The drug that interferes with the transport of the neurotransmitter dopamine and produces a sense of euphoria is:
A. Morphine
B. Cocaine
C. LSD
D. Hashish
**Correct Answer: B**

**45.** The cellular barriers of innate immunity include:
A. Polymorpho-nuclear leukocytes (PMNL-neutrophils)
B. Monocytes and natural killer cells
C. Macrophages in tissues
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**46.** A patient is diagnosed with a benign tumor. This means that the tumor is:
A. Confined to its original location and does not spread to other parts of the body
B. Actively spreading to other parts of the body
C. Caused by a virus
D. The most dangerous type of cancer
**Correct Answer: A**

**47.** The principle of immunization is based on the property of the immune system to generate memory. This means that a subsequent encounter with the same pathogen elicits a:
A. Primary response, which is of low intensity
B. Anamnestic (secondary) response, which is highly intensified
C. Tertiary response
D. Allergic response
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** The source plant for the cannabinoids, which include marijuana, hashish, charas, and ganja, is:
A. *Papaver somniferum*
B. *Erythroxylum coca*
C. *Cannabis sativa*
D. *Atropa belladonna*
**Correct Answer: C**

**49.** Interferons are proteins secreted by virus-infected cells that:
A. Directly kill the virus
B. Protect non-infected cells from further viral infection
C. Stimulate the production of antibodies
D. Act as a physical barrier
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** A person who has undergone a transplant, such as a kidney transplant, has to take immunosuppressant drugs for the rest of their life because:
A. The new kidney is not functional
B. The cell-mediated immune response of the body will try to reject the foreign organ
C. The antibody-mediated immune response will fail
D. The person is likely to get new infections
**Correct Answer: B**

&& Microbes in Human Welfare

#### Easy

**1.** The bacterium used for the production of curd from milk is:
A. *Acetobacter aceti*
B. *Lactobacillus*
C. *Saccharomyces cerevisiae*
D. *Penicillium notatum*
**Correct Answer: B**

**2.** The large holes in 'Swiss cheese' are due to the production of a large amount of CO₂ by a bacterium named:
A. *Lactobacillus*
B. *Propionibacterium shermanii*
C. *Aspergillus niger*
D. *Saccharomyces cerevisiae*
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** The yeast used for bread making and for fermenting beverages is:
A. *Penicillium*
B. *Aspergillus*
C. *Saccharomyces cerevisiae*
D. *Clostridium botulinum*
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** The first antibiotic to be discovered was:
A. Streptomycin
B. Tetracycline
C. Penicillin
D. Erythromycin
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** Citric acid is produced by the fungus:
A. *Aspergillus niger*
B. *Acetobacter aceti*
C. *Clostridium butylicum*
D. *Lactobacillus*
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** The large vessels in which microbes are grown on an industrial scale to produce beverages and antibiotics are called:
A. Bioreactors
B. Fermenters
C. Digesters
D. Both A and B
**Correct Answer: D**

**7.** The primary treatment of sewage involves the physical removal of particles through:
A. Aeration
B. Filtration and sedimentation
C. Biological oxidation
D. Chemical treatment
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The masses of bacteria associated with fungal filaments to form mesh-like structures in secondary sewage treatment are called:
A. Flocs
B. Sludge
C. Primary sludge
D. Biogas
**Correct Answer: A**

**9.** The major component of biogas is:
A. Oxygen
B. Hydrogen sulphide
C. Methane
D. Carbon dioxide
**Correct Answer: C**

**10.** Microbes that are used to control insect pests are a type of:
A. Biofertilizer
B. Biocontrol agent
C. Biogas
D. Antibiotic
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** A good example of a biofertilizer is the symbiotic association between fungi and the roots of higher plants, known as:
A. Lichen
B. Mycorrhiza
C. Flocs
D. Sludge
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** The bacterium *Bacillus thuringiensis* (Bt) is used to control:
A. Fungal diseases
B. Bacterial diseases
C. Insect pests like butterfly caterpillars
D. Weeds
**Correct Answer: C**

**13.** The bacteria that grow anaerobically on cellulosic material and produce large amounts of methane are called:
A. Methanogens
B. Halophiles
C. Thermoacidophiles
D. Cyanobacteria
**Correct Answer: A**

**14.** The Ladybird beetle is a useful biocontrol agent for controlling:
A. Mosquitoes
B. Aphids
C. Caterpillars
D. Fungi
**Correct Answer: B**

**15.** The free-living fungus *Trichoderma* is effective as a biocontrol agent against:
A. Insect pests
B. Weeds
C. Plant pathogens in the soil
D. Aphids
**Correct Answer: C**

**16.** The enzymes used in detergent formulations to help remove oily stains from laundry are:
A. Proteases
B. Amylases
C. Lipases
D. Pectinases
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The 'Roquefort cheese' is ripened by growing a specific:
A. Bacterium
B. Yeast
C. Fungus
D. Alga
**Correct Answer: C**

**18.** Baculoviruses are excellent candidates for species-specific, narrow-spectrum insecticidal applications because they:
A. Are very harmful to humans
B. Have no negative impacts on non-target insects
C. Kill all types of insects
D. Are easy to produce
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** The main source of biofertilizers are:
A. Bacteria
B. Fungi
C. Cyanobacteria
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**20.** Penicillin was discovered by:
A. Louis Pasteur
B. Robert Koch
C. Alexander Fleming
D. Selman Waksman
**Correct Answer: C**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The measure of the organic matter present in water, which is an indicator of its pollution level, is the:
A. Biochemical Oxygen Demand (BOD)
B. Chemical Oxygen Demand (COD)
C. Total Dissolved Solids (TDS)
D. pH level
**Correct Answer: A**

**22.** The bioactive molecule Cyclosporin A, which is used as an immunosuppressive agent in organ transplant patients, is produced by the fungus:
A. *Monascus purpureus*
B. *Trichoderma polysporum*
C. *Aspergillus niger*
D. *Penicillium chrysogenum*

**23.** Statins, which are used as blood-cholesterol lowering agents, are produced by the yeast:
A. *Saccharomyces cerevisiae*
B. *Monascus purpureus*
C. *Candida lipolytica*
D. *Trichoderma polysporum*

**24.** In secondary sewage treatment, a small part of the activated sludge is pumped back into the aeration tank to serve as a(n):
A. Inoculum
B. Source of organic matter
C. Aerating agent
D. Source of anaerobic bacteria
**Correct Answer: A**

**25.** The enzyme streptokinase, which is used as a 'clot buster' for removing clots from the blood vessels of patients, is produced by the bacterium:
A. *Streptococcus*
B. *Staphylococcus*
C. *Lactobacillus*
D. *Clostridium*

**26.** The technology for biogas production in India was developed mainly due to the efforts of the Indian Agricultural Research Institute (IARI) and the:
A. Ministry of Environment and Forests
B. Khadi and Village Industries Commission (KVIC)
C. Council of Scientific and Industrial Research (CSIR)
D. Department of Biotechnology (DBT)
**Correct Answer: B**

**27.** Which of the following is a symbiotic nitrogen-fixing cyanobacterium?
A. *Azotobacter*
B. *Azospirillum*
C. *Nostoc*
D. *Anabaena* (in association with Azolla)
**Correct Answer: D**

**28.** The bottled fruit juices bought from the market are clearer as compared to those made at home because they are clarified by the use of:
A. Pectinases and Proteases
B. Lipases and Amylases
C. Streptokinase
D. Cyclosporin A
**Correct Answer: A**

**29.** The 'flocs' in sewage treatment are:
A. Masses of anaerobic bacteria
B. Masses of aerobic bacteria and fungal filaments
C. The primary settled solids
D. The effluent from the primary treatment
**Correct Answer: B**

**30.** The free-living bacteria in the soil that can fix atmospheric nitrogen are:
A. *Rhizobium*
B. *Frankia*
C. *Azotobacter* and *Azospirillum*
D. Cyanobacteria
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** The Ministry of Environment and Forests in India has initiated the Ganga Action Plan and the Yamuna Action Plan to:
A. Save these major rivers from pollution
B. Build more dams for electricity generation
C. Promote tourism
D. Increase fishing activities
**Correct Answer: A**

**32.** A high BOD value in a water body indicates that:
A. The water is highly polluted with organic matter
B. The water is clean and rich in dissolved oxygen
C. The water is suitable for drinking
D. There is a low level of microbial activity
**Correct Answer: A**

**33.** The anaerobic sludge digesters in a sewage treatment plant are where:
A. Aerobic bacteria are grown
B. Flocs are formed
C. Biogas is produced
D. The effluent is aerated
**Correct Answer: C**

**34.** The full potential of penicillin as an effective antibiotic was established by:
A. Alexander Fleming
B. Louis Pasteur
C. Ernst Chain and Howard Florey
D. Robert Koch
**Correct Answer: C**

**35.** The genus *Glomus* is a fungus that forms:
A. Ectomycorrhiza
B. Endomycorrhiza (VAM)
C. Lichens
D. Nitrogen-fixing nodules
**Correct Answer: B**

**36.** The large aeration tanks in a sewage treatment plant are constantly agitated and air is pumped into them to:
A. Settle the solids
B. Promote the growth of anaerobic bacteria
C. Promote the growth of aerobic bacteria into flocs
D. Kill all the microbes
**Correct Answer: C**

**37.** The effluent from the primary settling tank is passed into:
A. Large aeration tanks for secondary treatment
B. Anaerobic sludge digesters
C. Natural water bodies
D. A landfill
**Correct Answer: A**

**38.** The purpose of Integrated Pest Management (IPM) is to:
A. Eradicate all pests completely using chemicals
B. Rely solely on biocontrol methods
C. Manage pests in a sustainable way by minimizing the use of chemical pesticides
D. Use only genetically modified crops
**Correct Answer: C**

**39.** The main function of the fungus in a mycorrhizal association is to:
A. Absorb phosphorus from the soil and pass it to the plant
B. Provide food to the plant
C. Fix atmospheric nitrogen
D. Protect the plant from insects
**Correct Answer: A**

**40.** Toddy, a traditional drink in some parts of southern India, is made by fermenting sap from:
A. Sugarcane
B. Grapes
C. Palms
D. Rice
**Correct Answer: C**

#### Hard

**41.** Which of the following is a correct statement?
A. BOD is a measure of the dissolved oxygen in water.
B. The greater the BOD of waste water, the less is its polluting potential.
C. The effluent from the primary treatment plant is generally released into natural water bodies.
D. Secondary treatment of sewage is also called the biological treatment phase.
**Correct Answer: D**

**42.** Match the following and select the correct option:
Column I              Column II
(a) Statins           (i) *Trichoderma polysporum*
(b) Cyclosporin A     (ii) *Monascus purpureus*
(c) Streptokinase     (iii) *Streptococcus*
(d) Butyric Acid      (iv) *Clostridium butylicum*
A. a-ii, b-i, c-iii, d-iv
B. a-iv, b-iii, c-i, d-ii
C. a-ii, b-iii, c-iv, d-i
D. a-i, b-ii, c-iii, d-iv
**Correct Answer: A**

**43.** During the secondary treatment of sewage, the BOD is significantly reduced. This is because:
A. The aerobic microbes consume the major part of the organic matter in the effluent
B. The anaerobic bacteria digest the organic matter
C. The heavy solids settle down in the settling tank
D. The water is chlorinated
**Correct Answer: A**

**44.** Which of the following is not a benefit of using biofertilizers?
A. They are cost-effective and eco-friendly.
B. They enrich the nutrient quality of the soil.
C. They are immediately available to the plants in a soluble form.
D. They do not cause water pollution.
**Correct Answer: C**

**45.** A significant step in the history of microbiology was the development of the vaccine against smallpox by:
A. Louis Pasteur
B. Edward Jenner
C. Robert Koch
D. Alexander Fleming
**Correct Answer: B**

**46.** The DNA of *Bacillus thuringiensis* (Bt) contains a cry gene which codes for a protein that is toxic to certain insects. This protein:
A. Is toxic to the bacterium itself
B. Is activated in the acidic gut of the insect
C. Binds to the epithelial cells of the midgut and creates pores, causing swelling and lysis
D. Acts as a repellent for the insect
**Correct Answer: C**

**47.** The primary sludge in a sewage treatment plant is the:
A. Supernatant from the primary settling tank
B. Solids that settle down in the primary settling tank
C. Activated sludge from the aeration tank
D. Effluent after biological treatment
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** The gas mixture produced in an anaerobic sludge digester, known as biogas, is predominantly:
A. Methane, Hydrogen sulphide, and CO₂
B. Methane, Oxygen, and CO₂
C. Butane, Hydrogen, and N₂
D. Methane and Butane
**Correct Answer: A**

**49.** The effectiveness of traditional knowledge in medicine and agriculture can be seen in products like curd, idli, and dosa, which are all produced by:
A. Fermentation by microbes
B. Genetic engineering
C. The use of chemical preservatives
D. Dehydration
**Correct Answer: A**

**50.** A major limitation of using only chemical pesticides for pest control is that they:
A. Are harmful to non-target organisms
B. Can pollute the environment (soil, water)
C. Can lead to the evolution of resistant pests
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

***

&& Biotechnology – Principles and Processes

#### Easy

**1.** Biotechnology primarily deals with the use of live organisms or their products for:
A. Industrial processes to produce products useful to humans
B. The study of the environment
C. The classification of organisms
D. The study of animal behaviour
**Correct Answer: A**

**2.** The two core techniques that enabled the birth of modern biotechnology are genetic engineering and:
A. Fermentation
B. Aseptic techniques (maintenance of sterile conditions)
C. Pasteurization
D. Hybridization
**Correct Answer: B**

**3.** The enzymes that cut DNA at specific sites are called:
A. DNA ligases
B. DNA polymerases
C. Restriction enzymes
D. Helicases
**Correct Answer: C**

**4.** The technology of making multiple identical copies of a specific segment of DNA is called:
A. DNA sequencing
B. DNA fingerprinting
C. Gene cloning
D. Gene therapy
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** A small, circular, double-stranded DNA molecule that is distinct from a cell's chromosomal DNA and is used as a vector in genetic engineering is a:
A. Chromosome
B. Plasmid
C. Ribosome
D. Lysosome
**Correct Answer: B**

**6.** The polymerase chain reaction (PCR) is a technique used for the:
A. Amplification of DNA
B. Cutting of DNA
C. Separation of DNA fragments
D. Ligation of DNA fragments
**Correct Answer: A**

**7.** A foreign piece of DNA inserted into a host organism is called:
A. Recombinant DNA
B. Native DNA
C. Vector DNA
D. Genomic DNA
**Correct Answer: A**

**8.** The enzyme that joins two DNA fragments together by forming phosphodiester bonds is:
A. Restriction endonuclease
B. DNA polymerase
C. DNA ligase
D. Exonuclease
**Correct Answer: C**

**9.** The specific sequence of bases recognized by a restriction enzyme is called its:
A. Origin of replication
B. Recognition site
C. Selectable marker
D. Cloning site
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** Agarose gel electrophoresis is a technique used to:
A. Amplify DNA
B. Separate DNA fragments according to their size
C. Cut DNA
D. Join DNA fragments
**Correct Answer: B**

**11.** In gel electrophoresis, DNA molecules move towards the positive electrode (anode) because they are:
A. Positively charged
B. Negatively charged
C. Neutral
D. Large in size
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** A 'bioreactor' is a vessel used for:
A. Growing microorganisms or cells on a large scale
B. Separating DNA fragments
C. Sterilizing instruments
D. Storing chemicals
**Correct Answer: A**

**13.** The process of making a host cell competent to take up foreign DNA can be achieved by treating it with:
A. A specific concentration of a divalent cation, such as calcium
B. Heat shock
C. Ice
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**14.** A 'selectable marker' in a cloning vector is a gene that helps in:
A. Identifying and eliminating non-transformants
B. Increasing the efficiency of transformation
C. Making the DNA replicate faster
D. Cutting the DNA
**Correct Answer: A**

**15.** The first recombinant DNA was constructed by Stanley Cohen and Herbert Boyer in the year:
A. 1953
B. 1972
C. 1983
D. 1990
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The enzyme Taq polymerase, used in PCR, is isolated from a bacterium that is:
A. Psychrophilic (cold-loving)
B. Mesophilic (medium temperature-loving)
C. Thermophilic (heat-loving)
D. Halophilic (salt-loving)
**Correct Answer: C**

**17.** The term 'molecular scissors' refers to:
A. DNA ligase
B. DNA polymerase
C. Restriction enzymes
D. Helicase
**Correct Answer: C**

**18.** The process of separating and purifying the desired product after the biosynthetic stage in a bioreactor is called:
A. Upstream processing
B. Downstream processing
C. Fermentation
D. Bioprocessing
**Correct Answer: B**

**19.** A 'vector' in genetic engineering is a DNA molecule used as a vehicle to:
A. Carry foreign genetic material into another cell
B. Cut the host cell's DNA
C. Provide energy for replication
D. Synthesize proteins
**Correct Answer: A**

**20.** The sequence that is responsible for controlling the copy number of the linked DNA in a plasmid is the:
A. Selectable marker
B. Cloning site
C. Origin of replication (ori)
D. Vector promoter
**Correct Answer: C**

---

#### Medium

**21.** Restriction enzymes that produce 'sticky ends' cut the two strands of the DNA double helix:
A. At the exact same position, creating blunt ends
B. At different positions, creating overhanging stretches
C. In a random fashion
D. Only at the ends of the DNA molecule
**Correct Answer: B**

**22.** The three main steps of a single cycle of PCR, in the correct order, are:
A. Annealing, Extension, Denaturation
B. Denaturation, Annealing, Extension
C. Extension, Denaturation, Annealing
D. Denaturation, Extension, Annealing
**Correct Answer: B**

**23.** In the pBR322 plasmid, the genes for resistance to the antibiotics ampicillin (ampᴿ) and tetracycline (tetᴿ) act as:
A. Origins of replication
B. Cloning sites
C. Selectable markers
D. Promoters
**Correct Answer: C**

**24.** The process of insertional inactivation is used to:
A. Screen for transformants from non-transformants
B. Screen for recombinants from non-recombinants
C. Increase the efficiency of ligation
D. Amplify the gene of interest
**Correct Answer: B**

**25.** Ethidium bromide is a stain used in gel electrophoresis to visualize DNA. It fluoresces bright orange when exposed to:
A. Infrared light
B. Visible light
C. UV light
D. X-rays
**Correct Answer: C**

**26.** The process of forcing DNA into host cells by bombarding them with high-velocity micro-particles of gold or tungsten coated with DNA is called:
A. Electroporation
B. Micro-injection
C. Biolistics (gene gun)
D. Transformation
**Correct Answer: C**

**27.** A palindromic sequence in DNA is a sequence of base pairs that reads:
A. The same on the two strands when the orientation of reading is kept the same
B. The same forwards and backwards on a single strand
C. As a series of repeating units
D. Differently on both strands
**Correct Answer: A**

**28.** The enzyme that synthesizes a short RNA primer, which is necessary for DNA polymerase to start replication, is called:
A. Helicase
B. Ligase
C. Primase
D. Topoisomerase
**Correct Answer: C**

**29.** The separation of DNA fragments from the agarose gel and their transfer to a synthetic membrane like nitrocellulose is known as:
A. Northern blotting
B. Western blotting
C. Southern blotting
D. Gel extraction
**Correct Answer: C**

**30.** To isolate DNA from a bacterial cell, the cell wall must be digested with the enzyme:
A. Cellulase
B. Chitinase
C. Lysozyme
D. Protease
**Correct Answer: C**

**31.** The recognition site for the restriction enzyme EcoRI is:
A. 5' - AAGCTT - 3'
B. 5' - GGATCC - 3'
C. 5' - GAATTC - 3'
D. 5' - GTCGAC - 3'
**Correct Answer: C**

**32.** In a PCR reaction, the two primers are designed to be complementary to the:
A. 5' ends of the same strand of the target DNA
B. 3' ends of the two separate strands of the target DNA
C. The middle region of the target DNA
D. The entire length of the target DNA
**Correct Answer: B**

**33.** Agrobacterium tumefaciens, a pathogen of several dicot plants, is able to deliver a piece of DNA known as 'T-DNA' to transform normal plant cells into a tumor. This T-DNA is located in the:
A. Main bacterial chromosome
B. Ti plasmid
C. Ri plasmid
D. Bacteriophage
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** A stirred-tank bioreactor is advantageous over a shake flask because it:
A. Provides better aeration and mixing
B. Allows for sampling of the culture periodically
C. Has a control system for temperature and pH
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**35.** The 'elution' step in the process of gel electrophoresis refers to:
A. Staining the gel with ethidium bromide
B. Running the DNA fragments through the gel
C. Cutting out the DNA bands from the gel and extracting the DNA
D. Loading the DNA into the wells
**Correct Answer: C**

**36.** To isolate DNA from a plant cell, which has a cell wall made of cellulose, the enzyme used is:
A. Lysozyme
B. Chitinase
C. Cellulase
D. Protease
**Correct Answer: C**

**37.** In recombinant DNA technology, the term 'vector' refers to:
A. The enzyme that cuts DNA
B. The host cell that takes up the recombinant DNA
C. The DNA segment to be cloned
D. A plasmid or virus used to transfer DNA into a living cell
**Correct Answer: D**

**38.** If a foreign gene is ligated at the BamHI site in the pBR322 plasmid, the recombinant plasmid will:
A. Lose tetracycline resistance
B. Lose ampicillin resistance
C. Lose both tetracycline and ampicillin resistance
D. Retain both resistances
**Correct Answer: A**

**39.** The first restriction endonuclease to be isolated was:
A. EcoRI
B. BamHI
C. Hind II
D. Taq I
**Correct Answer: C**

**40.** A disarmed pathogen is one which:
A. Is dead and can no longer infect
B. Has lost its virulence but can still be used as a vector
C. Is resistant to all antibiotics
D. Has been modified to cause a more severe disease
**Correct Answer: B**

---

#### Hard

**41.** The blue-white screening method for selecting recombinants is based on the principle of:
A. Antibiotic resistance
B. Insertional inactivation of a gene coding for an enzyme (e.g., β-galactosidase)
C. The presence of an origin of replication
D. The size of the plasmid
**Correct Answer: B**

**42.** A probe is a single-stranded DNA or RNA molecule tagged with a radioactive molecule that is used to:
A. Cut DNA at a specific site
B. Detect the presence of a complementary DNA sequence by hybridization
C. Amplify a DNA sequence
D. Ligate two DNA fragments
**Correct Answer: B**

**43.** If a recombinant DNA is inserted within the coding sequence of the enzyme β-galactosidase, the bacterial colonies will not produce any colour in the presence of a chromogenic substrate. These colonies are:
A. Non-recombinants
B. Recombinants
C. Non-transformants
D. Ampicillin-resistant
**Correct Answer: B**

**44.** Which of the following is not a feature of a good cloning vector?
A. Presence of an origin of replication
B. Presence of multiple recognition sites for a single restriction enzyme
C. Presence of selectable markers
D. Easy to isolate and purify
**Correct Answer: B**

**45.** In the process of PCR, if we start with one molecule of double-stranded DNA, the number of DNA molecules obtained after 30 cycles will be approximately:
A. 2 × 30
B. 30²
C. 2³⁰
D. 2⁹⁰⁰
**Correct Answer: C**

**46.** The reason for using a thermostable DNA polymerase like Taq polymerase in PCR is that:
A. It is much cheaper than other polymerases
B. It can withstand the high temperature required for the denaturation of double-stranded DNA
C. It has a higher fidelity (fewer errors)
D. It does not require a primer
**Correct Answer: B**

**47.** The expression of a foreign gene in a host cell can be optimized by using a:
A. Vector with a strong promoter
B. Host cell that grows rapidly
C. Continuous culture system in a bioreactor
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**48.** A 'gene library' is a collection of:
A. All the genes of a single organism stored in a vector
B. All the proteins produced by an organism
C. All the different types of vectors available for cloning
D. All the restriction enzymes isolated
**Correct Answer: A**

**49.** To make a bacterial cell competent to take up a hydrophilic DNA molecule like a plasmid, it is treated with a specific concentration of a divalent cation like Ca²⁺. This is thought to:
A. Increase the efficiency of the DNA ligase enzyme
B. Increase the permeability of the bacterial cell wall by creating transient pores
C. Make the DNA molecule more hydrophobic
D. Activate the origin of replication
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** A sparged stirred-tank bioreactor is different from a simple stirred-tank bioreactor because it has a system for:
A. Agitation
B. pH control
C. Bubbling sterile air through the culture medium
D. Temperature control
**Correct Answer: C**

***

&& Biotechnology and its Applications

#### Easy

**1.** Bt cotton is a transgenic plant that is resistant to:
A. Fungal diseases
B. Bacterial blight
C. Insect pests like bollworms
D. Weeds
**Correct Answer: C**

**2.** The 'Bt' in Bt cotton stands for the bacterium:
A. *Bacillus thuringiensis*
B. *Bacillus thermophilus*
C. *Bifidobacterium*
D. *Agrobacterium tumefaciens*
**Correct Answer: A**

**3.** Genetically engineered insulin, used for treating diabetes, is called:
A. Pro-insulin
B. Humulin
C. Glucagon
D. Somatostatin
**Correct Answer: B**

**4. The technique of RNA interference (RNAi) is used to:**
A. Amplify a gene
B. Cut DNA
C. Silence a specific mRNA, preventing protein synthesis
D. Insert a gene into a host
**Correct Answer: C**

**5.** A transgenic organism is one that:
A. Has foreign DNA incorporated into its genome
B. Has been produced by sexual reproduction
C. Is a hybrid of two different species
D. Is resistant to all diseases
**Correct Answer: A**

**6.** Gene therapy is a technique used to:
A. Diagnose genetic diseases
B. Correct a defective gene
C. Produce transgenic animals
D. Amplify DNA
**Correct Answer: B**

**7.** The first clinical gene therapy was given in 1990 to a 4-year-old girl for the deficiency of the enzyme:
A. Phenylalanine hydroxylase
B. Adenosine deaminase (ADA)
C. Tyrosinase
D. Hexosaminidase A
**Correct Answer: B**

**8.** The diagnostic technique that is based on the principle of antigen-antibody interaction is:
A. PCR (Polymerase Chain Reaction)
B. ELISA (Enzyme-Linked Immunosorbent Assay)
C. Gel electrophoresis
D. DNA fingerprinting
**Correct Answer: B**

**9.** The cry gene, which produces the Bt toxin, is isolated from:
A. A fungus
B. A bacterium
C. A virus
D. A plant
**Correct Answer: B**

**10.** 'Golden rice' is a transgenic crop that is enriched with:
A. Vitamin A
B. Vitamin C
C. Vitamin D
D. Iron
**Correct Answer: A**

**11.** Animals that have had their DNA manipulated to possess and express a foreign gene are known as:
A. Hybrid animals
B. Transgenic animals
C. Cloned animals
D. Somatic hybrids
**Correct Answer: B**

**12.** The use of bio-resources by multinational companies and other organisations without proper authorisation from the countries and people concerned is termed:
A. Biotechnology
B. Biopiracy
C. Bioethics
D. Bioremediation
**Correct Answer: B**

**13.** The Indian Parliament recently cleared the 'second amendment' of the Indian Patents Bill, that takes issues like patent terms and emergency provisions into consideration. This is related to:
A. Biopiracy
B. Bioethics
C. Bioremediation
D. Genetic engineering
**Correct Answer: A**

**14.** The main objective of producing pest-resistant GM crops is to:
A. Reduce the reliance on chemical pesticides
B. Increase the yield of the crop
C. Improve the nutritional value of the crop
D. Make the crop look better
**Correct Answer: A**

**15.** The Bt toxin exists as an inactive protoxin in the bacterium. It is converted into its active form in the:
A. Acidic pH of the insect's foregut
B. Alkaline pH of the insect's midgut
C. Neutral pH of the insect's hindgut
D. Saliva of the insect
**Correct Answer: B**

**16.** The transgenic model of mice is commonly used for:
A. Vaccine safety testing
B. Chemical safety testing
C. Studying diseases like cancer and cystic fibrosis
D. All of the above
**Correct Answer: D**

**17.** The technique used to detect HIV infection at a very early stage, when the virus concentration is very low, is:
A. ELISA
B. Urine analysis
C. PCR
D. Widal test
**Correct Answer: C**

**18.** The organization in India that is responsible for making decisions regarding the validity of GM research and the safety of introducing GM-organisms for public services is:
A. ICMR (Indian Council of Medical Research)
B. CSIR (Council of Scientific and Industrial Research)
C. GEAC (Genetic Engineering Approval Committee)
D. ICAR (Indian Council of Agricultural Research)
**Correct Answer: C**

**19.** The production of human insulin in *E. coli* was made possible by the American company:
A. Monsanto
B. Genentech
C. Eli Lilly
D. Pfizer
**Correct Answer: C**

**20.** 'Flavr Savr' is a transgenic variety of tomato that has an increased:
A. Size
B. Colour
C. Nutritional value
D. Shelf life
**Correct Answer: D**

---

#### Medium

**21.** The two polypeptide chains of mature human insulin are linked together by:
A. Hydrogen bonds
B. Peptide bonds
C. Phosphodiester bonds
D. Disulphide bridges
**Correct Answer: D**

**22.** In the process of RNA interference (RNAi), the silencing of a specific mRNA is mediated by:
A. Single-stranded DNA
B. Double-stranded RNA
C. Single-stranded RNA
D. Double-stranded DNA
**Correct Answer: B**

**23.** The Bt toxin protein binds to the surface of the midgut epithelial cells of the insect, creating pores that cause:
A. Cell swelling and lysis
B. Inhibition of protein synthesis
C. Inactivation of enzymes
D. Blockage of the gut
**Correct Answer: A**

**24.** The first transgenic cow, 'Rosie', produced human protein-enriched milk. This milk contained the human:
A. Alpha-lactalbumin
B. Casein
C. Insulin
D. Hemoglobin
**Correct Answer: A**

**25.** Gene therapy for Adenosine Deaminase (ADA) deficiency involves introducing a functional ADA gene into the patient's:
A. Red blood cells
B. Platelets
C. Lymphocytes
D. Neurons
**Correct Answer: C**

**26.** The nematode that infects the roots of tobacco plants and causes a great reduction in yield, which can be prevented by RNAi, is:
A. *Ascaris lumbricoides*
B. *Wuchereria bancrofti*
C. *Meloidogyne incognita*
D. *Ancylostoma duodenale*
**Correct Answer: C**

**27.** The main challenge in the production of human insulin using *E. coli* was:
A. The difficulty in growing *E. coli*
B. The bacterial cells could not produce the A and B chains
C. Getting the insulin assembled into a mature form (removing the C-peptide)
D. The insulin produced was toxic to humans
**Correct Answer: C**

**28.** The use of PCR in molecular diagnosis allows for the early detection of diseases because it can:
A. Detect the presence of antibodies
B. Amplify very low amounts of pathogen DNA or RNA
C. Visualize the pathogen directly
D. Measure the body's immune response
**Correct Answer: B**

**29.** The transgenic animal models are useful for studying the role of genes in the development of diseases. This is done by:
A. Introducing genes that make the animal susceptible to the disease
B. Inactivating specific genes
C. Studying the effect of new drugs
D. Both A and B
**Correct Answer: D**

**30.** Bioethics is a field of study that deals with the:
A. Ethical issues that may arise from advances in biology and medicine
B. Financial aspects of biotechnology
C. Legal framework for patents
D. Environmental impact of GM organisms
**Correct Answer: A**

**31.** The CryIAc and CryIIAb genes are effective in controlling:
A. Corn borer
B. Cotton bollworms
C. Nematodes
D. Fungi
**Correct Answer: B**

**32.** A probe, used in molecular diagnosis, is a:
A. Single-stranded DNA or RNA tagged with a radioactive molecule
B. Double-stranded DNA
C. Protein that binds to a specific antigen
D. A vector used for cloning
**Correct Answer: A**

**33.** The main reason for making crops pest-resistant using biotechnology is to reduce post-harvest losses and:
A. Increase the usage of pesticides
B. Decrease the reliance on agro-chemicals
C. Make the crops more expensive
D. Improve the taste of the crops
**Correct Answer: B**

**34.** Before the production of genetically engineered insulin, the insulin used for treating diabetic patients was extracted from:
A. Humans
B. Monkeys
C. Cattle and pigs
D. Bacteria
**Correct Answer: C**

**35.** Gene therapy for ADA deficiency is not a permanent cure if the functional gene is introduced into:
A. Early embryonic cells
B. Bone marrow cells
C. Lymphocytes
D. Stem cells
**Correct Answer: C**

**36.** The CryIAb gene is used to protect which crop from the corn borer?
A. Cotton
B. Rice
C. Corn (Maize)
D. Tobacco
**Correct Answer: C**

**37.** The human insulin produced by recombinant DNA technology consists of:
A. A, B, and C polypeptide chains
B. Only the A and B polypeptide chains
C. Only the C polypeptide chain
D. A and C chains
**Correct Answer: B**

**38.** The source of the complementary RNA for the RNAi process could be from an infection by:
A. Viruses having an RNA genome
B. Transposons (mobile genetic elements)
C. Both A and B
D. Bacteria
**Correct Answer: C**

**39.** An example of a biopiracy case related to an Indian crop is the patenting of:
A. Bt Cotton
B. Golden Rice
C. Basmati Rice
D. Flavr Savr Tomato
**Correct Answer: C**

**40.** A transgenic food crop which may help in solving the problem of night blindness in developing countries is:
A. Bt Soyabean
B. Golden Rice
C. Bt Corn
D. Flavr Savr tomatoes
**Correct Answer: B**

#### Hard

**41.** The correct steps for producing human insulin in *E. coli* are:
(i) Prepare two DNA sequences corresponding to A and B chains
(ii) Introduce them into plasmids of *E. coli*
(iii) Extract the chains and combine them by creating disulfide bonds
(iv) Culture the *E. coli* to produce the chains
A. (i) → (ii) → (iv) → (iii)
B. (ii) → (i) → (iv) → (iii)
C. (i) → (iv) → (ii) → (iii)
D. (iv) → (iii) → (i) → (ii)
**Correct Answer: A**

**42.** In the RNA interference process, the silencing of a specific mRNA is achieved by the action of an enzyme complex called:
A. DNA polymerase
B. RNA polymerase
C. RISC (RNA-induced silencing complex)
D. Reverse transcriptase
**Correct Answer: C**

**43.** The Bt toxin protein does not kill the *Bacillus* bacterium itself because:
A. The bacterium is immune to the toxin
B. The toxin is in an inactive protoxin form
C. The bacterium's gut is acidic
D. The bacterium does not have the specific receptors for the toxin
**Correct Answer: B**

**44.** Which of the following is a limitation of gene therapy as a permanent cure?
A. It is a very expensive procedure.
B. The functional gene must be introduced into cells that are immortal and can divide.
C. It can only be used for a limited number of diseases.
D. It has a low success rate.
**Correct Answer: B**

**45.** The production of a transgenic animal like 'Tracy' the sheep was aimed at producing a human protein, alpha-1-antitrypsin, which is used to treat:
A. Emphysema
B. Cystic fibrosis
C. Phenylketonuria (PKU)
D. Cancer
**Correct Answer: A**

**46.** The 'sticky ends' on the DNA fragments produced by restriction enzymes are useful in genetic engineering because they:
A. Allow the DNA fragments to be separated by size
B. Prevent the DNA from being degraded by nucleases
C. Form hydrogen bonds with their complementary sticky ends, facilitating the action of DNA ligase
D. Make the DNA visible under UV light
**Correct Answer: C**

**47.** The reason that the pro-insulin produced by the human body needs to be processed is that:
A. It is too large to be functional
B. The C-peptide needs to be removed for the A and B chains to become active
C. It is toxic in its initial form
D. It needs to be activated by an enzyme in the blood
**Correct Answer: B**

**48.** A major ethical concern regarding the use of transgenic animals is:
A. The animals are too expensive to produce
B. The unpredictability of their effect on the ecosystem if they escape
C. The suffering of the animals during the procedures
D. Both B and C
**Correct Answer: D**

**49.** A molecular probe is used in the process of hybridization to detect a specific gene. The principle behind this is the:
A. Double helical structure of DNA
B. Complementary base pairing property of nucleic acids
C. Semi-conservative mode of replication
D. Universality of the genetic code
**Correct Answer: B**

**50.** The Indian government has set up organizations like GEAC to monitor GM research and regulate the introduction of GM organisms. This falls under the domain of:
A. Biopiracy
B. Bioethics
C. Bioremediation
D. Biopatenting
**Correct Answer: B**
